3. End-To-End Simulation Testing & QA Verification Suite
To prepare the structural engine for live deployment, this testing matrix defines the absolute parameters required for continuous integration (CI/CD) automated testing blocks.
3.1 Unit Test Case 01: Combat Core Math Verification
Objective: Validate deterministic hit and damage calculations against target armor thresholds.
Input State: Attacker Accuracy = 100 | Defender Dodge = 100 | Attacker Base Damage = 50 | Attacker Crit Chance = 0.00% | Defender Armor = 15.
Expected Test Outcome: Hit Determination rolls exactly 1.00 (100% Hit Chance). Crit Modifier evaluates as 1.0x. Raw Damage computes as 50. Net Damage computes as exactly 35. Defender HP reductions must register as precisely 35 units per hit frame.
3.2 Unit Test Case 02: Auto-Eat Sliding Scale Trigger Validation
Objective: Verify that health recovery code loops fire properly without dropping frames or allowing character death state transitions.
Input State: Player Max HP = 1,000 | Player Current HP = 300 | UI Configuration Slider Value = 35% | Inventory Contents = 5x Seared Minnow (Restores 40 HP each).
Calculation Trigger Check: 300 \le \left( \frac{35}{100} \times 1,000 \right) \rightarrow 300 \le 350 \quad (\text{Evaluates as TRUE})
Expected Test Outcome: Engine processes immediate automated consumption of 1x Seared Minnow. Inventory stack count decrements smoothly from 5 to 4. Player Current HP increments immediately to 340. System verifies execution before processing the next incoming enemy attack frame payload.
3.3 Unit Test Case 03: Offline Processing Validation Verification
Objective: Ensure offline resource extraction logic properly handles time degradation curves and tool durability boundaries.
Input State: Disconnect Duration = 20 Hours (72,000 Seconds) | Tool Status = Copper Pickaxe with exactly 150 Durability points | Active Worker = Baseline Human | Gathering Node = Region 01 Copper Ore (10-second base extraction time, Base Node Wear = 1 point, Tool Resilience = 0).
Effective Action Time (T_{\text{eff}}) Derivation: T_{\text{eff}} = (8\text{ hours} \times 1.0) + (8\text{ hours} \times 0.5) + (4\text{ hours} \times 0.25) = 8 + 4 + 1 = 13\text{ hours } (46,800\text{ seconds})
Action Capacity Allocation Check: \text{Max Theoretical Actions} = \frac{46,800\text{ seconds}}{10\text{ seconds/action}} = 4,680\text{ Actions}
Durability Limit Check: Tool breaks completely after exactly 150 Actions, because 150 Actions multiplied by 1 point of wear drops durability to zero.
Expected Test Outcome: The offline simulation engine cuts off resource rewards tracking at exactly 150 successful actions. The sync manifest awards the shared village inventory exactly 150 Copper Ore units and rewards the character skills database table with the corresponding level XP block. The remaining 12.58 hours of effective time are discarded. The tool status row is flags as Broken.
3.4 Unit Test Case 04: Breeding Inheritance Validator
Objective: Guarantee genetic attribute modifier calculations strictly obey statistical boundaries and cap values.
Input State: Parent 1 Strength Growth Modifier = 1.40 | Parent 2 Strength Growth Modifier = 1.20 | Random Variance Seed forced to maximal limit (+0.02) | Mutation Roll forced to fail.
Computation Sequence: \text{Base Offspring Modifier} = \frac{1.40 + 1.20}{2} = 1.30 \text{Final Offspring Modifier} = 1.30 + 0.02 = 1.32
Expected Test Outcome: The newly instantiated child character row in the database displays a permanent Strength genetic growth modifier of exactly 1.32. Validation code checks that the value remains below the absolute inheritance cap of 2.00.

--- Dalsi(2).docx ---
MODULE 33: REMOTE CONFIGURATION DEPLOYMENT, LIVEOPS A/B TESTING & DYNAMIC PLAYER SEGMENTATION ENGINES
1. Remote Configuration Schema & Hot-Swapping Infrastructure
To tweak game balancing variables (such as drop rates, region event modifiers, or building cost scalars) without demanding client application updates from platform stores, the runtime environment references a server-authoritative Remote Configuration registry.
1.1 Remote Configuration Master JSON Specification
This data contract is hosted on global Content Delivery Networks (CDNs) as an immutable, version-controlled blob. The client fetches and parses this payload strictly at boot or during explicit zone transitions.
{  "remoteConfigMeta": {    "configVersionToken": "v2.14.9_build_20260701",    "minimumClientVersionAllowed": "1.4.0",    "pushedAtTimestamp": "2026-07-01T22:40:00Z"  },  "globalBalancingOverrides": {    "region_01_global_drop_modifier_scalar": 1.00,    "forge_base_gold_cost_multiplier_t7_to_t10": 1.25,    "breeding_mutation_probability_base_coefficient": 0.015  },  "activeLiveOpsEvents": [    {      "eventIdentifier": "event_midsummer_vila_2026",      "targetRegionIndex": 2,      "activationEpochSeconds": 1782943200,      "terminationEpochSeconds": 1783548000,      "localizedStringKeyReference": "ui_evt_title_midsummer"    }  ]}
1.2 Zero-Downtime Memory Injection Logic
When the API gateway detects a configuration update token change, it broadcasts an internal message through the Redis Pub/Sub framework. Stateless API compute pods intercept this signal and initiate an asynchronous background thread to overwrite memory registries without interrupting live WebSocket loops.
2. A/B Testing Traffic Splitting Engine
To test system changes safely, the platform splits user profiles into separate testing brackets using a deterministic hashing technique. This ensures users are assigned to consistent groups without requiring persistent assignments in the database.
2.1 MurmurHash3 Group Assignment Variant Formula
When an account logs into the server, its unique account_id string is combined with the explicit experiment_id token. The resulting string is run through a non-cryptographic MurmurHash3 algorithm to generate an unsigned 32-bit integer:
\text{Group Hash} = \text{MurmurHash3}(\text{account\_id} + \text{experiment\_id}) \text{Assignment Variant Index} = \text{Group Hash} \pmod{100}
Variant Allocation Branching Matrix:
Index Range 0 \le \text{Index} < 10: Assigned to Variant A (Experimental Rule Layer).
Index Range 10 \le \text{Index} < 20: Assigned to Variant B (Alternative System Settings Layer).
Index Range 20 \le \text{Index} < 100: Assigned to Control Group (Standard System Baseline).
This allocation strategy allows the game engine to execute real-time feature gating with an absolute evaluation cost of O(1) memory mapping cycles.
3. Real-Time Behavioral Player Segmentation
The analytics platform runs an automated, interval-based clustering worker that scans player behavior schemas. Accounts are categorized into targeted profile buckets, adjusting the available LiveOps offers and storefront layouts.
3.1 Structural System Segmentation Profiles
Segment Alpha - Hardcore Grinder: Accounts tracking greater than 18 active slot automation loop execution hours per rolling 24-hour window.
Segment Beta - Premium Whale: Accounts recording greater than $100.00 in direct fiat transactional store conversions within a 30-day tracking history.
Segment Gamma - High Churn Risk: Active profiles where the collective Auto-Eat food inventory balances have hit a zero state more than 5 times in the past 48 hours, stalling production metrics.
3.2 Relational Segment Assignment Database Map
CREATE TABLE account_behavioral_segments (    account_id UUID PRIMARY KEY,    active_segment_tags VARCHAR(32)[] NOT NULL, -- Array configuration mapping e.g. ['whale', 'hardcore']    last_computed_at TIMESTAMP WITH TIME ZONE DEFAULT NOW() NOT NULL);-- Indexing for quick segment queries by LiveOps storefront route managersCREATE INDEX idx_segment_tag_search ON account_behavioral_segments USING GIN (active_segment_tags);
3.3 Dynamic Storefront Routing Evaluation Routine
When a player loads the virtual store, the routing system queries the GIN index to check their behavioral category, fetching the corresponding customized item display array.
SELECT product_catalog_json FROM dynamic_storefront_manifestsWHERE target_segment_restriction_tags && (    SELECT active_segment_tags     FROM account_behavioral_segments     WHERE account_id = '9b1deb4d-3b7d-4bad-9bdd-2b0d7b3dcb6d')ORDER BY priority_weight_scalar DESC LIMIT 1;

--- Dalsi(20).docx ---
MODULE 09: UNITY SOFTWARE ARCHITECTURE, CLASS DESIGN & IMPLEMENTATION BLUEPRINTS
1. ScriptableObject Architecture & Data Templates
To decouple static configuration data from runtime dynamic state tracking, Folk-Idle utilizes a pure ScriptableObject-driven architecture in Unity. These files act as read-only data assets that populate runtime instances, preventing memory bloat and optimizing performance on mobile devices.
1.1 RaceConfigurationSO
Inherits from ScriptableObject. Defines the absolute baseline traits for a folklore lineage.
Data Fields:
raceType: Enum (Human, Vila, Fomóiri, Draugr, Kobold, Moosleute, Vodník)
baseStrGrowth: float (Base multiplier coefficient)
baseDexGrowth: float
baseIntGrowth: float
baseConGrowth: float
baseLckGrowth: float
passiveTraitID: string
passiveMultiplier: float
1.2 BaseItemSO
Inherits from ScriptableObject. Defines structural configuration parameters for game items before rarity or quality scaling transformations are computed.
Data Fields:
itemID: string (Unique internal key, e.g., iron_sword)
localizationKey: string (Points to local translation files)
primarySlot: Enum (Weapon, Shield, Helmet, Chest, Leggings, Boots, Ring, Amulet, Material, Consumable)
baseValueGold: int (Standard baseline merchant sell price)
flatAttackPower: int (Structural baseline applied to weapons)
flatDefenseRating: int (Structural baseline applied to armor pieces)
allowedAffixTags: List of strings (Restricts what secondary modifiers can roll on this specific base)
1.3 EnemyConfigurationSO
Inherits from ScriptableObject. Holds structural scaling offsets and bestiary assets for combat targets.
Data Fields:
enemyID: string
localizationNameKey: string
targetRegionID: int
baselineLevel: int
isRegionalBoss: bool
uniqueDropTableID: string
modelSprite: Sprite (Reference to 2D image asset asset)
2. Runtime Entity Model Class Layouts (Pure C# Plain Old CLR Objects)
These classes contain no MonoBehaviour overhead and do not exist within the Unity scene hierarchy. They manage pure state tracking and mathematical transformations, making them safe to serialize into JSON strings for database transport layers.
2.1 CharacterModel
Tracks the individual state parameters of an inhabitant of the village population.
Structural State Parameters:
characterID: System.Guid (Unique primary identifier)
characterName: string
currentRace: race_enum
generationIndex: int
currentAgeTier: age_enum
elapsedRealtimeSeconds: double (Accumulates time to compute aging threshold transitions)
currentLevel: int
currentExperience: int
primaryAttributes: Dictionary of string and int (Contains calculated values for strength, dexterity, intelligence, constitution, luck)
geneticGrowthModifiers: Dictionary of string and float (Contains the structural inheritance modifiers passed down from parents)
2.2 InventoryItemInstance
Tracks runtime modifications, rarity assignments, and unique properties for individualized equipment tracking rows.
Structural State Parameters:
instanceID: System.Guid (Unique primary row index)
staticDataReferenceID: string (Matches matching BaseItemSO data asset)
currentRarityTier: int (Calculated scalar value from 1 to 14)
isCurrentlyEquipped: bool
rolledAffixes: List of AffixDataPayload structures
2.3 AffixDataPayload
Structural State Parameters:
modifierTypeTag: string (e.g., crit_chance_percent, lifesteal_percent)
scalarValue: float (Calculated raw value contribution)
3. System Managers & Runtime State Controllers (MonoBehaviour Engines)
These components exist as persistent singleton controllers inside the primary Unity gameplay scene execution stack. They handle engine lifecycles, tick processing, and coordinate runtime class systems.
3.1 TimeTickSystemEngine
Acts as the global time-slice pulse generator for all active simulation slots.
Operational Mechanics:
Implements a persistent operational update loop checking against a fixed system tick baseline: Tick_Interval = 0.1 seconds.
Tracks internal tick counters for the three active worker slots independently.
Automatically updates the global village runtime state machine whenever a calculation threshold validates as complete.
3.2 CombatSimulationDirector
Manages the active execution flow of the simplified 2D combat loop defined in earlier modules.
Core Loop Lifecycle Tracking:
Method: ExecutePlayerTurnAttackSequence()
Calculates total player accuracy against target enemy dodge parameters to return hit evaluation tokens.
Applies random percentage evaluations to trigger critical hit damage multipliers.
Subtracts enemy armor metrics from total raw damage to establish the net health deduction pass.
Updates the active UI panel values asynchronously.
Method: ProcessDefensiveResolutionSequence()
Evaluates dodge, block strength, and structural armor checks for the player character model.
Deducts corresponding health parameters.
Instantly processes the auto-eat monitoring validation check before allowing the subsequent calculation cycle to initiate.
3.3 OfflineAFKCalculationProcessor
Processes delta time manifestations upon client network reconnection loops.
Processing Architecture:
Step 1: Queries server time API endpoints to lock down absolute temporal duration metrics: Total_Delta_Seconds = Server_Time_Current - Client_Time_At_Disconnect.
Step 2: Feeds Total_Delta_Seconds into the 4-tier efficiency degradation matrix to isolate the true effective action duration parameter (T_{eff}).
Step 3: Resolves gathering loops sequentially. If processing tool instances strike a durability rating of 0 during the batch evaluation cycle, the iteration index steps down instantly to preserve resource pools and lock inventory inputs.
Step 4: Dispatches a consolidated sync packet manifest update directly to the central PostgreSQL infrastructure layer.
4. Asynchronous Observer Pattern & Game Event Broker Architecture
To prevent structural tight-coupling between data state layers and visual presentation canvas objects, Folk-Idle implements a centralized, strongly typed Event Broker architecture.
4.1 GlobalGameEventBroker
A global static registry mapping structured structures to listener actions. This system completely replaces standard Unity update checks with notification parameters.
Structural Event Profile: CurrencyChangedEvent
Contained Payload: newGoldTotal (int), newDiamondTotal (int)
Trigger Scenario: Fired explicitly by inventory modules when items are sold or forge transactions validate as successful.
Receiving Systems: Header UI Display instantly updates text fields, demanding 0% validation checks on the main update frame.
Structural Event Profile: CharacterTaskStateSwappedEvent
Contained Payload: activeCharacterID (Guid), targetFsmState (Enum)
Trigger Scenario: Dispatched when a player reallocates a citizen from gathering nodes over to active combat maps.
Receiving Systems: Bottom Navigation Dock, Client-Side FSM Controller, and Node List render panels adjust layouts automatically.
Structural Event Profile: ToolDurabilityDepletedEvent
Contained Payload: affectedToolType (Enum), currentDurability (int)
Trigger Scenario: Triggered when tool integrity hits 0 during active loops.
Receiving Systems: Halts active extraction loops, pushes notification popups to the primary viewport layer, and toggles repair interaction targets.

--- Dalsi(21).docx ---
MODULE 08: MONETIZATION POLICY, ANTI-CHEAT FRAMEWORK & SERVER OPERATIONS
1. Monetization Architecture & Premium Currency Economy
The design philosophy prioritizes player retention and competitive balance. Monetization pathways focus strictly on time efficiency, Quality of Life (QoL) convenience, and aesthetic customization, completely bypassing direct pay-to-win vertical power increases. The premium currency, Diamonds, is obtainable via hard in-game milestones (Bestiary completion, Regional Boss achievements) or through direct microtransactions.
1.1 Premium Convenience Services & Pricing Matrices
Timeline Expansion Pass (Premium Timeline Shift)
Baseline Function: Adjusts the standard offline time degradation curve to support players with long real-world absence windows.
Free Timeline Thresholds: 0 to 8 hours at 100% efficiency | 8 to 16 hours at 50% efficiency | 16 to 24 hours at 25% efficiency | 24+ hours at 0% efficiency.
Premium Timeline Thresholds (Purchased for $5.00 flat or 500 Diamonds): 0 to 12 hours at 100% efficiency | 12 to 24 hours at 50% efficiency | 24 to 36 hours at 25% efficiency | 36+ hours at 0% efficiency.
Armory Equipment Loadout Presets
Baseline Function: Allows instant mechanical swapping of full gear sets across active character slots.
Scaling Cost: First 2 preset pages are free. Additional preset unlocks cost 100 Diamonds per page, up to a maximum of 5 pages.
Shared Storage Vault Expansion
Baseline Function: Expands virtual inventory slots beyond the standard village building upgrades.
Cost Multiplier: Each additional 50 infinite stack material slots cost: \text{Diamond Cost}(S) = \lfloor 50 \times 1.5^{(S - 1)} \rfloor Where S represents the current storage purchase iteration index.
Cosmetic Customization and Visual Assets
Asset Types: Custom character portraits for folklore lineages, localized visual themes for the village hub layout, and exclusive particle trails for combat action tickers. These additions inject 0% stat modifications into the sub-stat calculation matrices.
2. Anti-Cheat Architecture & Memory Protection
Idle games are inherently vulnerable to local system clock modifications (Time-Travel exploits) and active runtime memory alteration (RAM freezing via external software packages). Folk-Idle counters these threat vectors via cryptographically signed state assertions.
2.1 The Chrono-Sync Validation Engine
The application relies on an authoritative server clock decoupled from the user's mobile device operating system time framework.
Heartbeat Telemetry: The client application transmits a compressed state payload to the backend API at a baseline frequency of once every 60 seconds during online execution.
NTP Verification: Every payload contains the client’s internal mono-tonic time counter matched against the Network Time Protocol (NTP) server truth timestamp.
Violation Threshold: If the delta between the client-reported execution timeline and the server's tracking timeline exceeds a hard tolerance metric of \pm 5\text{ seconds}, a Time-Synchronization Exception is triggered.
Exception Outcome: The server instantly pauses execution counters, drops the active data manifest frame, forces a client-side interface lock, and overrides local system registers with the server database truth parameters.
2.2 Server-Authoritative Randomness & Generation
To prevent localized memory injections from creating fabricated items or inflated currency values within the shared village inventory:
Deterministic Seed Management: Random rolls for Forge success rates, affix generations, item drops, and breeding mutations are calculated entirely server-side.
Tokenized Loot Distribution: When an enemy is killed or an ore node is depleted, the client transmits an intent packet. The server handles the drop chance calculation, generates a secure UUID for the item row, saves it to the items database table, and returns a signed confirmation token to the client to update the local visual display stack. The client possesses 0% authority to instantiate items locally.
3. High-Concurrency Server Infrastructure & Database Optimization
With up to 50 individual character profiles running continuous background state matrices per active account, database read/write routines must be aggressively optimized to maintain server throughput during large-scale leaderboard cron cycles or world boss events.
3.1 Asynchronous Transaction Batching
To eliminate database locking bottlenecks, run-time character actions do not invoke immediate, isolated SQL operations.
The Memory Write-Buffer: Active progress indicators, currency gains, and skill experience allocations are held in a high-speed Redis cache block layer instance.
Flush Cycles: The contents of the Redis transient layer are flattened into a single transactional SQL update statement and pushed to the core PostgreSQL storage framework every 5 minutes, or immediately upon explicit manual triggers (such as when a player forces a manual logout, enters a breeding grounds execution, or confirms an item upgrade at the Great Forge).
3.2 Relational Document Hybrid Design
As defined in the core relational schema database blueprints, complex variable data payloads like character primary stats, inherited genetic growth modifiers, and item affix groupings are intentionally housed within JSONB column payloads instead of expansive multi-row join tables.
Performance Benefit: This hybrid structural setup allows the database to retrieve a character's complete profile configuration along with its gear stat data packages via a single, execution-efficient query block, minimizing indexing overhead and cutting operational server costs during rapid calculations.

--- Dalsi(22).docx ---
MODULE 07: UI/UX INTERFACE ARCHITECTURE, STATE MACHINES & DATA FLOW
1. Global UI Canvas Architecture & Layout Panels
The interface layout is strictly menu-driven and data-heavy, optimizing screen space for rapid cross-referencing of stats, inventory volumes, and character tasks. The viewport is divided into three persistent operational zones.
1.1 Header Panel (Global Status Bar)
Resource Trackers: Real-time display of shared Village Gold and Premium Diamonds.
Population Counter: Active view of current population scaling (e.g., "24 / 50 Citizens").
Global Progress Metric: Total account level score sum with a link triggering the Leaderboard sub-overlay.
1.2 Persistent Bottom Navigation Dock
A static 5-button dock allowing instant switching of the Main Content View across primary operational loops:
Button 1: Characters Tab (Management of all 50 slots, allocation, gear swapping, and breeding grounds).
Button 2: Combat Tab (Zone selection, bestiary tracking, and active combat execution view).
Button 3: Gathering Tab (Resource node selection and node assignment interfaces).
Button 4: Crafting Tab (Production lines for Smithing, Cooking, and Alchemy).
Button 5: Village Tab (Housing infrastructure upgrades and specialized building development).
1.3 Main Content View
Dynamic viewport rendering specific layout templates based on the navigation state or chosen character context.
2. Character Combat View & Auto-Eat Interface Blueprint
The combat view is highly streamlined to prioritize data clarity over graphical rendering. It handles active simulation output display and structural parameter configuration.
2.1 Visual Layer Layout
Center Viewport: Static 2D graphical portrait representation of the active enemy target.
Enemy Name Tag: Text field indicating Name and calculated baseline Level (e.g., "Forest Troll [Lv.10]").
Health Bar Array: Stacked horizontal bars showing exact value representations.
Player HP Bar: Current_HP / Max_HP text overlay.
Enemy HP Bar: Current_HP / Max_HP text overlay.
Action Ticker Panel: Scrolling text readout logging chronological tick outcomes (e.g., "Draugr inflicts 42 Melee Damage. Troll armor blocks 12. Troll loses 30 HP.").
2.2 Interactive Components
Stats Inspection Overlay Button: Located directly beneath the enemy portrait. Pressing opens a non-blocking modal view displaying all derived sub-stats of the enemy (Armor, Attack Speed, Dodge, Accuracy, Crit Chance).
The Auto-Eat Configuration Slider: A persistent interactive UI slider mapped from 0% to 100%.
Functionality: The player drags the indicator node to define the exact percentage baseline trigger for food consumption.
Implementation Layer: Changes to the slider scale write directly to the local memory cache and update the database row tracking that active slot profile configuration upon state finalization.
Food Stock Tracker: Small indicator adjacent to the slider displaying the item icon and inventory stack count of the current highest-healing food item designated for emergency consumption.
3. Client-Side Finite State Machine (FSM)
Each character allocation slot runs an independent state controller machine on the client app execution thread. This isolates task execution data structures and prevents asynchronous rendering blockages.
3.1 Structural State System Definitions
State 1: Idle
Conditions: Character is sitting in the village pool unassigned.
UI Execution: Displays "Unassigned" status tag with an active button pointing to task selection menus.
State 2: Combat_Active
Conditions: Triggered when character is assigned to an unlocked regional node.
UI Execution: Renders the combat progress loop, triggers hit/damage calculations at intervals determined by Attack Speed, and updates health values.
State 3: Gathering_Active
Conditions: Character assigned to an extraction node (Mining, Woodcutting, Fishing, Herbalism).
UI Execution: Displays a cyclic looping filling progress bar matching the computed completion speed calculation. Drops combat layout panels completely.
State 4: Crafting_Active
Conditions: Character assigned to a production queue inside a village building terminal.
UI Execution: Renders item creation queues, displays consumption lists, and increments production counters upon countdown expiration.
3.2 Non-Blocking State Transitions
When a user reassigns Character A from Mining to Combat, the client fires a structural payload update to the backend database server while shifting the local FSM container index. This recalculates the layout render hierarchy seamlessly without demanding a full application scene reload, preserving device battery and processing efficiency.
4. Local Simulation View vs. Server Truth Validation
To maintain zero gameplay lag on mobile processing units over unstable mobile network environments, the game executes an asynchronous validation loop split between client-side simulation graphics and server-validated data structures.
4.1 Client Optimistic Update Flow
Execution: When performing active loops online (such as watching a progress bar fill or an enemy health bar deplete), the local client calculates and displays state mutations instantly using matching mathematical structures.
UI Responsiveness: Health bars move smoothly, numbers text boxes increment locally, and item rewards appear in the visual UI layout array without forcing a synchronous await return lock from the cloud database server.
4.2 Server Integrity Verification Loop
Synchronization Heartbeat: Every 60 seconds during active online play, or explicitly when a user triggers a state transition (e.g., stopping a task, swapping a weapon, opening a box), the client transmits a lightweight state delta manifest block containing local timestamps and accumulated actions to the server API endpoint.
Conflict Resolution Logic: The server backend computes the identical timeframe using the secure server-side clock truth parameters.
If Client Data matches Server Computation (within an engineering network jitter variance margin of +/- 2%): The database transaction writes safely, validating the progress.
If Client Data mismatches Server Computation (exceeding variance bounds, indicating local memory tampering or execution acceleration hacks): The server rejects the batch manifest payload, forces a silent hard rollback state modification on the client memory registers, and syncs the local UI state back to match the database truth row precisely.

--- Dalsi(23).docx ---
MODULE 06: MULTIPLAYER SYSTEMS, GUILD ARCHITECTURE & LEADERBOARD LOGISTICS
1. Global Leaderboard Framework
To foster competition while accommodating the time-independent nature of idle progression, the game utilizes a decentralized, asynchronously updated leaderboard network. The backend calculates rankings via batched cron jobs every 5 minutes to minimize direct database stress.
1.1 Leaderboard Classifications
Total Account Mastery Ladder: Ranks players by the absolute sum of all levels across all living characters currently residing in their village pool.
Skill-Specific Masteries: Separate tracking ladders for individual professions (e.g., individual top-ranked Mining, Fishing, or Alchemy level accounts). Tied character levels break ties based on accumulated raw experience points.
Time-Attack Boss Rush: Records the absolute lowest Time to Kill (TTK) achieved against specific Regional Bosses (Level 10, 20, 30, etc.). Calculations are verified server-side using the combat loop equations from Module 01 to eliminate local client speed hacking.
Interval Ladders (Weekly/Monthly): Tracks net experience points or gold accumulated strictly within a designated calendar window. This permits newer accounts to compete against end-game players on a short-term velocity metric.
1.2 Weekly Reset Mechanics
Interval ladders execute an automated hard reset every Monday at 00:00 UTC. Top-ranking players are automatically rewarded with specialized cosmetic titles, profile emblems, and a static payout of Diamonds based on bracket percentiles (Top 1%, Top 5%, Top 10%).
2. Guild Systems & Collective Progression
Guilds act as macro-economic groups that incentivize active players to organize shared logistics. Guild creation requires a Level 30 Account Milestone and a flat expenditure of 100,000 Gold. Joining a guild is unrestricted but bound by a 24-hour cooldown penalty upon voluntary exit or eviction before another guild can be joined.
2.1 Guild Experience Point (GXP) Generation
Guilds level up up to a maximum threshold of Level 50. Guild XP is aggregated from the passive actions of all members.
Every 1,000 Combat or Professional XP earned by an individual member's active character automatically generates 1 flat Guild XP point.
Offline AFK calculation yields translate to GXP at the exact same ratio upon client reconnection, processing the efficiency degradation curves dynamically.
2.2 Guild Hall Perks & Global Buffs
The Guild Master can allocate collective Guild Gold (donated freely by members) to upgrade persistent corporate structures within the Guild Hall interface. These upgrades yield flat stat adjustments applied globally to every character owned by every guild member.
Treasury Expansion: Each tier increases the maximum deposit limit of the shared Guild Bank by 5,000,000 Gold.
Strategic Armory: Grants a global flat bonus to Physical Armor. Stat scales as: +5 flat Armor per upgrade level. Maximum level 10.
Administrative Registry: Increases the total member capacity cap of the guild. Baseline is 10 members. Each upgrade level adds +2 member slots, up to a maximum of 30 members at Level 10.
Collective Resource Monoliths:
Miner's Monolith: Grants +1% flat Mining Yield per level.
Sylvan Monolith: Grants +1% flat Woodcutting Speed per level.
Sailor's Monolith: Grants +1% flat Fishing Catch Rate per level.
3. Cooperative PvE: Guild Bosses & World Events
Cooperative encounters feature entities with massive structural health pools designed to absorb damage over multi-day calculation periods.
3.1 Guild Raid Boss Mechanics
Every week, the Guild Master can summon one specific Folklore Raid Boss (e.g., The Midnight Leshy, The Chained Fafnir) using collective Guild Raid Tokens obtained through the completion of Daily Guild Quests.
Raid Loop Duration: Once summoned, the boss remains active for exactly 72 hours or until its health pool reaches zero.
Asynchronous Contribution: Members do not fight simultaneously. A member allocates one of their active combat characters to execute a 15-minute mock simulation. The total damage dealt during this simulated instance is permanently subtracted from the global boss health registry on the server database. Each member can execute 3 simulation battles per raid cycle.
3.2 Dynamic Contribution Reward Allocation Formula
To prevent high-level accounts from completely monopolizing loot tables, rewards are calculated utilizing a proportional tier bracket linked directly to the member's individual damage contribution relative to the total health pool of the boss.
Let Player_Damage be the total damage inflicted by a single player across all 3 attempts. Let Boss_Max_HP be the absolute maximum health pool of the summoned Raid Boss. Contribution_Percentage = (Player_Damage / Boss_Max_HP) * 100
Tier S Reward Bracket (Contribution >= 10%): 100% chance for 3x Random Epic Upgrade Materials, 50 Diamonds, and a guaranteed Tier 7 (Legendary) baseline equipment drop.
Tier A Reward Bracket (5% <= Contribution < 10%): 100% chance for 2x Random Epic Upgrade Materials, 25 Diamonds, and a guaranteed Tier 6 (Epic) equipment drop.
Tier B Reward Bracket (1% <= Contribution < 5%): 100% chance for 1x Random Rare Upgrade Material, 10 Diamonds, and a guaranteed Tier 4 (Rare) equipment drop.
Tier C Reward Bracket (Contribution < 1%): Flat compensation payout of 5,000 Gold and 2 Diamonds.
3.3 Server-Wide World Boss Events
World Bosses are server-driven infrastructure events triggered automatically on the 1st and 15th day of every calendar month. All accounts on the server contribute damage asynchronously over a continuous 24-hour window. Upon defeat, all contributing accounts receive a distribution of Diamonds and high-tier materials scaled linearly to their placement on the World Event Contribution Leaderboard.
4. Asynchronous Guild Wars (Clash of Realms)
Guild Wars operate as zero-sum, non-realtime competitive cycles running over a fixed 5-day duration (Monday 12:00 UTC to Friday 12:00 UTC).
4.1 Automated Matchmaking Algorithm
The backend pairing system matches two guilds containing equivalent total active player counts and matching Guild Tier brackets (+/- 2 Guild Levels) to prevent unfair structural bottlenecks.
4.2 War Point (WP) Aggregation Systems
Guilds compete not through direct physical PVP combat, but through execution velocity across three designated operational battlefronts. Whichever guild accumulates the highest cumulative War Points at the expiration of the timer window wins the war.
Front 1: The Combat Vanguard
Execution Rule: Members earn 10 War Points for every standard monster cleared within their active regional farming zones, and 500 War Points for every successful regional boss kill executed during the war week.
Front 2: The Production Logistics
Execution Rule: Every item crafted via Smithing, Cooking, or Alchemy that scales above Tier 5 (Epic rarity) contributes War Points equivalent to: WP = 50 * Item_Rarity_Tier.
Front 3: The Gathering Supply Chain
Execution Rule: Every 1,000 units of raw materials (Ores, Timber, Herbs, Fish) deposited into the special Guild War Supply Vault generates 100 War Points. Items deposited here are permanently consumed by the war engine and cannot be withdrawn.
4.3 Victory & Defeat Payouts
Winning Guild: Receives a flat +20% Guild XP bonus multiplier for the subsequent 48 hours, a massive deposit of Gold directly into the Guild Bank, and 5x War Chests distributed to all participating members containing random high-tier Forge materials.
Losing Guild: Receives a minor consolidation payout of Guild Gold and 1x War Chest per participating member.
5. Economic Guardrails & Safe Trading Infrastructure
To preserve the progression longevity of the itemization database and completely block real-money trading (RMT) vectors or bot multi-accounting exploits, open player-to-player direct trading is strictly prohibited. Economic interaction is mediated exclusively by a highly controlled Guild Trade Depot.
5.1 The Guild Trade Depot Limitations
Asset Restrictions: Only unrefined raw gathering materials (Ores, Raw Wood, Uncooked Fish, Herbs) and generic crafting bases can be transferred. Equipped gear, items with unique random affixes, items processed via the Forge above Tier 3, and premium currencies (Diamonds) are completely untradeable.
Peer-to-Peer Gifting Lockout: Items cannot be gifted for free. All exchanges must occur via a direct item-for-gold barter system managed by the server engine.
5.2 Algorithmic Price Floor & Price Ceiling Corridors
The server enforces strict valuation margins on all trade operations. Players cannot set custom prices outside of a calculated dynamic economic corridor linked directly to the item's baseline itemization parameters.
Let Base_Value be the static vendor sell price of a raw resource unit. Price_Floor = Base_Value * 0.80 Price_Ceiling = Base_Value * 3.00
Example: If an Iron Ore item has a hard-coded system vendor value of 10 Gold:
The absolute lowest price a player can list it for in the depot is 8 Gold.
The absolute highest price a player can list it for in the depot is 30 Gold.
Any listing request submitted via the client API that violates these bounds returns a standard server error validation code, entirely eliminating external wealth transfer exploits and maintaining the mathematical balance of the game economy.

MODULE 05: VILLAGE MANAGEMENT, HOUSING INFRASTRUCTURE & SPECIALIZED BUILDINGS
1. The Village Core & Population Pool Economy
The village functions as the primary operational hub, regulatory anchor, and deployment baseline for the player's workforce. While a maximum of 3 active characters can be assigned to explicit run-time tasks, the remaining population resides within the passive Village Pool.
1.1 Population Pool Regulations
Absolute Capacity Cap: The village pool cannot exceed a maximum capacity of 50 total characters across all age tiers.
Eviction Mechanic: Players can permanently evict a character from the village via the town registry UI to free up a population slot for preferred genetic lineages or newly discovered folklore races. Evicted characters are permanently deleted from the database schema, and all unequipped items return to the shared armory.
Global Level Benchmark: The collective level sum of all living village residents determines the player's total account progression score for global leaderboard positioning.
2. Housing Infrastructure & Expansion Rules
To expand the population capacity from the initial baseline of 10 slots up to the absolute maximum threshold of 50 slots, players must construct and continuously upgrade residential housing structures using refined materials generated from Woodcutting and Smithing.
2.1 Residential Building Profiles
Common Cottages
Baseline Purpose: Unlocks primary population capacity increments.
Structural Slots Provided: Each constructed Cottage adds +2 total population slots to the village cap.
Maximum Build Count: 10 units maximum.
The Village Inn
Baseline Purpose: Unlocks temporary lodging structures and increases child-to-adult progression speed.
Structural Slots Provided: Adds +5 total population slots.
Unique Passive: Reduces the real-world duration required for characters to mature from the Child tier to the Adult tier by 20% (reducing the timeline from 14 real days down to 11.2 real days).
Maximum Build Count: 1 unit maximum.
Noble Manors
Baseline Purpose: Late-game high-density housing extensions.
Structural Slots Provided: Each Manor adds +5 total population slots.
Pre-requisite: Requires a Level 5 Town Hall structure.
Maximum Build Count: 5 units maximum.
3. Specialized Functional Buildings
Specialized buildings provide localized operational centers for the advanced gameplay systems defined across earlier architectural modules, including breeding mechanics, equipment composition, and mentorship networks.
3.1 The Breeding Grounds
Architectural System Alignment: Houses the genetic combination framework detailed in Module 02.
Baseline Functionality: Enables two adult characters of matching races at or above Level 50 to interface and generate offspring.
Tier Upgrades:
Level 1: 1 Active breeding slot pair. Baseline 48-hour cooldown tracking.
Level 2: Reduces parental breeding cooldown parameters by 25% (lowering the countdown timer to 36 hours).
Level 3: Unlocks a second concurrent breeding slot pair, allowing two separate lineages to breed simultaneously.
3.2 The Great Forge & Armory
Architectural System Alignment: Interfaces directly with the 14-tier item itemization database and premium affix reroll mechanics outlined in Modules 01 and 03.
Baseline Functionality: Acts as the physical terminal for item fusion. 3 identical rarity items are compressed here alongside Gold costs to create a higher rarity tier item.
Tier Upgrades & System Gatekeeping:
Level 1 Forge: Restricts maximum item fusion outputs to Tier 4 (Rare).
Level 2 Forge: Restricts maximum item fusion outputs to Tier 6 (Epic).
Level 3 Forge: Restricts maximum item fusion outputs to Tier 8 (Mythic).
Level 4 Forge: Restricts maximum item fusion outputs to Tier 11 (Divine).
Level 5 Forge: Removes all gatekeeping parameters, enabling full synthesis up to Tier 14 (Transcendent).
3.3 The Mentorship Academy
Architectural System Alignment: Validates and processes the passive utilities of the "Old" character age bracket detailed in Module 02.
Baseline Functionality: Provides physical assignment slots where Senior and Old characters can be stationed alongside Children or low-level Adults.
Mentorship Execution Loop: Stationary old mentors consume no food, generate no resource outputs, and cannot engage in combat. For every Old character assigned to the Academy benches, all characters assigned to active gathering, crafting, or combat professions across the entire game receive a flat, stacking +5% experience point (XP) acquisition modifier. Maximum simultaneous mentors allowed in the Academy slots is limited to 5.
4. Building Construction Cost Equations
Constructing or upgrading any architectural asset in the village boundary demands an escalating expenditure of Gold, Refined Timber (Woodcutting/Processing), and Metal Bars (Smithing). Costs follow a steep geometric scaling progression curve linked directly to the target building level (B_{\text{Level}}).
4.1 Global Infrastructure Cost Formula
\text{Gold Cost}(B_{\text{Level}}) = \lfloor \text{Base Gold} \times 2.15^{(B_{\text{Level}} - 1)} \rfloor \text{Timber Cost}(B_{\text{Level}}) = \lfloor \text{Base Wood} \times 1.85^{(B_{\text{Level}} - 1)} \rfloor \text{Metal Bar Cost}(B_{\text{Level}}) = \lfloor \text{Base Bars} \times 1.65^{(B_{\text{Level}} - 1)} \rfloor
4.2 Structural Cost Coefficients Table
Common Cottages (Base Values)
Base Gold: 500
Base Wood: 50 Oak Timber
Base Bars: 10 Copper Bars
The Village Inn (Base Values)
Base Gold: 5,000
Base Wood: 250 Pine Timber
Base Bars: 75 Iron Bars
The Great Forge & Armory (Base Values)
Base Gold: 10,000
Base Wood: 150 Beech Timber
Base Bars: 100 Tin Bars
The Mentorship Academy (Base Values)
Base Gold: 12,500
Base Wood: 400 Birch Timber
Base Bars: 80 Silver Bars

MODULE 04: PROFESSIONAL SKILLS, CRAFTING CHAINS & RESOURCE LOGISTICS
1. Gathering Skill Mechanics & Resource Node Distribution
Gathering skills operate on periodic loop timers. When a character is assigned to a node, a progress bar fills based on the node's base difficulty and the character's skill level. Upon completion, resources are injected into the shared village inventory, tool durability drops, and skill experience points (XP) are rewarded.
1.1 Professional Skill Experience Curve
The experience required to advance any Gathering or Crafting skill from Professional Level L to Level L+1 utilizes a flatter geometric growth pattern than combat to encourage broad management.
XP_Skill(L) = floor(50 * 1.12^(L-1) + 80 * (L-1))
Level 1 to 2: 50 XP
Level 10 to 11: 875 XP
Level 50 to 51: 17,982 XP
Level 100 to 101: 4,218,950 XP
1.2 Resource Node Regional Matrix
Each of the 10 core folklore regions houses one specific tier of node for all four gathering professions. Higher tier nodes require minimum skill levels to interact.
Region 01 (Level 1 Minimum): Copper Ore | Beech Trees | Pond Minnow | Field Marigold
Region 02 (Level 10 Minimum): Tin Ore | Oak Trees | River Trout | Bog Nightshade
Region 03 (Level 20 Minimum): Iron Ore | Willow Trees | Mud Carp | Cave Moss
Region 04 (Level 30 Minimum): Coal Node | Pine Trees | Chasm Pike | Mountain Ginger
Region 05 (Level 40 Minimum): Silver Ore | Birch Trees | Steppe Salmon | Wild Ginseng
Region 06 (Level 50 Minimum): Gold Ore | Maple Trees | Coastline Cod | Salt Lotus
Region 07 (Level 60 Minimum): Mithril Ore | Yew Trees | Deep Mire Eel | Screaming Mandrake
Region 08 (Level 70 Minimum): Adamantite Ore | Elder Trees | Canyon Catfish | Jagged Bloodgrass
Region 09 (Level 80 Minimum): Obsidian Ore | Ancient Wood | Fjord Shark | Frost Moonflower
Region 10 (Level 90 Minimum): Celestial Ore | Yggdrasil Burl | Astral Whale | Golden Ambrosia
2. Tool Durability & Depletion Rules
Gathering operations require a profession-specific tool equipped in the shared Village Toolset (Pickaxe, Axe, Harpoon, Sickle). Tools do not occupy character equipment slots; they are drawn globally by active workers.
2.1 Durability Consumption Formula
Every successful gathering action reduces the current durability of the active tool.
\text{Durability Loss} = \max\left(1, \text{Base Node Wear} \times (1 + \text{Race Penalty}\%) - \text{Tool Resilience}\right)
Base Node Wear scales linearly by node tier (Tier 1 = 1 point, Tier 10 = 10 points).
Moosleute characters suffer the +25% Tool Durability Degradation penalty here, multiplying Base Node Wear by 1.25 before resilience mitigation.
2.2 Tool Broken State & AFK Truncation
When a tool's durability hits 0, it enters a Broken state.
Online Play: The gathering action immediately halts, and a UI alert prompts tool repair using Gold.
Offline AFK Play: The offline calculation engine simulates actions chronologically. If tool durability hits 0 before the elapsed offline time (T_{\text{eff}}) finishes, the resource generation loop for that character cuts off instantly at that simulated timestamp.
3. Crafting Progression & Processing Chains
Crafting professions utilize raw gathered items to produce refined materials, progression gear, auto-eat food, and temporary combat buff potions.
3.1 Smithing (Refining & Equipment Forging)
Smithing processes raw ores into metallic bars, which are then used to manufacture physical base armor items and weapons for the core combat slots.
Smelting Loop: 3x Raw Ore + 1x Coal = 1x Metal Bar. (Kobold passive grants a 10% chance to duplicate the resulting bar).
Forging Weapons: Requires 8x Metal Bars of Tier X to create a Tier X Base Weapon (Melee, Range, or Blunt structural archetype).
Forging Armor Set Pieces:
Helmet: 5x Metal Bars
Chestplate: 10x Metal Bars
Leggings: 8x Metal Bars
Boots: 4x Metal Bars
Shield: 6x Metal Bars
3.2 Cooking (Sustain & Auto-Eat Economy)
Cooking processes raw fish combined with secondary ingredients to create food items. Food is the absolute primary source of Health Regeneration (HP_{\text{Regen}}) within the combat simulation loop.
Tier 1 Recipe - Seared Minnow: 1x Pond Minnow + 1x Field Marigold = 1x Seared Minnow. Consuming restores 40 HP instantly when triggered by the slider check.
Tier 5 Recipe - Steppe Salmon Platter: 1x Steppe Salmon + 2x Wild Ginseng = 1x Salmon Platter. Restores 650 HP instantly.
Tier 10 Recipe - Ambrosial Whale Roast: 1x Astral Whale + 5x Golden Ambrosia = 1x Cosmic Roast. Restores 8,500 HP instantly.
Excellent Quality Crafting: Vodník characters possess a 15% chance to trigger an Excellent Cook event, multiplying the final HP restoration value of the created food item by a permanent 1.50x factor.
3.3 Alchemy (Buff Potions & Utility Elixirs)
Alchemy combines harvested herbs with liquid vials to produce consumable potions. Characters can have exactly one offensive and one defensive potion active simultaneously.
Combat Damage Potion: Requires 3x Herb Tier X + 1x Liquid Base. Increases corresponding type damage (Melee, Ranged, Magic) by 15% for a continuous duration of 30 minutes.
Regeneration Potion: Requires 2x Herb Tier X + 2x Cave Moss. Boosts baseline out-of-combat and in-combat flat health regeneration by 25 points per second for 30 minutes.
Luck Elixir: Requires 5x Field Marigold + 1x Mountain Ginger. Increases Loot Rarity Modifier (Loot Luck) by 10% for 15 minutes.
Moosleute Synergy: Potions brewed by a Moosleute character receive a 10% increase to stat potency (e.g., a Damage Potion provides +16.5% damage instead of +15%).
4. Shared Village Storage & Logistics
To optimize database transaction calls and facilitate multi-character task tracking, inventory management is simplified into an asynchronous, non-blocking village registry system.
4.1 Global Inventory Rules
Shared Pool: All characters draw inputs directly from the same global array. There are no individual character bags.
Item Stack Caps: Raw materials, refined bars, cooked food, and crafted potions stack infinitely within a single database entry slot.
Equipment Allocation Logic: Unequipped weapons and armor pieces occupy distinct singular rows within the items table due to their individualized affix data payloads.
4.2 Inventory Cap & AFK Storage Protection
Kobold characters carry a structural penalty where non-ore and non-bar drops occupy double space metrics. The inventory tracking engine calculates space via virtual slots.
\text{Virtual Slot Weight} = \sum \text{Standard Items} + \sum \left(\text{Non-Ore Items Extracted By Kobolds} \times 2\right)
If Virtual Slot Weight strikes the absolute Village Storage Cap during an offline cycle, all further gathering or monster drop additions drop to 0% efficiency, discarding subsequent items while preserving Gold and XP accumulations.

MODULE 32: IN-APP PURCHASES (IAP), RECEIPT VALIDATION ENGINES & ANTI-FRAUD PAYMENT PIPELINES
1. Server-Authoritative Store Receipt Validation Workflow
To eliminate local client-side premium currency fabrication injections (such as patching local purchase success boolean values), Folk-Idle utilizes an absolute server-to-server (S2S) trusted receipt validation loop. The client application acts strictly as a proxy to pass platform transaction tokens.
1.1 Multi-Platform Verification Network Pipeline
When a user initiates an In-App Purchase for a Diamond package via the Apple App Store or Google Play Store, the transaction process is routed through authoritative server gates.
+------------------+         +--------------------+         +-----------------------+|  Client Device   | ------> | Stateless API Node | ------> | Platform Store API    || (Obtains Token)  |         | (Sends Auth Req)   |         | (Apple/Google Verify) |+------------------+         +--------------------+         +-----------------------+         ^                            |                             |         |                            v                             v         |                    [Atomic DB Upsert] <------- [Cryptographic Success]         +--------------------------- |
The client device communicates with the native App Store API, completing the payment processing gate and receiving an encrypted base64 receipt token.
The client transmits the raw token along with the targeted product_id to the secure server route /api/v1/billing/verify-receipt.
The API node forwards the payload to the respective verification endpoint (Google OAuth API or Apple App Store Server API) using trusted backend credentials.
If the platform store answers with a cryptographic confirmation code, the server proceeds to mint the premium assets inside the database.
2. Idempotent Transaction Processing Schema
To prevent network-timeout echo errors from executing duplicate asset distribution loops (double-minting premium diamonds when a user taps a purchase button during cellular connection drops), the database enforces strict transaction idempotency keys.
2.1 Authorized Purchase Ledger Schema
The server maps platform-issued transaction identification IDs into a primary unique filtering index.
CREATE TABLE primary_purchase_ledger (    purchase_id BIGSERIAL PRIMARY KEY,    account_id UUID NOT NULL,    platform_transaction_id VARCHAR(128) NOT NULL UNIQUE, -- Enforces absolute idempotency    product_identifier VARCHAR(64) NOT NULL,    fiat_cost_cents INT NOT NULL,    fiat_currency_code CHAR(3) NOT NULL,    processed_at TIMESTAMP WITH TIME ZONE DEFAULT NOW() NOT NULL);CREATE INDEX idx_purchase_account_mapping ON primary_purchase_ledger (account_id);
2.2 Server-Side Verification Query Routine
Before modifying user balance parameters, the transaction script verifies the incoming payload signature properties against the unique hardware index.
BEGIN;-- Insert transaction signature tracking properties; fails instantly if identical platform token existsINSERT INTO primary_purchase_ledger (account_id, platform_transaction_id, product_identifier, fiat_cost_cents, fiat_currency_code)VALUES ('9b1deb4d-3b7d-4bad-9bdd-2b0d7b3dcb6d', 'GPA.3312-4412-9901-12345', 'diamonds_pack_tier_3', 1999, 'USD');-- Upon successful unique constraint confirmation, execute secure premium currency injectionUPDATE account_security_registrySET current_premium_diamonds = current_premium_diamonds + 1200WHERE account_id = '9b1deb4d-3b7d-4bad-9bdd-2b0d7b3dcb6d';COMMIT;
3. Realtime Refund Realignment & Account Quarantine Vectors
When a user executes an external chargeback or receives a regulatory app marketplace refund request, Apple and Google emit an asynchronous Webhook alert JSON payload to the server-configured notification endpoints.
3.1 Webhook Payload Example: App Store Server Notification V2 (Refund Event)
{  "notificationType": "REFUND",  "notificationUUID": "f20b810d-c11a-422d-8f90-223344556677",  "version": "2.0",  "data": {    "bundleId": "com.folkidle.game",    "transactionId": "GPA.3312-4412-9901-12345",    "productId": "diamonds_pack_tier_3",    "revocationDate": 1782942000000  }}
3.2 Automated Resource Reclamation Tree
Upon capturing a valid REFUND notification string, the server fires a background script targeting the profile linked to the original transactionId.
Scenario A: Sufficient Balance: If the target account's current current_premium_diamonds ledger matches or exceeds the value of the refunded product, the server automatically subtracts the exact resource volume, logging an economic balance correction.
Scenario B: Negative Balance Mitigation: If the user has already spent the premium diamonds (rendering the balance parameter lower than the reclamation quota), the server immediately mutates the profile's access settings to Quarantine_Active. This isolates the account from global leaderboards and locks active character processing slots until the balance discrepancy is cleared.

MODULE 27: UNITY UI CANVAS OPTIMIZATIONS, BATCHED TEXT RENDERING & RUNTIME MEMORY ALLOCATION PROFILING
1. UI Canvas Isolation & Graphic Rebuild Mitigation Strategies
Because Folk-Idle is a menu-driven, data-dense interface, text values and metrics change multiple times per second across up to three concurrent slot operations. In Unity’s UI system (UGUI), updating a single UI element dirties its parent Canvas, forcing the engine to regenerate the entire graphic batch mesh on the CPU.
1.1 Multi-Canvas Hierarchical Isolation Architecture
To prevent a single text tick from recalculating the static parts of the viewport layout, the interface layer is split into distinct functional sub-canvases isolated by rendering update speeds.
Static Background Canvas: Houses historical background parchment graphics, board trims, and static button silhouettes. This canvas remains undirtied during core loops, incurring zero mesh rebuild costs.
Periodic Intermittent Canvas: Houses village population caps, building upgrade state markers, and skill tracking matrix windows. Rebuilds trigger exclusively upon explicit player selection mutations or build completion callbacks.
High-Frequency Simulation Canvas: Houses active character health tickers, damage number overlays, resource volume increments, and action completion bars. This canvas regenerates mesh arrays at a fixed 10 Hz simulation pulse frequency.
1.2 Layout Component Execution Locks
Standard automatic layout controllers (VerticalLayoutGroup, HorizontalLayoutGroup, ContentSizeFitter) execute expensive per-frame geometric calculations during canvas dirty events. Production menus completely avoid these components inside the High-Frequency Simulation Canvas. Position matrices for list elements are computed via direct anchor offset array scripts running inside pure O(1) coordinate translation loops.
2. Low-Allocation Object Pooling Framework for Dynamic UI Elements
Instantiating and destroying GameObject components for combat damage numbers, loot notifications, or action ticker logs triggers severe heap fragmentation and invokes Unity's garbage collector. The engine implements a generic, thread-safe object pooling architecture.
2.1 Non-Allocating UI Component Pooling Engine
public class UIComponentPool<T> where T : UnityEngine.Component{    private readonly T prefabReference;    private readonly UnityEngine.Transform activeStorageParent;    private readonly System.Collections.Generic.Queue<T> pooledInstancesPool;    private readonly System.Collections.Generic.List<T> activeInstancesTrack;    public UIComponentPool(T prefab, UnityEngine.Transform parent, int initialCapacity = 64)    {        this.prefabReference = prefab;        this.activeStorageParent = parent;        this.pooledInstancesPool = new System.Collections.Generic.Queue<T>(initialCapacity);        this.activeInstancesTrack = new System.Collections.Generic.List<T>(initialCapacity);        for (int i = 0; i < initialCapacity; i++)        {            T instance = UnityEngine.Object.Instantiate(this.prefabReference, this.activeStorageParent);            instance.gameObject.SetActive(false);            this.pooledInstancesPool.Enqueue(instance);        }    }    public T SpawnElement()    {        T element;        if (this.pooledInstancesPool.Count > 0)        {            element = this.pooledInstancesPool.Dequeue();        }        else        {            element = UnityEngine.Object.Instantiate(this.prefabReference, this.activeStorageParent);        }        element.gameObject.SetActive(true);        this.activeInstancesTrack.Add(element);        return element;    }    public void DespawnElement(T element)    {        element.gameObject.SetActive(false);        this.activeInstancesTrack.Remove(element);        this.pooledInstancesPool.Enqueue(element);    }}
3. Garbage Collection (GC) Minimization & Struct-Driven Allocation Controls
String concatenation in C# (such as characterName + " Level " + currentLevel) allocates short-lived char array objects on the managed heap. When updating dozens of labels at a 10 Hz frequency, heap allocation velocity triggers macro frame drops during garbage collections.
3.1 Heap Garbage Projection Formula
Without allocation-free optimization, cumulative garbage mass scales exponentially over time relative to execution parameters:
G_{\text{total}}(t) = t \times f \times \sum_{i=1}^{S} B_i
Where:
t represents elapsed runtime in seconds.
f represents the interface update frequency (10\text{ Hz}).
S represents the total count of active data labels rendering data updates simultaneously.
B_i represents the byte allocation mass generated by a singular string mutation event.
3.2 Integer-to-String Static Array Lookups
To bypass heap allocation during numeric metric tracking, values bound by hard-coded system parameters (such as character levels 1 to 100, item rarities 1 to 14, or damage increments up to 10,000) are drawn directly from pre-allocated string lookups generated during the application initialization routine.
public static class FastStringCache{    private static readonly string[] levelStringsArray;    static FastStringCache()    {        levelStringsArray = new string[101];        for (int i = 0; i <= 100; i++)        {            levelStringsArray[i] = i.ToString();        }    }    public static string GetLevelString(int level)    {        if (level >= 0 && level <= 100) return levelStringsArray[level];        return level.ToString();    }}
3.3 TextMeshPro In-Place Character Array Injection
For arbitrary value arrays (such as fluctuating Gold counts or Health parameters), updates utilize TextMeshPro’s non-allocating char buffer array interface methods (SetText), mutating existing char data matrices directly in memory without instantiating string wrappers.
4. Unity Profiler Performance Benchmarks & Memory Validation Parameters
To validate compliance with memory allocation restrictions before releasing client build patches to production app marketplaces, target builds run under strict runtime evaluation scripts.
4.1 Profiler Automated Assertion Suite
Managed Heap Allocations Target Bound: Must register exactly 0 bytes of heap memory allocations per active frame tick during standard automation, combat, or gathering tracking cycles.
UI Canvas Rebuild Frame Time Ceiling: Rebuild loops inside the High-Frequency Simulation Canvas must terminate within 1.2 milliseconds on standard low-end mobile target chipsets.
Garbage Collector Frequency Lockout: Garbage collections must never fire spontaneously more than once every 30 minutes during standard continuous background gameplay execution states.
4.2 Automated Optimization Verification Contract
{  "profileBenchmarkID": "PERF_UGUI_MATRIX_V1",  "testExecutionFrameCount": 18000,  "testTargetSimulationFrequency": "10Hz Ticks",  "trackedSystemMetrics": {    "maxAllowedCanvasRebuildsPerSec": 10,    "targetFrameTimeMilliseconds": 16.66,    "heapAllocationToleranceBytes": 0  },  "assertionValidations": [    "Assert.AreEqual(0, Profiler.GetMonoHeapBytesAllocatedPerFrame(), 'Managed heap allocation detected inside core simulation UI loop.')",    "Assert.IsTrue(Profiler.GetLastFrameTime() <= 16.66ms, 'Client frame latency drops below 60 frames per second standard execution floor.')"  ]}

MODULE 26: LEADERBOARD CRON MECHANICS, MATCHMAKING ENGINES & ASYNCHRONOUS GUILD WAR IMPLEMENTATIONS
1. Leaderboard Architecture & Ranking Aggregation Loops
To prevent performance degradation on primary PostgreSQL shards from continuous sorting queries, the global ladder framework utilizes high-speed memory structures inside the Redis caching tier.
1.1 Redis Sorted Sets (ZSET) Memory Topology
Player rankings across distinct categories—such as Combined Account Mastery, Gold Reserves, and individual skill categories—are managed inside isolated Redis Sorted Sets.
Data Structure Mechanics: Every active user profile forms an entry within the ZSET where the player's unique account_id string acts as the unique member key, and the numeric progression score is mapped as the sorting element value.
Algorithmic Complexity: Inserting updates via ZADD or fetching targeted placement slices via ZREVRANGE operates at an execution cost of O(\log N), decoupling query delays from total user count scaling.
1.2 Multi-Tiered Database Persistence Cycle
While Redis handles realtime ranking retrieval requests, state validation rules require sequential snapshots to populate long-term historical records.
                  +-----------------------------------+                  |  Realtime Player Progress Updates |                  +-----------------------------------+                                    |                            ZADD Memory Ticks                                    v                  +-----------------------------------+                  |        Redis ZSET Cache           |                  |     (Real-Time Leaderboard)       |                  +-----------------------------------+                                    |                         5-Minute Cron Extract                                    v                  +-----------------------------------+                  |      Stateless Worker Node        |                  +-----------------------------------+                                    |                         Bulk Uncommitted Upsert                                    v                  +-----------------------------------+                  |   PostgreSQL Secondary Replica    |                  |     (Immutable Historical Logs)   |                  +-----------------------------------+
The 5-Minute Replication Sweep: A stateless background worker task executes a cron cycle every 300 seconds. It reads top ranking slots from memory, formats the keys into flat tabular rows, and streams a bulk UPSERT command block directly into the read-only database storage tables.
Weekly Archival Purge: At exactly 00:00 UTC on Mondays, the cron engine exports final scoring vectors into compressed storage blocks to freeze weekly event brackets, clears the temporary competition ZSET layers, and initializes next-cycle metrics cleanly.
2. Asynchronous Guild War Matchmaking Engine
The Guild War platform runs on an asynchronous confrontation model. Guilds construct a defensive network of player profile snapshots that opponent factions evaluate and attack during active combat windows.
2.1 The Matchmaking Distance Calculation Matrix
The matching engine fires automatically every Sunday at 23:30 UTC. It maps active guild rows into localized pairing buckets by minimizing a multi-variable geometric distance function (D_{ij}):
D_{ij} = \sqrt{\alpha (R_i - R_j)^2 + \beta (M_i - M_j)^2}
Where:
R_i, R_j represent the current Matchmaking Ratings (MMR) of Guild i and Guild j.
M_i, M_j represent the counts of active combat-ready character profiles deployed within each guild's defense roster.
\alpha, \beta are system scaling coefficients calibrated to prioritize structural rating parity over roster size parity (\alpha = 1.0, \beta = 0.35).
2.2 Operational Matching Queue Steps
The engine scans the database registry, filtering out guilds that failed to register a valid defense array during the open roster window.
The remaining entities are sorted ascending by baseline MMR.
The engine iterates down the sequence, matching adjacent guilds if their calculated distance vector falls within tolerance parameters.
If an odd number of factions remains within a localized rating pool, the search window expands dynamically by 15% every 30 seconds until a valid opponent match is confirmed.
3. Battle Resolution Logic for Asynchronous Guild Raids
When a player launches an assault on an opponent's guild node, the interaction runs entirely on server-authoritative compute threads using snapshots of the defender's characters, ensuring zero client manipulation vectors.
3.1 Defensive Roster State Deserialization
Upon match validation, the server loads the target defender's snapshot manifest from the database JSONB payload. This includes exact attribute values, genetic growth configurations, active potion status tracking, and the current 5-piece armor set synergy variables.
3.2 Automated Combat Script Resolution Loop
// Pure server-authoritative combat resolution routine for asynchronous guild warspublic class GuildBattleEngine{    public BattleReport ResolveMatch(CharacterSnapshot attacker, CharacterSnapshot defender)    {        int turnLimit = 100;        int currentTurn = 1;                while (attacker.CurrentHP > 0 && defender.CurrentHP > 0 && currentTurn <= turnLimit)        {            // Execute Attacker Action Phase            ExecutePhaseStrike(attacker, defender);            if (defender.CurrentHP <= 0) break;                        // Execute Defender Automated Counter-Phase            ExecutePhaseStrike(defender, attacker);            if (attacker.CurrentHP <= 0) break;                        currentTurn++;        }                return CompilationFinalReport(attacker, defender, currentTurn);    }    private void ExecutePhaseStrike(CharacterSnapshot activeUnit, CharacterSnapshot targetUnit)    {        double hitProbability = (double)activeUnit.Accuracy / (activeUnit.Accuracy + targetUnit.Dodge);        double roll = System.Security.Cryptography.RandomNumberGenerator.GetDouble();                if (roll <= hitProbability)        {            int netDamage = Math.Max(1, activeUnit.RawMeleeDamage - targetUnit.FlatPhysicalArmor);            targetUnit.CurrentHP -= netDamage;        }    }}
3.3 Mitigation Rules for Asynchronous Balances
Because the defender cannot actively manage their inventory or manually deploy emergency consumables during an attack, defensive snapshots receive a flat, balancing health scaling scalar:
\text{HP}_{\text{Defender\_Snapshot}} = \text{Base\_Max\_HP} \times 1.25
This ensures defensive arrays present a viable progression challenge to active, item-swapping attackers.
4. Cross-Shard Micro-Service Topology for Global Tournaments
To unify players across distinct regional database shards during end-game inter-server events, the cluster switches from regional sharding models over to a unified gRPC event-mesh execution model.
4.1 gRPC Inter-Service Network Architecture
Regional shard nodes communicate with a centralized tournament master micro-service via HTTP/2 pipelines utilizing protocol buffer configurations (.proto).
syntax = "proto3";package folkidle.tournament.v1;message SyncMatchStateRequest {  string match_uuid = 1;  string attacker_account_id = 2;  int32 inflicted_damage_sum = 3;  bool is_final_blow = 4;}message SyncMatchStateResponse {  bool processing_status = 1;  int32 global_node_remaining_hp = 2;}service GlobalTournamentService {  rpc SyncMatchState(SyncMatchStateRequest) returns (SyncMatchStateResponse);}
4.2 Split Network Transaction Integrity
Atomic Validation Check: State updates targeting cross-shard matches use an isolation network fence model. When a regional server node initiates an updates request, the centralized master server acquires an in-memory execution lock on that specific target match index using a distributed lock instance (Redlock).
Conflict Resolution Handling: If two different regional cluster nodes transmit overlapping damage manifests matching the same target boss or guild profile simultaneously, the cluster evaluates the server-authoritative timestamps down to microsecond intervals. The trailing transaction payload is safely rejected, returning an out-of-sync notification token to the regional node to prompt an immediate visual redraw pass on the client interface.

MODULE 25: CLIENT-SERVER CRYPTOGRAPHIC SECURITY, NETWORK TELEMETRY MONITORING & THREAT VECTOR MITIGATION
1. End-to-End Cryptographic Packet Signing & Payload Encryption
To secure the stateless API architecture against Man-in-the-Middle (MitM) inspection, packet interception, and automated replay attacks, all client-server network interactions are bound by strict cryptographic contracts over TLS 1.3.
1.1 AES-256-GCM Payload Encapsulation
Volatile state modification payloads transmitted via HTTP POST or WebSockets (such as breeding confirmations, forge updates, or boss combat resolution manifests) undergo symmetric encryption using authenticated AES-256-GCM blocks.
Key Exchange Strategy: Symmetric session keys are derived during client authentication using an Elliptic Curve Diffie-Hellman (ECDH) ephemeral key exchange protocol.
Replay Attack Defenses: Every encrypted packet wraps a structural timestamp header and an auto-incrementing cryptographic nonce string generated server-side per active session. Packets containing nonces that mismatch or repeat within a rolling 24-hour verification window are dropped immediately.
1.2 HMAC-SHA256 Token Validation
Every API transaction appends an individual signature header (X-FolkIdle-Signature). The signature is computed locally by the client application using a Hashed Message Authentication Code (HMAC) tracking the raw payload body combined with a rolling secret key.
X-FolkIdle-Signature = HMAC-SHA256(Payload_Body + Session_Nonce, Rolling_Secret)
The ASP.NET Core server recalculates this signature before parsing the request JSON string. If the computed hash value fails to match the header value exactly, the network payload is dropped, terminating the client TCP connection socket instantly.
2. Anti-Tamper Memory Scrambling & Code Obfuscation in Unity
Idle games operating on mobile operating systems are prime targets for runtime memory freezing and alteration tools (e.g., Cheat Engine, GameGuardian). Folk-Idle mitigates this risk at the compilation and compilation layer.
2.1 IL2CPP Compilation and Metadata Stripping
The Unity client application completely avoids standard Mono script compilation configurations. Production builds enforce IL2CPP (Ahead-Of-Time) conversion pathways.
Assembly Obfuscation: The machine code output undergoes structural renaming loops via symbols strip utilities. Class definitions, variable keys, and method namespaces are transformed into randomized alphanumeric strings (e.g., CharacterModel.currentLevel transforms into a_x79b). This layout effectively prevents decompilers (such as ILSpy or Reflector) from mapping logical game loop structures.
2.2 Memory Pointer Scrambling via Value Shufflers
Critical numeric fields tracking game state parameters within memory registries (such as character health variables, gold balances, or premium diamond quantities) are never stored as naked primitive types (int, float). They utilize a generic struct template wrapper (AntiTamperVar<T>) that continuously obfuscates values in RAM.
// Architectural specification for memory pointer value scramblingpublic struct AntiTamperVar<T> where T : struct{    private T obfuscatedValue;    private int memoryXorKey;    public AntiTamperVar(T actualValue)    {        this.memoryXorKey = System.Security.Cryptography.RandomNumberGenerator.GetInt32(1, int.MaxValue);        this.obfuscatedValue = ApplyXorTransform(actualValue, this.memoryXorKey);    }    public T GetValue() => ApplyXorTransform(this.obfuscatedValue, this.memoryXorKey);}
The memoryXorKey shifts randomly on every read/write access tick, preventing external scanners from finding static memory value locations during runtime execution.
3. Network Telemetry & Behavioral Anomaly Detection Algorithms
Automated macro clickers and custom execution bot scripts can mimic player inputs to bypass traditional client-side anti-cheat protections. The backend monitors input pacing structures across all user interaction paths.
3.1 Input Cadence Variance Math
The server telemetry pipeline tracks the time intervals (\Delta t) between consecutive client interaction packets. Human inputs naturally exhibit erratic time deltas, whereas basic automation software displays strict, repetitive cadences.
An anomaly score (A_{\text{score}}) is calculated over a rolling window of K user-initiated state transitions:
A_{\text{score}} = \sum_{i=1}^{K} \frac{1}{\Delta t_i \cdot \sigma^2}
Where \Delta t_i is the time delta between consecutive events, and \sigma^2 is the rolling mathematical variance of the input cadence interval across the historical sampling window. If a user’s input stream approaches zero variance (\sigma^2 \to 0), the anomaly score climbs exponentially.
3.2 Automated Telemetry Profiling Constraints
Cadence Violations Threshold: Sustained input variance tracking below \sigma^2 = 0.002 over a sequence of 50 consecutive actions flags the account for automated input automation.
Concurrent Action Sieve: If the API gateway intercepts simultaneous transaction payloads originating from the same authenticated user token tracking different geographic IP domains, the secondary route is severed, triggering immediate account security lockdowns.
4. Automated Quarantine, Shadow Banning & Purge Pipelines
Accounts flagged by the fraud detection monitoring frameworks or the telemetry analysis engines do not receive immediate UI warning notifications. They are moved to a sandboxed routing layer.
4.1 The Account Quarantine State Flag
When an anomaly score breaches security tolerance parameters, an asynchronous background thread issues an immediate database state update mutating the target profile's access flag.
UPDATE account_security_registry SET routing_status_flag = 'Quarantine_Active', security_audit_score = security_audit_score + 10WHERE account_id = '9b1deb4d-3b7d-4bad-9bdd-2b0d7b3dcb6d';
4.2 Shadow Banning Infrastructure Restrictions
An account assigned to the Quarantine_Active flag is systematically isolated from the global game economy without changing local client UI functionality.
Leaderboard De-indexing: The account's level sums and time-attack boss scores are filtered out of all global and weekly leaderboard query returns. The client UI continues to display fabricated ladder placement indexes locally to prevent the user from realizing a restriction has been applied.
Guild Trade Depot Sequestration: Any listing items posted by a quarantined player are routed to an isolated marketplace block visible exclusively to other quarantined bot profiles, blocking item or gold transfers to legitimate player accounts.
Hard Lock Cascade Execution: If the internal account security audit score increases beyond a maximum tolerance threshold, the server cancels the session key, revokes the authentication token, pushes a network disconnection packet code to the client frame, and schedules the account data rows for a complete cascading database purge cycle.
