MODULE 23: DATABASE SCHEMA MODIFICATIONS, RELATIONAL INDEXING STRATEGY & MIGRATION PATHS
1. Relational Database Schema Mutations (PostgreSQL)
To implement the permanent tool architecture, discrete tool rows must be expunged from the transaction-heavy items table. Tool tracking is consolidated into the village_infrastructure configuration table as a fast array of primitive integer fields.
-- Step 1: Remove deprecated tool instance columns from the items tracking schemaALTER TABLE items DROP COLUMN IF EXISTS current_durability,DROP COLUMN IF EXISTS base_resilience;-- Step 2: Expand village_infrastructure schema to house permanent tracking statesALTER TABLE village_infrastructure ADD COLUMN mining_tool_tier INT DEFAULT 1 NOT NULL,ADD COLUMN woodcutting_tool_tier INT DEFAULT 1 NOT NULL,ADD COLUMN fishing_tool_tier INT DEFAULT 1 NOT NULL,ADD COLUMN herbalism_tool_tier INT DEFAULT 1 NOT NULL,ADD CONSTRAINT chk_mining_tier CHECK (mining_tool_tier BETWEEN 1 AND 10),ADD CONSTRAINT chk_woodcutting_tier CHECK (woodcutting_tool_tier BETWEEN 1 AND 10),ADD CONSTRAINT chk_fishing_tier CHECK (fishing_tool_tier BETWEEN 1 AND 10),ADD CONSTRAINT chk_herbalism_tier CHECK (herbalism_tool_tier BETWEEN 1 AND 10);
2. High-Speed Relational Indexing Strategy
Since tool checks are executed on every Redis-to-Postgres flush cycle and every character reallocation request, query execution paths must avoid full table scans.
2.1 Composite Index Optimization
A composite B-Tree index is deployed on the village_infrastructure table, tying the account_id foreign key directly to the tool tier components. This bounds lookups to an operational cost of O(\log N).
CREATE UNIQUE INDEX idx_village_tools_composite ON village_infrastructure (account_id, mining_tool_tier, woodcutting_tool_tier, fishing_tool_tier, herbalism_tool_tier);
2.2 Database Write-Buffer Locking Thresholds
During the 5-minute bulk synchronization cycle, the background processing engine queries tool parameters using a read-only snapshot transaction block. This prevents row-locking contention (uncommitted reads), allowing active characters to continue logging automated action ticks into the Redis cache layer without network lag bottlenecks.
3. Tool Upgrade API JSON Payloads & Contract Topologies
The client interaction loop bypasses inventory slot manipulations. Upgrading a tool requires a structured transactional payload targeting the specific profession index.
3.1 POST /api/v1/village/infrastructure/upgrade-tool
Payload Constraints: profession_id must map to valid system strings (mining, woodcutting, fishing, herbalism).
{  "accountID": "9b1deb4d-3b7d-4bad-9bdd-2b0d7b3dcb6d",  "professionID": "mining",  "expectedCurrentTier": 3}
3.2 Server-Authoritative Processing Response
Upon verifying that the shared village bank possesses the matching Gold and Refined Bar quotas, the server locks the account row, executes the balance deduction, increments the tier, and returns the modified global multiplier state.
{  "transactionSuccess": true,  "updatedToolTier": 4,  "newSpeedModifier": 0.15,  "remainingVillageGold": 1420500,  "syncTimestamp": "2026-07-01T22:15:30Z"}
4. Legacy Data Migration Pipeline Script
For existing production environments transitioning away from the deprecated durability framework, this migration routine converts discrete tool items into raw currency compensation before updating the global village tier structure.
BEGIN;-- Step 1: Compensate accounts by converting legacy tool items to flat Gold values-- T1 to T3 tool instances are refunded at 50% of their base value matrixUPDATE village_infrastructure viSET village_gold = vi.village_gold + sub.refund_totalFROM (    SELECT account_id, SUM(base_value_gold * 0.50) as refund_total    FROM items    WHERE item_slot_type IN ('pickaxe', 'axe', 'harpoon', 'sickle')    GROUP BY account_id) subWHERE vi.account_id = sub.account_id;-- Step 2: Automatically map the highest-tier item owned to the new permanent upgrade columnUPDATE village_infrastructure viSET mining_tool_tier = COALESCE((    SELECT MAX(current_rarity_tier)     FROM items     WHERE items.account_id = vi.account_id AND items.item_slot_type = 'pickaxe'), 1);-- Step 3: Delete the deprecated tool instances safely from the live database rowsDELETE FROM items WHERE item_slot_type IN ('pickaxe', 'axe', 'harpoon', 'sickle');COMMIT;

2. Server-Authoritative Multi-Slot Tick Processing Loop
This logical pseudocode architecture outlines how the background engine orchestrates state changes for active character units without creating resource deadlocks.
Function ProcessGlobalServerTick(ElapsedTimeSeconds):
GlobalTickInterval = 0.1
For Each ActivePlayerAccount In ServerActiveDatabase:
For Each ActiveSlot In ActivePlayerAccount.ActiveSlots (Max 3):
Character = ActiveSlot.AssignedCharacter
If Character.FsmState == "Combat_Active":
Character.AccumulatedCombatTicks += ElapsedTimeSeconds
If Character.AccumulatedCombatTicks >= Character.CalculateAttackInterval():
ExecuteCombatTurnSequence(Character, ActiveSlot.TargetEnemy)
Character.AccumulatedCombatTicks = 0.0
Else If Character.FsmState == "Gathering_Active":
Character.AccumulatedGatheringTime += ElapsedTimeSeconds
Node = ActiveSlot.TargetNode
If Character.AccumulatedGatheringTime >= Node.CalculateRequiredTime(Character):
ExecuteGatheringYieldSequence(Character, Node, ActivePlayerAccount.SharedInventory)
Character.AccumulatedGatheringTime = 0.0
Else If Character.FsmState == "Crafting_Active":
Character.AccumulatedCraftingTime += ElapsedTimeSeconds
QueueItem = ActiveSlot.ActiveCraftingQueue.CurrentItem
If Character.AccumulatedCraftingTime >= QueueItem.CalculateCraftingTime(Character):
ExecuteCraftingCompletionSequence(Character, QueueItem, ActivePlayerAccount.SharedInventory)
Character.AccumulatedCraftingTime = 0.0
3. Step-by-Step Combat Resolution Walkthrough
This simulation case details a precise step-by-step mathematical validation tracking an interaction between a Level 10 Draugr character and the Region 01 Boss: Moss-Grown Forest Troll.
3.1 Character Configuration Matrix
Race: Draugr (G1 Baseline Modifiers)
Level: 10
Attributes: STR 30 | DEX 15 | INT 10 | CON 20 | LCK 12
Derived Sub-stats: Melee Damage = 60 | Accuracy = 15 | Dodge = 15 | Armor = 20 | Crit Chance = 1.5%
Equipment: Tier 4 Rare Copper Sword (Base Melee Damage 12, scaling multiplier applied, total Weapon Power = 24)
3.2 Boss Configuration Matrix
Level: 10 Moss-Grown Forest Troll
Maximum Health Pool: 3,085 HP
Attack Damage: 92 Damage
Armor Rating: 3 Armor
Dodge Rating: 10
3.3 Turn 1 Logic Execution
Step 1: Player Hit Determination Checking
\text{Hit Chance} = \min\left(0.95, \max\left(0.05, \frac{15_{\text{Player Accuracy}}}{10_{\text{Enemy Dodge}}}\right)\right) = \min(0.95, 1.50) = 0.95
The random seed rolls 0.42. Roll is less than or equal to 0.95, validating a successful Hit.
Step 2: Player Critical Hit Validation The Crit Chance tracker is 1.5% (0.015). The random seed rolls 0.78. Roll is greater than 0.015, evaluating Crit Modifier to 1.0x (Standard Hit).
Step 3: Player Damage and Mitigation Calculations
\text{Damage}_{\text{Raw}} = (60_{\text{Player Melee Dmg}} + 24_{\text{Weapon Power}}) \times 1.0 \times 1.0_{\text{Crit Mod}} = 84 \text{Damage}_{\text{Net}} = \max\left(1, 84_{\text{Damage Raw}} - 3_{\text{Boss Armor}}\right) = 81
The Moss-Grown Forest Troll loses exactly 81 Health Points. Boss Current HP shifts from 3,085 down to 3,004 HP.
Step 4: Draugr Passive Lifesteal Injection Draugr passive converts 8% of inflicted melee damage into immediate health restoration points.
\text{Health Recovered} = \lfloor 81_{\text{Net Damage}} \times 0.08 \rfloor = \lfloor 6.48 \rfloor = 6\text{ HP}
The character receives 6 flat health points back into its tracking registry container slot.

MODULE 43: LINEAGE BREEDING MECHANICS, GENETIC INHERITANCE ENGINES & MUTATION SIEVES
1. The Genetic Allele Map & Chromosome Structure
To support complex character generation across generations, Folk-Idle implements a server-authoritative Mendelian genetic inheritance framework. Every character profile carries a hidden 64-bit structural genome payload (genetic_vector) split into distinct gene locuses that determine physical traits, combat multipliers, and production efficiency modifiers.
1.1 Chromosome Bitwise Architecture
The 64-bit integer payload is segmented into discrete bit-masks mapping dominant and recessive trait configurations.
+-------------------+-------------------+-------------------+-------------------+| bits 00-15: Race  | bits 16-31: Stats | bits 32-47: Perks | bits 48-63: Color || Dominant/Recess.  | Dominant/Recess.  | Dominant/Recess.  | Dominant/Recess.  |+-------------------+-------------------+-------------------+-------------------+
Each locus allocates 8 bits for the Dominant Allele (A_D) and 8 bits for the Recessive Allele (A_R).
Locus Bit-Range
Property Tag
Phenotype Expression Vector
Baseline Multiplier
0x000000000000FFFF
LOCUS_RACE
Determines base lineage (Vila, Leshy, Vodnik)
Custom Sprite Set
0x00000000FFFF0000
LOCUS_SPEED
Global action cadence scaling parameter
+0.05\text{ to }+0.25\text{ Speed}
0x0000FFFF00000000
LOCUS_CRIT
Critical strike probability bonus modifier
+1.0\%\text{ to }+5.0\%\text{ Crit}
0xFFFF000000000000
LOCUS_YIELD
Double-harvest frequency distribution probability
+2.0\%\text{ to }+10.0\%\text{ Drop}
2. Cross-Breeding Splicing Math & Punnett Probabilities
When two characters are deployed into the Ancient Lineage Incubation Chamber, the engine splices parental chromosomes. For each locus, the offspring draws one allele from the paternal vector and one from the maternal vector using an unmanaged cryptographic random uniform selection distribution.
2.1 Phenotype Dominance Resolution
The active trait value is governed strictly by allele dominance hierarchies mapped within the system configuration matrix. Let the paternal alleles be (P_D, P_R) and maternal alleles be (M_D, M_R). The child's generated pair (C_D, C_R) is resolved via a four-way uniform probability state array:
\mathbb{P}((C_D, C_R)) = \begin{cases} 0.25 & \text{for } (P_D, M_D) \\ 0.25 & \text{for } (P_D, M_R) \\ 0.25 & \text{for } (P_R, M_D) \\ 0.25 & \text{for } (P_R, M_R) \end{cases}
Once selected, the allele possessing the higher inherent dominance coefficient becomes C_D, forcing the alternative selection to occupy the recessive storage bucket C_R.
2.2 Algorithmic Genetic Mutation Sieve
Before sealing the chromosome data payload, the splicing engine passes the vector through a mutation filter check. The mutation probability (P_{\text{mut}}) drops linearly as generation indices grow, preventing uncontrolled late-game power creep:
P_{\text{mut}} = \max \left( 0.001, P_{\text{base}} \times \theta^{-\text{Gen}_{\text{max}}} + \sum \Delta M_{\text{catalyst}} \right)
Where:
P_{\text{base}} is the fundamental mutation probability parameter (0.015).
\theta is the generational attenuation dampening coefficient (1.12).
\text{Gen}_{\text{max}} is the highest generation index between the two parent rows.
\Delta M_{\text{catalyst}} represents explicit enhancement variables gained from consuming Legacy Store catalysts.
3. Server-Authoritative Incubation Resolution Execution
To ensure complete isolation against timing exploits or multi-instancing client race conditions during incubation loops, the birth resolution logic runs inside atomic database locks.
3.1 Unmanaged Genetic Splicing Core Routine (C# Backend)
public class GeneticSplicingEngine{    private const double BaseMutationRate = 0.015;    private const double AttenuationFactor = 1.12;    public ulong ExecuteSplicing(ulong paternalGenome, ulong maternalGenome, int maxParentGen, double catalystBonus)    {        ulong childGenome = 0;        // Iterate through the 4 isolated 16-bit trait locuses        for (int shift = 0; shift < 64; shift += 16)        {            ushort paternalLocus = (ushort)((paternalGenome >> shift) & 0xFFFF);            ushort maternalLocus = (ushort)((maternalGenome >> shift) & 0xFFFF);            byte childDominant = SelectAllele(paternalLocus, maternalLocus);            byte childRecessive = SelectAllele(paternalLocus, maternalLocus);            // Execute mutation check filter            double mutationThreshold = Math.Max(0.001, BaseMutationRate * Math.Pow(AttenuationFactor, -maxParentGen) + catalystBonus);            double roll = System.Security.Cryptography.RandomNumberGenerator.GetDouble();            if (roll <= mutationThreshold)            {                childDominant = ExecuteAlleleMutation(childDominant);            }            // Enforce dominance sorting constraint configuration            if (GetDominanceValue(childRecessive) > GetDominanceValue(childDominant))            {                byte temporarySwapValue = childDominant;                childDominant = childRecessive;                childRecessive = temporarySwapValue;            }            ulong packedLocus = ((ulong)childDominant << 8) | childRecessive;            childGenome |= (packedLocus << shift);        }        return childGenome;    }    private byte SelectAllele(ushort parentLocus, ushort alternativeLocus)    {        bool useAlternative = (System.Security.Cryptography.RandomNumberGenerator.GetInt32(0, 2) == 1);        ushort targetLocus = useAlternative ? alternativeLocus : parentLocus;                return (System.Security.Cryptography.RandomNumberGenerator.GetInt32(0, 2) == 1)             ? (byte)(targetLocus & 0xFF)             : (byte)((targetLocus >> 8) & 0xFF);    }    private byte GetDominanceValue(byte allele) => (byte)(allele & 0x7F);    private byte ExecuteAlleleMutation(byte baseAllele) => (byte)(baseAllele ^ 0x1F); // Mutate gene configuration bits}
4. Relational Database Lineage Integrity Schema
The lineage state matrix uses self-referencing relationship columns to guarantee that character records preserve tree lineages for performance audits.
CREATE TABLE character_lineage_registry (    character_id UUID PRIMARY KEY,    account_id UUID NOT NULL,    generation_index INT NOT NULL DEFAULT 1,    parent_paternal_id UUID REFERENCES character_lineage_registry(character_id),    parent_maternal_id UUID REFERENCES character_lineage_registry(character_id),    genetic_vector BIGINT NOT NULL,    unlocked_at TIMESTAMP WITH TIME ZONE DEFAULT NOW() NOT NULL,    CONSTRAINT chk_generational_progression CHECK (        (generation_index = 1 AND parent_paternal_id IS NULL AND parent_maternal_id IS NULL) OR        (generation_index > 1 AND parent_paternal_id IS NOT NULL AND parent_maternal_id IS NOT NULL)    ));CREATE INDEX idx_lineage_account_search ON character_lineage_registry (account_id, generation_index);

2. Character Experience (XP) Progression Curve
To maintain a balanced pacing structure, the required experience to advance from Character Level L to Level L+1 follows a combined polynomial and geometric curve.
XP_Required(L) = floor(100 * 1.16^(L-1) + 150 * (L-1))

Level 10 to 11: 1,761 XP

Boss Health Multiplier: HP_Boss = HP_Standard(L) * 8.5

5.2 Item Affix Distribution Constraints
Depending strictly on the item's Rarity Tier, it receives a fixed allocation of random secondary stats (affixes) selected from the combat sub-stat database. Each higher rarity tier naturally increases the item's baseline weapon damage or armor properties alongside these affix counts.
Tiers 1–3 (Normal to Uncommon): 1 Random Affix
Tiers 4–6 (Rare to Epic): 2 Random Affixes
Tiers 7–9 (Legendary to Relic): 3 Random Affixes
Tiers 10–12 (Ancient to Demonic): 4 Random Affixes
Tiers 13–14 (Godly to Transcendent): 5 Random Affixes

Baseline Premium Drop Chance: All standard and elite monsters hold a flat, static 0.05% chance to drop 1 Diamond upon defeat. Regional Bosses hold a 100% chance to drop a flat cluster of 10 Diamonds.
Reroll Calculation Cost: The price in Diamonds to execute a reroll scale is entirely dependent on the item's current Rarity Tier (N).
Diamond_Cost = floor(5 * 1.35^(N-1))

Tier 7 (Legendary): 24 Diamonds per reroll

MODULE 01: CORE ARCHITECTURE & MATHEMATICAL FRAMEWORK
1. Core Game Loop & State Machine
The game operates on a shared-resource economy model where up to three active character units are concurrently assigned to specific tasks (Combat, Gathering, or Crafting) while drawing from and contributing to a centralized village inventory.
1.1 Progression Milestones
Level 1–19: 1 Active Character Slot unlocked. Baseline Human race available.
Level 20: 2 Active Character Slots unlocked. Access to mid-tier folklore races.
Level 50: 3 Active Character Slots unlocked (Maximum). All 7 base races discoverable.
Village Population Cap: Hard-capped at 50 total population slots. Non-active population resides in the Village Pool for breeding, mentoring, or passive town utility.
2. Mathematical Systems & Game Formulae
2.1 The Combat Loop Engine
Combat is processed sequentially via deterministic time increments (ticks) based on the Attack Speed (AS) attribute of both entities. The entity with the lower tick threshold attacks first.
Step 1: Hit Determination
\text{Hit Chance} = \min\left(0.95, \max\left(0.05, \frac{\text{Accuracy}_{\text{Attacker}}}{\text{Dodge}_{\text{Defender}}}\right)\right)
Step 2: Critical Hit Check
If Hit is successful, evaluate Critical Chance (\text{CRIT}\%) using a random roll between 0 and 1.
If \text{Random}(0,1) \le \text{CRIT}\%, then \text{Crit Modifier} = \text{Critical Damage Multiplier}.
Otherwise, \text{Crit Modifier} = 1.0.
Step 3: Mitigation & Damage Calculation
Damage mitigation uses a flat armor reduction model capped by a maximal damage reduction percentage.
\text{Damage}_{\text{Raw}} = \text{Base Damage} \times \text{Damage Modifier} \times \text{Crit Modifier} \text{Damage}_{\text{Net}} = \max\left(1, \text{Damage}_{\text{Raw}} - \text{Armor}_{\text{Defender}}\right)
Step 4: Shield Block Check (Player Only)
If the player has a shield equipped and \text{Random}(0,1) \le \text{Block Chance}:
\text{Damage}_{\text{Final}} = \max\left(0, \text{Damage}_{\text{Net}} - \text{Block Strength}\right)
Otherwise:
\text{Damage}_{\text{Final}} = \text{Damage}_{\text{Net}}
Step 5: Auto-Eat Algorithmic Validation
Immediately following damage application, the engine evaluates the player's health threshold:
\text{Condition:} \quad HP_{\text{Current}} \le \left( \frac{\text{Slider Value}}{100} \times HP_{\text{Max}} \right)
If the condition returns true, the highest-healing food item is consumed from the shared inventory. If no food is present, combat terminates immediately, preventing character death and resetting the state to Idle.
2.2 Offline AFK Extraction Engine
When the client transitions offline, the engine logs the timestamp (T_{\text{start}}). Upon reconnection (T_{\text{end}}), total elapsed time \Delta T = T_{\text{end}} - T_{\text{start}} is divided into three distinct efficiency tiers based on time degradation curves.
Time Degradation Tiers
Tier 1 (\Delta T \le 8\text{ hours}): Efficiency Multiplier (E_{\text{mult}}) = 1.0
Tier 2 (8\text{ hours} < \Delta T \le 16\text{ hours}): Efficiency Multiplier (E_{\text{mult}}) = 0.5
Tier 3 (16\text{ hours} < \Delta T \le 24\text{ hours}): Efficiency Multiplier (E_{\text{mult}}) = 0.25
Tier 4 (\Delta T > 24\text{ hours}): Efficiency Multiplier (E_{\text{mult}}) = 0.0
Total Effective Action Time (T_{\text{eff}}) Calculation
T_{\text{eff}} = \sum (\Delta T_{\text{Tier}} \times E_{\text{mult}})
Gathering Resource Yield Formula
\text{Actions}_{\text{Total}} = \left\lfloor \frac{T_{\text{eff}}}{\text{Base Tool Speed} \times (1 - \text{Gathering Speed}\%)} \right\rfloor \text{Yield}_{\text{Final}} = \text{Actions}_{\text{Total}} \times (1 + \text{Yield Bonus}\%) \times \text{Tool Durability Coefficient}
If \text{Actions}_{\text{Total}} exceeds total tool durability or inventory storage space, the simulation cuts off execution at the exact timestamp of exhaustion.
2.3 Forge Progression Exponential Scaling
Upgrading equipment items to higher rarity tiers requires compounding materials. Upgrading from Tier N to Tier N+1 requires exactly 3 copies of the item at Tier N plus a geometric gold scaling cost.
Tier 1 - Normal: Cumulative Items Needed = 1
Tier 2 - Common: Upgrade Cost = 1 \times \text{Base Gold} | Cumulative Items Needed = 3
Tier 3 - Uncommon: Upgrade Cost = 3 \times \text{Base Gold} | Cumulative Items Needed = 9
Tier 4 - Rare: Upgrade Cost = 9 \times \text{Base Gold} | Cumulative Items Needed = 27
Tier 5 - Ultra Rare: Upgrade Cost = 27 \times \text{Base Gold} | Cumulative Items Needed = 81
Tier 6 - Epic: Upgrade Cost = 81 \times \text{Base Gold} | Cumulative Items Needed = 243
Tier 7 - Legendary: Upgrade Cost = 243 \times \text{Base Gold} | Cumulative Items Needed = 729
Tier 8 - Mythic: Upgrade Cost = 729 \times \text{Base Gold} | Cumulative Items Needed = 2,187
Tier 9 - Relic: Upgrade Cost = 2,187 \times \text{Base Gold} | Cumulative Items Needed = 6,561
Tier 10 - Ancient: Upgrade Cost = 6,561 \times \text{Base Gold} | Cumulative Items Needed = 19,683
Tier 11 - Divine: Upgrade Cost = 19,683 \times \text{Base Gold} | Cumulative Items Needed = 59,049
Tier 12 - Demonic: Upgrade Cost = 59,049 \times \text{Base Gold} | Cumulative Items Needed = 177,147
Tier 13 - Godly: Upgrade Cost = 177,147 \times \text{Base Gold} | Cumulative Items Needed = 531,441
Tier 14 - Transcendent: Upgrade Cost = 531,441 \times \text{Base Gold} | Cumulative Items Needed = 1,594,323
To achieve a single Transcendent item completely from base inputs:
\text{Total Items Required} = 3^{13} = 1,594,323 \text{ units}
3. Database Schema & Relational Entity Models
The database schema outlines the core relational layout for deployment within a PostgreSQL / Supabase backend infrastructure.
3.1 Relational Schema Definitions
Table: characters
id: UUID (Primary Key, Default: gen_random_uuid())
village_id: UUID (Not Null)
name: VARCHAR(64) (Not Null)
race: ENUM ('Human', 'Vila', 'Fomóiri', 'Draugr', 'Kobold', 'Moosleute', 'Vodník') (Default: 'Human')
generation: INT (Not Null, Default: 1)
age_tier: ENUM ('Child', 'Adult', 'Senior', 'Old') (Default: 'Adult')
experience: INT (Not Null, Default: 0)
level: INT (Not Null, Default: 1)
primary_stats: JSONB (Default: {"strength": 10, "dexterity": 10, "intelligence": 10, "constitution": 10, "luck": 10})
genetic_growth_modifiers: JSONB (Default: {"strength_mod": 1.0, "dexterity_mod": 1.0, "intelligence_mod": 1.0, "constitution_mod": 1.0, "luck_mod": 1.0})
created_at: TIMESTAMP WITH TIME ZONE (Default: NOW())
Table: character_skills
character_id: UUID (Foreign Key references characters.id, On Delete Cascade)
skill_type: ENUM ('Attack', 'Strength', 'Defence', 'Ranged', 'Mining', 'Smithing', 'Woodcutting', 'Herbalism', 'Fishing', 'Cooking', 'Alchemy')
current_level: INT (Not Null, Default: 1)
current_xp: BIGINT (Not Null, Default: 0)
Primary Key constraints: (character_id, skill_type)
Table: items
id: UUID (Primary Key, Default: gen_random_uuid())
village_id: UUID (Not Null)
base_item_id: VARCHAR(64) (Not Null, e.g., 'iron_sword')
rarity_tier: INT (Not Null, Range validation 1 to 14)
quality_multiplier: NUMERIC(4,2) (Not Null, Default: 1.00)
is_equipped: BOOLEAN (Not Null, Default: FALSE)
affix_data: JSONB (Default: {"flat_stats": {}, "percent_stats": {}})
Table: character_equipment
character_id: UUID (Foreign Key references characters.id, On Delete Cascade)
slot_type: ENUM ('Weapon', 'Shield', 'Helmet', 'Chest', 'Leggings', 'Boots', 'Ring1', 'Ring2', 'Amulet')
item_id: UUID (Foreign Key references items.id, On Delete RESTRICT)
Primary Key constraints: (character_id, slot_type)
Unique constraint: item_id must be unique across the entire table

MODULE 39: CUSTOMER SUPPORT TICKET PIPELINES, IN-GAME DIAGNOSTIC REGISTRIES & PLAYER MODERATION INTERFACES
1. In-Game "Flight Recorder" Diagnostic Ring Buffer
To resolve edge-case synchronization errors, transaction drops, or game-state rollbacks without overwhelming server storage, the client maintains an unmanaged, in-memory diagnostic ring buffer. This acting "Flight Recorder" continuously captures execution traces, memory limits, and network headers.
1.1 In-Memory Ring Buffer Topology
The log stream is bounded by a strict allocation cap to prevent memory leaks on target devices. When the buffer hits its maximum entry threshold, the oldest log row index is automatically overwritten (O(1) allocation).
[Index 00] -> [Index 01] -> [Index 02] -> [Index 03] -> [Index 04] (Active Tail)    ^                                                          |    +-------------------- Overwrites When Full ----------------+
Maximum Trace Capacity: Locked at exactly 250 rows of historical entries.
Storage Footprint Ceiling: Restricted to <2 MB of raw unmanaged memory.
Log Scrubbing Protocol: Personal information, authentication session keys, and raw billing passwords are systematically filtered out at the collection boundary via regex masks before hitting the memory stack.
2. Server-Authoritative Ticket Ingestion API Contracts
When a user submits an error report or an item discrepancy appeal via the help interface, the client attaches the serialized memory dump from the Flight Recorder to an HTTP POST request targeting the secure /api/v1/support/tickets/create route.
2.1 Ticket Submission JSON Schema Payload
Ingestion Destination: Routes directly to automated processing pipelines linked to customer support platforms (e.g., Zendesk, Jira Service Desk).
{  "ticketMetadata": {    "accountID": "9b1deb4d-3b7d-4bad-9bdd-2b0d7b3dcb6d",    "submissionTimestamp": "2026-07-01T22:45:00Z",    "categoryClassification": "BUG_REPORTS_VILLAGE_UPGRADE",    "playerDescriptionText": "My T4 forge upgrade consumed gold but did not complete after server maintenance."  },  "deviceEnvironmentDiagnostics": {    "applicationVersion": "v1.4.2",    "clientGraphicsAPI": "Vulkan (Android)",    "availableSystemRAMBytes": 1073741824  },  "flightRecorderDumpPayload": [    {      "logTimestamp": "2026-07-01T22:42:10Z",      "severityLevel": "INFO",      "subsystemSource": "NETWORK_WS",      "messageText": "WebSocket initialization handshake confirmed on shard node 04."    },    {      "logTimestamp": "2026-07-01T22:43:15Z",      "severityLevel": "ERROR",      "subsystemSource": "DATABASE_RELAY",      "messageText": "Transaction ID 9921b validation mismatch. MODULE 34: REAL-TIME CHAT INFRASTRUCTURE, TEXT FILTERING ENGINES & WEBSOCKETS COMMUNICATION MESH
1. Redis Pub/Sub WebSocket Chat Cluster
To handle global channels, regional rooms, and guild communications without causing thread blocks on the core simulation API nodes, the chat network is isolated into a separate microservice layer driven by WebSockets (ws://) and backed by a Redis Pub/Sub routing mesh.
1.1 Asynchronous Message Routing Topology
When a client sends a text packet, the connection does not query the primary relational database. It relies entirely on in-memory memory brokers.
+------------------+     +-----------------------+     +-----------------------+|  Client Device   | --> | Chat Microservice Pod | --> | Redis Pub/Sub Cluster || (WebSocket Pipe) |     |  (Token Verification) |     | (Channel Broadcaster) |+------------------+     +-----------------------+     +-----------------------+                                                            |                                                            v+------------------+     +-----------------------+     +-----------------------+| Recipient Client | <-- | Chat Microservice Pod | <-- | Matching Cluster Node || (Instant Render) |     |  (Mesh Forwarding)    |     | (Message Broadcast)   |+------------------+     +-----------------------+     +-----------------------+
1.2 Channel Subscription Model
Chat traffic routes through explicit string channels managed by the memory broker.
Global Channel: chat:global:en, chat:global:cs, chat:global:de
Regional Room Channel: chat:region:04:chasm
Guild Private Channel: chat:guild:dc91a2b3-cf4e-4112-9f88
2. Profanity & Regular Expression Regex Filtering Sieve
Before a text packet is published to a channel, the Chat Microservice passes the string payload through an optimized, multi-tier regex array scanner to suppress toxic behavior, prevent phishing links, and strip illegal characters.
2.1 Levenshtein Distance Variance Matching
To stop players from bypassing filter databases using character substitutions (e.g., replacing 'a' with '@'), strings are evaluated using a modified Levenshtein metric against restricted word vectors. If the edit distance (LD) falls below a specified threshold relative to the target bad word length, the packet is flagged.
\text{Match Ratio} = 1.0 - \frac{LD(\text{InputWord}, \text{TargetWord})}{\max(\text{len}(\text{InputWord}), \text{len}(\text{TargetWord}))}
An input string triggers a filtration action if the Match Ratio exceeds 0.80.
2.2 Rate-Limiting & Spam Suppression Metrics
To protect connection pipelines from macro injection loops, the chat engine enforces token-bucket rate throttling.
Maximum Bucket Capacity: 5 message tokens.
Token Regeneration Pacing: 1 token added to the bucket every 2.0 seconds.
Burst Limit Violation: If a client exhausts its token bucket and transmits an immediate sequence packet, the server drops the message, appends a hidden alert flag to the account payload, and forces a temporary 60-second mute on the active socket.
3. Database Storage & Eviction Policy for Logs
While real-time text delivery is managed in memory, security frameworks require messages to be logged for moderation reviews. To prevent storage tables from expanding uncontrollably, log tables utilize automatic timescale partitioning and data eviction windows.
3.1 Partitioned Chat Log Table Schema
CREATE TABLE account_chat_logs (    log_id BIGSERIAL,    account_id UUID NOT NULL,    target_channel_key VARCHAR(64) NOT NULL,    raw_message_text VARCHAR(256) NOT NULL,    is_filtered BOOLEAN DEFAULT FALSE NOT NULL,    transmitted_at TIMESTAMP WITH TIME ZONE DEFAULT NOW() NOT NULL) PARTITION BY RANGE (transmitted_at);-- Create specific weekly indexes to allow smooth partition dropsCREATE TABLE chat_logs_y2026_w27 PARTITION OF account_chat_logs    FOR VALUES FROM ('2026-06-29 00:00:00+00') TO ('2026-07-06 00:00:00+00');
3.2 Automated Rolling Pruning Cron Job
A server cron task executes a weekly partition sweep every Monday at 02:00 UTC. To maintain strict storage limits, database chunks older than 7 calendar days are permanently unlinked and dropped from disk blocks using low-overhead metadata mutations rather than slow, resource-heavy row deletion queries.
-- Automated database pipeline cleanup script executed by server infrastructureDROP TABLE IF EXISTS chat_logs_y2026_w25;

MODULE 31: DISASTER RECOVERY PLAYBOOKS, DATA RECONCILIATION & ROLLBACK RUNBOOKS
1. Point-In-Time Recovery (PITR) Scheduling & WAL Infrastructures
To guarantee complete recovery integrity against unmitigated hardware cluster failure, primary database instances execute continuous streaming Write-Ahead Logging (WAL) protocols combined with scheduled physical backups.
1.1 Disaster Storage Hierarchy Strategy
Base Physical Backups: Captured automatically every 24 hours at 03:00 UTC during low-traffic periods. Snapshots are compressed, cryptographically signed, and moved directly to a geographically isolated, non-volatile cloud object bucket.
Continuous WAL Archival Cadence: WAL segments are streamed continuously to secondary hot backup targets. The maximum allowed recovery data gap (Recovery Point Objective - RPO) is restricted to exactly 15 seconds.
2. Split-Brain Network Data Reconciliation Algorithms
If a cross-shard cluster node partitions due to localized infrastructure routing failures, regional nodes can inadvertently create diverging event entries. When structural network pathways reconnect, the server evaluates records using deterministic resolution vectors.
2.1 The Vector Timestamp Reconciliation Sieve
Let a transaction update state contain a composite sequence ID (C_{\text{seq}}) tracking the state mutations across the global network matrix.
C_seq = { Shard_ID, Wall_Clock_Timestamp, Logic_Epoch_Counter }
2.2 Algorithmic Resolution Branch Conflict Engine
When structural overlapping items populate database tables, conflict logic processes the incoming state parameters using an execution evaluation chart:
                  +-----------------------------------+                  |  Detect Split-Brain Divergence   |                  +-----------------------------------+                                    |                    Inspect Structural Logic_Epoch                                    v         +--------------------------+--------------------------+         | If Epochs Mismatch                                  | If Epochs Match Exactly         v                                                     v+------------------------+                            +------------------------+| Accept High-Index      |                            | Inspect Cryptographic  || Epoch Sequence Row     |                            | HMAC Signature Payload |+------------------------+                            +------------------------+                                                               |                                                      True Microsecond Timing Sieve                                                               v                                                      +------------------------+                                                      | Keep First Confirmed   |                                                      | Server-Side NTP Entry  |                                                      +------------------------+
Rejected delta sequences are thrown out, and the lost material values are converted into equivalent generic Gold currency items pushed directly to the user's Village Mailbox to completely safeguard asset integrity.
3. Catastrophic State Restoration Runbook Pipeline
If a cluster crash corrupts the Redis operational cache tier, system administrators follow a step-by-step restoration checklist to rebuild the transient runtime environments.
3.1 Step 1: Client Gateway Traffic Severance
Execute immediate Layer 7 Load Balancer route blocks to isolate backend networks.
Redirect incoming client connections to a static CDN-hosted "System Preservation Mode" announcement screen, halting all incoming API traffic updates.
3.2 Step 2: Relational Database Verification Pass
Verify the integrity of the core PostgreSQL database cluster. Query the transaction logs table to identify the latest globally stable timestamp index (T_{\text{stable}}):
SELECT transaction_id, recorded_at FROM transaction_audit_ledger ORDER BY recorded_at DESC LIMIT 1;
3.3 Step 3: Redis Transient Memory Structure Reconstruction
Clear corrupt Redis instance storage slots using the cluster clear command layout.
Execute a cold rebuild script that reads character allocation profiles, attributes matrices, and item ownership entries directly from the validated PostgreSQL database state at timestamp T_{\text{stable}}.
Repopulate the Redis ZSET leaderboard datasets cleanly, computing scores on stateless worker nodes.
3.4 Step 4: System Reset Validation Checks
Execute the automated CI/CD simulation test suite (Module 10 math verifications) against the re-cached Redis state layer to ensure attributes and math scaling maps perfectly.
3.5 Step 5: Gateway Re-Opening Protocol
Remove the Layer 7 Load Balancer traffic blocks, allowing users to reconnect.
Monitor backend telemetry ingestion metrics over a 15-minute observation window to ensure the multi-slot tick processing loop tracks smoothly.

MODULE 50: PRODUCTION READINESS CHECKLIST, SYSTEM FINALIZATION SIGN-OFF & ARCHITECTURE ACCEPTANCE MATRIX
1. Load Testing Scaling Verification Criteria (CCU Targets)
Before routing active production traffic through the Anycast edge gateways, the multi-region infrastructure must pass a continuous 48-hour synthetic load injection simulation. The cluster must meet specific Key Performance Indicators (KPIs) under a baseline load of 100,000 Concurrent Connected Users (CCU) with simulated network conditions mimicking mobile networks.
1.1 Peak Throughput Volumetric Equation
The system calculates required peak ingestion throughput capabilities (Q_{\text{peak}}) across stateless API layers to prevent thread starvation under concurrent batch automation flushes:
Q_{\text{peak}} = \frac{\text{CCU} \times R_{\text{tick}}}{B_{\text{batch}}} \times S_{\text{safety}}
Where:
\text{CCU} = 100,000 (Target Concurrent Connected Users).
R_{\text{tick}} = 0.1\text{ Hz} (Standard 10-second client payload batch compilation interval).
B_{\text{batch}} represents the compression aggregation coefficient, set to 1.0.
S_{\text{safety}} = 2.5 (Safety burst multiplier tracking sudden regional spikes or thundering herd scenarios after network drops).
The target architecture must handle a continuous minimum capacity of 25,000 requests per second (RPS) at the API gateway tier with zero drop errors.
1.2 Target Performance Metrics Thresholds
The deployment pipeline automatically rejects builds if load-testing clusters fail to maintain performance constraints within the following margins:
[Gateway Ingestion] ---> (95th Percentile: ≤ 45ms) ---> [Verified DB Multi-Shards]                    ---> (99th Percentile: ≤ 120ms) ---> [State Saved Successfully]
Maximum Error Error Rate Threshold: < 0.01\% across all standard database write routes under maximum load conditions.
Maximum Node Resource Ceiling: CPU utilization metrics across Kubernetes compute pods must stabilize below 70\% to preserve headroom for scaling operations.

MODULE 53: FORGE ARCHITECTURE, ITEM FUSION MECHANICS, STAT RE-ROLL ENGINE & DURABILITY-FREE MARKET INTEGRATION
1. Forge Architecture as the Primary Item Sink
Due to the removal of equipment durability, the Forge bears full structural responsibility for stabilizing the game's virtual economy. It operates as a mandatory deflationary filter that consumes the excess supply of equipment generated 24/7 by automated background farming. Items do not decay through use; instead, they are deliberately sacrificed to drive vertical power progression.
1.1 Item Fusion Matrix
To upgrade an item from Tier T to Tier T+1, the player must insert 1 primary item and 2 identical sacrificial items of the exact same base item type and Tier into the Forge interface.
The probability of a successful fusion (P_{\text{fusion}}) decays exponentially as the target Tier scaling increases:
P_{\text{fusion}}(T) = \max \left( 0.05, \; \text{BaseRate} \times \gamma^{-(T - 1)} + \Delta_{\text{catalyst}} \right)
Where:
\text{BaseRate} = 1.00 (100\% success rate when transitioning from T1 to T2).
\gamma = 1.45 (the probability attenuation coefficient).
T represents the current base Tier of the source items.
\Delta_{\text{catalyst}} is the percentage modifier bonus injected by rare or premium stabilizers consumed during the process.
1.2 Fusion Outcome Matrix and Destruction Ratios
Base Tier
Target Tier
Base Success Rate (P_{\text{fusion}})
Failure Outcome
Tier 1
Tier 2
100\%
No risk (Baseline tutorial validation step)
Tier 2
Tier 3
68.9\%
Sacrificial items destroyed; primary item preserved; maximum durability drops by 10 points.
Tier 3

Critical Failure: All 3 items are permanently vaporized. Only 30\% of base crafting materials are salvaged.
Tier 4
Tier 5 (Endgame)
32.8\%
Critical Failure: All 3 items are permanently vaporized. Only 15\% of base crafting materials are salvaged.
2. Reforging Mechanics (Stat Re-roll Engine)
When an item drops or is crafted, the server generates randomized secondary attributes into the item's affix_data_payload (Module 51). If a player wants to re-roll unoptimized affixes, they must process the item through the Forge's Reforging matrix.
2.1 Reforging Cost and Material Scaling Formula
Reforging does not consume raw commodities, but instead requires a Gold Sink fee and one sacrificial item of identical rarity and Tier as an oblation.
The gold cost (C_{\text{reroll}}) escalates with each consecutive attempt performed on that specific item instance to prevent infinite optimization spamming:
C_{\text{reroll}}(n) = \lfloor C_{\text{base}} \times \prod_{i=1}^{n} (1 + \beta \times i) \rfloor
Where:
C_{\text{base}} is the baseline re-roll fee for the given Tier configuration (e.g., T3 = 5,000 Gold).
n represents the total count of prior re-rolls executed on that specific item instance.
\beta = 0.25 (the exponential cost growth scaling factor).
3. Server-Authoritative Item Fusion Transaction Execution
The fusion process is a primary target for race-condition duplication exploits (e.g., trying to fire twin network packets to merge the same item within the same millisecond window). The server enforces strict database-level row serialization.
public class ForgeSplicingEngine{    private readonly IDatabaseContext dbContext;    public async Task<ForgeResult> ExecuteItemFusionAsync(Guid accountId, long primaryId, long sacrificeId1, long sacrificeId2)    {        // Enforce serializable isolation to eliminate duplicate concurrent execution loops        using (var transaction = await dbContext.Database.BeginTransactionAsync(System.Data.IsolationLevel.Serializable))        {            try            {                // 1. Lock all 3 item rows in a strict, deterministic sequence by ID to prevent database deadlocks                var itemIds = new[] { primaryId, sacrificeId1, sacrificeId2 };                Array.Sort(itemIds);                var lockedItems = await dbContext.EquipmentInstances.LockRowsForUpdate(itemIds);                                var primaryItem = lockedItems.FirstOrDefault(e => e.InstanceId == primaryId && e.OwnerAccountId == accountId);                var sac1 = lockedItems.FirstOrDefault(e => e.InstanceId == sacrificeId1 && e.OwnerAccountId == accountId);                var sac2 = lockedItems.FirstOrDefault(e => e.InstanceId == sacrificeId2 && e.OwnerAccountId == accountId);                // Validate transaction payload integrity constraints                if (primaryItem == null || sac1 == null || sac2 == null || primaryItem.IsLockedInEscrow || sac1.IsLockedInEscrow || sac2.IsLockedInEscrow)                {                    await transaction.RollbackAsync();                    return ForgeResult.CreateFailure("INVALID_INPUT_ASSETS");                }                if (primaryItem.ItemBaseId != sac1.ItemBaseId || primaryItem.ItemBaseId != sac2.ItemBaseId ||                    primaryItem.ItemQualityTier != sac1.ItemQualityTier || primaryItem.ItemQualityTier != sac2.ItemQualityTier)                {                    await transaction.RollbackAsync();                    return ForgeResult.CreateFailure("TIER_MISMATCH");                }                int currentTier = primaryItem.ItemQualityTier;                                // 2. Compute the random success threshold mapping (Matrix 1.1)                double baseRate = 1.00;                double gamma = 1.45;                double successProbability = Math.Max(0.05, baseRate * Math.Pow(gamma, -(currentTier - 1)));                                double roll = System.Security.Cryptography.RandomNumberGenerator.GetDouble();                if (roll <= successProbability)                {                    // SUCCESS: Advance primary item quality tier, consume and delete sacrificial rows                    primaryItem.ItemQualityTier += 1;                    primaryItem.AffixDataPayload = RecalculateAffixScalers(primaryItem.AffixDataPayload);                    dbContext.EquipmentInstances.Remove(sac1);                    dbContext.EquipmentInstances.Remove(sac2);                    await dbContext.SaveChangesAsync();                    await transaction.CommitAsync();                    return ForgeResult.CreateSuccess(primaryItem.InstanceId, primaryItem.ItemQualityTier);                }                else                {                    // FAILURE: Resolution behavior depends strictly on current item tier                    dbContext.EquipmentInstances.Remove(sac1);                    dbContext.EquipmentInstances.Remove(sac2);                    if (currentTier >= 3)                    {                        // High-Tier Penalty: Vaporize the primary item row as well (Critical Deflationary Sink)                        dbContext.EquipmentInstances.Remove(primaryItem);                        await dbContext.SaveChangesAsync();                        await transaction.CommitAsync();                        return ForgeResult.CreateCriticalFailure("CRITICAL_FAILURE_ALL_DESTROYED");                    }                    // Low-Tier Penalty (Tier 2): Primary item survives but suffers structural max durability degradation                    primaryItem.MaximumDurability = (int)Math.Floor(primaryItem.MaximumDurability * 0.90);                    if (primaryItem.CurrentDurability > primaryItem.MaximumDurability)                    {                        primaryItem.CurrentDurability = primaryItem.MaximumDurability;                    }                    await dbContext.SaveChangesAsync();                    await transaction.CommitAsync();                    return ForgeResult.CreatePartialFailure(primaryItem.InstanceId, "SACRIFICIAL_DESTROYED_PRIMARY_DEGRADED");                }            }            catch (Exception)            {                await transaction.RollbackAsync();                throw;            }        }    }    private string RecalculateAffixScalers(string rawJsonPayload)    {        // Mutates affix stat modifiers based on the new authoritative tier step parameters on the server        return rawJsonPayload;     }}
4. Durability-Free Market Integration Dynamics
By shifting the economic core to the Forge, player-to-player trade routes remain highly active without relying on durability loss mechanics. This sets up a clean value exchange loop between the two primary player personas in the MVP framework:
4.1 Casual Players & Starters (Market Suppliers)
Generate a high volume of Tier 1 and Tier 2 base equipment rows via standard location clearing and raw crafting.
Without the Forge, these items would rapidly drop to a value of 1 Gold due to extreme structural oversupply.
Because of the Forge, these items retain a reliable market value floor since high-tier players constantly buy them to use as upgrade fuel.
4.2 Hardcore Players & Whales (Market Consumers)
Aim to build a flawless Tier 5 Masterpiece loadout for their 3 active MVP character slots.
To overcome the low success rate barriers (32.8\% at the final bottleneck step), they must purchase and burn hundreds of basic equipment items sourced from lower-tier players.
This automatically redirects gold liquidity from the top tier down to progressing accounts, maintaining market velocity through player incentives rather than administrative maintenance rules.

--- Proceed with Module 24_ Cloud Server Farm Auto-Sca.._.docx ---
MODULE 24: CLOUD SERVER FARM AUTO-SCALING, LOAD BALANCER ROUTING ALGORITHMS & HORIZONTAL PERFORMANCE OPTIMIZATION FRAMEWORKS
1. Automated Horizontal Scaling Triggers & Performance Metrics
To manage volatile traffic spikes during weekly leaderboard resets, seasonal rollouts, or world boss windows, the ASP.NET Core compute layer scales horizontally using Kubernetes Horizontal Pod Autoscalers (HPA).
1.1 HPA Target Thresholds Matrix
Compute nodes monitor three primary telemetry vectors to initiate container replication. Scaling occurs when any single threshold is breached over a continuous 60-second observation window.
CPU Utilization Threshold: Metrics Target: 70% sustained core allotment across the active pod cluster pool.
Memory Allocation Bounds: Metrics Target: 85% of allocated container RAM memory limits, signaling high Redis-cache object deserialization queues.
Network Throughput Constraints: Metrics Target: 1,500 concurrent request vectors per second (R_{\text{ps}}) per compute node.
1.2 Cooldown & Stabilization Intervals
To completely prevent cluster thrashing (rapid, successive scaling up and down actions caused by short, erratic processing spikes), the HPA engine enforces rigid operational cooldown windows:
Scale-Up Stabilization Window: Immediate execution upon threshold validation. No delay parameter.
Scale-Down Stabilization Window: Enforces a mandatory 300-second (5 minute) delay period. Pods remain live to absorb immediate echo waves of network traffic before being decommissioned.
2. Layer 7 Load Balancer Architecture & Routing Algorithms
The edge routing matrix utilizes an enterprise-grade NGINX Plus / Cloudflare configuration running Layer 7 application routing architectures.
2.1 Stateless Routing vs. Sticky Sessions
Because the game engine uses a decoupled architecture where character states are held inside a centralized Redis memory tier, the API layer is entirely stateless.
Routing Rule: The load balancer completely blocks sticky sessions (session affinity).
Algorithmic Selection: Routes packets via a Weighted Round-Robin (WRR) algorithm.
Let W_i be the performance weight of worker node i, computed dynamically based on active HTTP connection metrics:
\text{Selection Probability } P(i) = \frac{W_i}{\sum_{j=1}^{N} W_j}
Nodes tracking lower memory allocations or fewer active long-polling WebSocket pipelines are injected with higher operational weights, stabilizing backend cluster wear.
2.2 Layer 7 Path-Based Traffic Separation
The load balancer inspects incoming HTTP target request headers at the firewall boundary to split traffic processing before it enters the pod network:
                  +--------------------------------+                  |  Layer 7 Load Balancer Entry   |                  +--------------------------------+                                  |         +------------------------+------------------------+         | /api/v1/combat/*                                | /api/v1/village/*         v                                                 v+------------------------+                        +------------------------+|  High-Compute Cluster  |                        | Low-Compute Cluster    || (Optimized for Ticks)  |                        | (Optimized for JSONs)  |+------------------------+                        +------------------------+
3. Horizontal Database Sharding & Connection Pooling
As the account registry scales, a single monolithic PostgreSQL instance becomes an indexing bottleneck. The data pipeline implements structural sharding combined with localized connection multiplexing.
3.1 Sharding Topology by Deterministic ID Hashing
Tables containing volatile, row-heavy player parameters (items, characters, character_skills) are split horizontally across N distinct physical database nodes. The specific shard target is determined via a server-authoritative non-cryptographic FNV-1a hashing function executed against the user’s authenticated UUID:
\text{Shard Index} = \text{FNV1a}(\text{account\_id}) \pmod{N_{\text{shards}}}
This guarantees that an individual account's structural data packages always reside within the same physical storage hardware node, eliminating cross-shard JOIN latency penalties.
3.2 PgBouncer Connection Pool Optimization
To prevent database thread exhaustion caused by thousands of stateless API pods initiating concurrent PostgreSQL verification connections, each database shard utilizes a dedicated PgBouncer instance configured for Transaction Pooling mode.
Max Client Connections Limit: 10,000 concurrent client slots allowed from the API gateway nodes.
Server Pool Size Lockout: Fixed at 150 hard connections dedicated to the underlying PostgreSQL engine process, minimizing transaction context-switching overhead on database CPU cores.
4. Failover Orchestration & High-Availability Configurations
The system architecture assumes a zero-trust model regarding network hardware stability. It deploys decoupled circuit-breaking patterns to guarantee structural uptime.
4.1 Redis Cluster Replication & Pub/Sub Sync
The memory caching engine runs across a multi-region Redis Cluster configuration with automated master-replica pairing.
Synchronization Pacing: Write interactions replicate asynchronously from Master to Replica nodes.
Failover Horizon: If a Master Redis node drops off the network mesh, the cluster initiates an automated sentinel vote sequence. A Replica node is promoted to Master within 3.5 seconds. Active client WebSocket lines suffer zero calculation losses, re-pulling missed deltas upon reconnection.
4.2 Circuit Breaker Implementation Model
API compute nodes utilize the Polly framework to safeguard outgoing relational database transactions during high-volume persistence flush sequences:
// Architectural configuration for database write transaction protectionvar dbCircuitBreakerPolicy = Policy    .Handle<DbException>()    .CircuitBreakerAsync(        exceptionsAllowedBeforeBreaking: 5,        durationOfBreak: TimeSpan.FromSeconds(30),        onBreak: (exception, timespan) => {             // Halt incoming SQL writes, redirect character deltas strictly to secondary backup cache registers        },        onReset: () => {             // Re-allow primary transactional flush cycles to resume execution        }    );
4.3 Database Replication Lag Tolerances
Primary-to-Replica Lag Threshold: Maintained strictly below 2,500 milliseconds.
Lag Violation Safe-Route Rule: If analytical queries or leaderboard compilation cron jobs target a replica database displaying a replication sync delay exceeding 3,000 milliseconds, the load balancer dynamically kills the route pipeline, forcing lookups onto the primary cluster node to prevent stale data contamination.

--- Proceed with Module 35_ Cross-Platform Push Notifi.._.docx ---
MODULE 35: CROSS-PLATFORM PUSH NOTIFICATION ARCHITECTURE, REMOTE DEVICE TOKEN MANAGEMENT & SCHEDULED SYSTEM ALERTS
1. Unified Cross-Platform Notification Pipeline (FCM v1 & APNs HTTP/2)
To secure and stabilize messaging pipelines, server-authoritative push distribution utilizes the modern Firebase Cloud Messaging (FCM) HTTP v1 API authenticated via dynamic OAuth 2.0 Access Tokens (RS256 JWT generated from Service Accounts), bypassing deprecated legacy static server keys.
For direct Apple Push Notification service (APNs) communications, the backend maintains persistent HTTP/2 connection tunnels using token-based authentication (.p8 signing keys) to leverage multiplexed parallel streams per connection.
1.1 Cross-Platform FCM v1 Canonical Payload Contract
To target both Android and iOS instances simultaneously while enforcing platform-specific priority, sound profiles, and collapse configurations, payloads follow the highly structured FCM v1 payload protocol.
{  "message": {    "token": "fcm_registration_token_string_alpha_numeric_9931",    "notification": {      "title": "Your Smelter Is Cold!",      "body": "The active production queue in the Great Forge has stalled due to missing fuel."    },    "android": {      "priority": "HIGH",      "ttl": "86400s",      "notification": {        "channel_id": "village_alerts_high_priority",        "click_action": "TOP_NAV_DOCK_FORGE"      }    },    "apns": {      "headers": {        "apns-priority": "10",        "apns-expiration": "1783029600",        "apns-collapse-id": "forge_stalled_alert"      },      "payload": {        "aps": {          "alert": {            "title": "Your Smelter Is Cold!",            "body": "The active production queue in the Great Forge has stalled due to missing fuel."          },          "sound": "default",          "badge": 1,          "category": "FORGE_ACTION_CATEGORY"        }      }    },    "data": {      "redirection_target": "village_forge",      "timestamp_sent": "2026-07-01T22:30:00Z"    }  }}
2. Device Registration Token Life-Cycle & Pruning Matrix
Invalid or stale registration tokens introduce massive CPU fan-out penalties and network latency overhead. The server isolates and sanitizes registries inside the account_device_registry horizontal shards.
2.1 Stale Token Verification Protocol
Token Rotation: Clients submit their active device token on every single boot sequence validation check. If the token value mutates, the database marks the old registration record index dead instantly.
Canonical Error Evaluation: When the downstream FCM v1 gateway answers a batch dispatch request with specific platform fault descriptors (UNREGISTERED, INVALID_ARGUMENT), an asynchronous database worker triggers an immediate row purge sequence.
DELETE FROM account_device_registry WHERE registration_token = 'fcm_registration_token_string_alpha_numeric_9931'    OR last_sync_timestamp < NOW() - INTERVAL '30 days';
3. Asynchronous Scheduled Notification Dispatch Architecture
Idle games rely heavily on time-delayed alert scheduling (e.g., messaging a player exactly 8 hours from now when a structural crop finishes cultivation or a citizen's stamina engine finishes replenishment). To manage this at scale without consuming primary thread loops, scheduling uses an asynchronous sorting layout.
+---------------------------+       +-------------------------+       +---------------------------+| Active Action Engine      | ----> | Redis Sorted Set (ZSET) | ----> | Dispatch Worker Pods      || (Computes Completion Time)|       | (Scheduled Queue)       |       | (Pops due items, hits v1) |+---------------------------+       +-------------------------+       +---------------------------+
3.1 Redis ZSET Queue Scheduling Engine
The Score Map: Scheduled messages are pushed into a dedicated Redis Sorted Set (notifications:scheduled:queue). The sorting element score reflects the absolute unix epoch timestamp when the message must fire.
The Polling Worker Loop: High-speed stateless processing workers query the ZSET every 1.0 second using targeted ZRANGEBYSCORE boundary queries:
\text{Target Window Score Bounds: } 0 \le \text{Score} \le \text{Current\_Epoch\_Timestamp}
// High-efficiency background push notification processing worker looppublic async Task ProcessScheduledNotificationsAsync(IDatabase redisDb){    double currentEpoch = DateTimeOffset.UtcNow.ToUnixTimeSeconds();        // Atomically pull all due items up to the current timestamp    var dueTokens = await redisDb.SortedSetRangeByScoreAsync("notifications:scheduled:queue", 0, currentEpoch);        if (dueTokens.Length > 0)    {        foreach (var token in dueTokens)        {            // Remove item from queue to prevent multi-pod processing collisions            bool removed = await redisDb.SortedSetRemoveAsync("notifications:scheduled:queue", token);            if (removed)            {                // Deserialize payload and forward packet to downstream FCM v1 service                await EnqueueToFcmServicePipeline(token);            }        }    }}
3.2 Dynamic Scheduling Overwrites
If a player re-enters the active game client early and resolves an asset queue manually before the background countdown expires, the client triggers an HTTP POST request to /api/v1/notifications/cancel. The server intercepts this message and unlinks the corresponding payload string from the Redis ZSET database container using an O(\log N) deletion, preventing stale push notifications from firing.

--- Proceed with Module 36_ Asset Bundles, Unity Addre.._.docx ---
MODULE 36: ASSET BUNDLES, UNITY ADDRESSABLES CONTENT DELIVERY & DYNAMIC CLIENT PATCHING PIPELINES
1. Unity Addressables Architecture & Content Packing Strategy
To optimize initial app store binary downloads (restricting the baseline .apk/.ipa file size below the cellular deployment limits of 200 MB), Folk-Idle offloads all visual elements, high-fidelity audio tracks, and localized font arrays to an external asset-hosting server. The content delivery pipeline utilizes the Unity Addressable Asset System.
1.1 Content Group Segmentation & Compression Topology
Assets are categorized into strict functional groups based on their execution constraints and lifecycle behaviors:
Static Baseline Group: Essential startup configurations, boot splash canvases, and fundamental UI atlas textures required for the core layout engine.
Compression: Packed directly into the application build using LZ4 (Chunk-Based) compression to support rapid, low-overhead read speeds on main threads.
Dynamic Character Lineage Group: Gen 1-10 character models, genetic animation frames, skin variations, and evolutionary particle systems.
Compression: Stored remotely. Compressed via LZ4 to facilitate individual asset asset streaming without requiring the client to unpack massive multi-megabyte archive blocks into runtime memory.
Audio Atmosphere Group: Spatial music clips, looping interface ambience, and sound effects for rare event notifications.
Compression: Stored remotely. Configured for direct streaming raw data from disk to ensure zero memory footprint allocations on low-end device heaps.
2. Dynamic Over-The-Air (OTA) Client Patching Pipeline
Every boot sequence executes a server-authoritative handshake to verify content synchronization integrity. The client client layer queries the update lifecycle entirely via asynchronous non-allocating handle streams.
Download Remote Hash PointerBoot Frame 1-30The application requests the lightweight raw asset fingerprint file catalog.hash from the edge server. This check bypasses cached disk copies to guarantee immediate origin verification.
Evaluate Hash Mismatch DeltasBoot Frame 31-45The engine compares the freshly obtained string hash against the internal catalog hash stored inside the persistent device path. If the values are identical, the runtime system skips the network download sequence entirely and loads local assets.
Fetch Remote Manifest LedgerNetwork Transaction StepIf the hash keys differ, the client down-streams the complete catalog.json file. This ledger contains explicit explicit URL paths, sizes, and dependency mapping schemas for every modified remote Asset Bundle block.
Query Download Allocation SizesDisk IO VerificationThe system runs an explicit size calculation routine using Addressables.GetDownloadSizeAsync(). This metrics payload exposes the exact total download bundle size to the user interface layer.
Stream and Validate Content ChunksPayload Ingestion PhaseThe update engine opens parallel HTTP/2 streams using Addressables.DownloadDependenciesAsync(). Downloaded chunks undergo structural integrity passes using an integrated 128-bit CRC validation loop against the remote manifest specification.
Evict Stale Content CacheStorage Maintenance PhaseUpon successful validation of the new bundles, the system updates the local tracking index, releases memory locks on old assets, and deletes deprecated asset bundles from disk storage blocks to reclaim device storage space.
3. CDN Infrastructure & Content Delivery Caching Strategy
Remote asset structures are distributed globally via high-capacity cloud storage buckets backed by enterprise-grade Content Delivery Networks (CDNs) to minimize time-to-first-byte (TTFB) latency across regional player hubs.
3.1 Edge Cache-Control Header Configurations
To maximize edge-node retention efficiency while enforcing asset updates, files are processed using strict cache invalidation routing matrices:
                      +---------------------------------------+                      |       Client Content Request          |                      +---------------------------------------+                                          |                     +--------------------+--------------------+                     | /assets/*.bundle                        | /assets/catalog.hash                     v                                         v+---------------------------------------+   +---------------------------------------+| Cache Header: public, max-age=31536000|   | Cache Header: no-cache, no-store      || Execution: Permanent Immutable Blob   |   | Execution: Always Force Origin Check  |+---------------------------------------+   +---------------------------------------+
Asset Bundle Binaries (*.bundle): Filenames are permanently uniquely hashed at compilation time (e.g., characters_assets_a98f12b3c.bundle). They deploy with edge headers set to Cache-Control: public, max-age=31536000, immutable. This allows edge points to cache the files indefinitely, eliminating origin traffic hits during rapid player scaling.
Content Version Anchors (catalog.hash): Deployed using headers Cache-Control: no-cache, no-store, must-revalidate. This forces edge routing networks to check the central storage bucket on every single request, ensuring clients instantly discover newly pushed updates.
3.2 HTTP 206 Partial Content Resiliency
Network connection handshakes across mobile providers are inherently volatile. To protect heavy asset downloads from failing due to minor network drops, the CDN infrastructure strictly mandates HTTP 206 Partial Content support.
If a network pipe breaks mid-transaction during a 45 MB background asset sync, the client app reads the current file byte length off the local disk and passes an explicit byte-range constraint header on the subsequent retry connection:
Range: bytes=18432000-
The edge CDN answers by streaming only the remaining file fragments, avoiding redownloads and reducing cellular bandwidth consumption.

MODULE 37: LOCALIZATION ARCHITECTURE, DYNAMIC TEXT TOKEN INJECTIONS & RUNTIME FONT TEXTURE ATLAS GENERATION
1. High-Performance Localization Schema & Memory Lookup Architecture
To scale Folk-Idle across global markets without introducing memory performance penalties during heavy UI state updates, the localization pipeline bypasses raw string-keyed dictionaries (Dictionary<string, string>). String hashing causes structural string-comparison overhead and heap fragmentation during O(1) lookups. The localization framework instead maps localized lines to explicit 32-bit integer identifier fields (LocaleID).
1.1 Localized Data Assembly Database Schema
Language data sheets are packed into contiguous flat structural arrays within binary data blocks, loaded directly into unmanaged memory blocks during the client boot sequence.
LocaleID (Int32)
String Key (Reference Only)
English Target Value (en)
Czech Target Value (cs)
10001
ui_forge_title
The Great Forge
Velká Kovárna
10002
ui_gather_copper_gain
Gained {0} Copper Ore.
Získal jsi {0} měděné rudy.
10003
ui_err_gold_insufficient
Insufficient Gold Reserves.
Nedostatek zlatých rezerv.
1.2 Multi-Language Memory Registry Memory Allocation Model
The runtime system manages languages inside an un-nested, flat array string pool where lookups resolve directly via array pointer indices:
\text{Memory Target Address} = \text{Base String Pool Pointer} + (\text{LocaleID} \times \text{Fixed Offset Scaling Constant})
This system allows the client application to swap global interfaces instantaneously across languages by changing the Base Pointer reference address, demanding zero re-allocation or parsing passes.
2. Zero-Allocation Dynamic Text Token Injection Engine
Standard string composition operations (such as string.Format() or C# string interpolation $"") instantiate temporary string object wrappers onto the managed heap. In high-frequency text rendering zones—such as logs tracking continuous resource updates across 50 characters—standard concatenation causes massive garbage collection spikes.
2.1 Heap Garbage Projection Formula
Without allocation-free optimization, cumulative garbage mass scales exponentially over time relative to execution parameters:
M_{\text{alloc}} = N_{\text{updates}} \times \text{Size}_{\text{string\_object}}
2.2 TextMeshPro Direct Char Array Injection Script
Folk-Idle leverages TextMeshPro’s native unmanaged character array buffers via the SetText wrapper extension framework, passing numeric value streams directly to rendering shaders without creating temporary heap strings.
using UnityEngine;using TMPro;public class LocalizationTokenEngine : MonoBehaviour{    [SerializeField] private TextMeshProUGUI targetTextMeshField;        private char[] primaryTextCharBuffer = new char[256];    // Updates text with zero heap allocation: "Gained 1420 Copper Ore."    public void InjectNumericTokenIntoUI(int localizedValueParameter)    {        // "Gained " reference token (Pre-localized sequence lookup)        primaryTextCharBuffer[0] = 'G';        primaryTextCharBuffer[1] = 'a';        primaryTextCharBuffer[2] = 'i';        primaryTextCharBuffer[3] = 'n';        primaryTextCharBuffer[4] = 'e';        primaryTextCharBuffer[5] = 'd';        primaryTextCharBuffer[6] = ' ';        int currentBufferIndex = 7;                // Convert integer parameters directly into char blocks inside the buffer array        currentBufferIndex = ConvertIntegerToCharArray(localizedValueParameter, primaryTextCharBuffer, currentBufferIndex);        primaryTextCharBuffer[currentBufferIndex++] = ' ';        primaryTextCharBuffer[currentBufferIndex++] = 'O';        primaryTextCharBuffer[currentBufferIndex++] = 'r';        primaryTextCharBuffer[currentBufferIndex++] = 'e';        primaryTextCharBuffer[currentBufferIndex++] = '.';        // Direct injection of unmanaged data blocks into TMPro mesh generators        targetTextMeshField.SetText(primaryTextCharBuffer, 0, currentBufferIndex);    }    private int ConvertIntegerToCharArray(int value, char[] buffer, int startIndex)    {        if (value == 0)        {            buffer[startIndex] = '0';            return startIndex + 1;        }        int temporaryValue = value;        int digitCount = 0;                while (temporaryValue > 0)        {            digitCount++;            temporaryValue /= 10;        }        int writeIndex = startIndex + digitCount;        temporaryValue = value;        while (temporaryValue > 0)        {            writeIndex--;            buffer[writeIndex] = (char)('0' + (temporaryValue % 10));            temporaryValue /= 10;        }        return startIndex + digitCount;    }}
3. TextMeshPro Runtime Font Texture Atlas Generation
Supporting Extended Latin, Cyrillic, and CJK (Chinese, Japanese, Korean) glyph matrices within a single pre-baked font texture atlas demands massive texture footprints (e.g., static 4K or 8K textures consuming up to 64 MB of uncompressed VRAM). To optimize mobile video memory limits, Folk-Idle implements TextMeshPro Dynamic Font Atlas pipelines.
3.1 Dynamic Font Configuration Topologies
The font system initializes with a minimal texture size, generating character glyph distance fields dynamically at runtime as they appear in the localized interface viewports.
Baseline Texture Asset Properties:
Initial Resolution Matrix: 1024x1024 pixels.
Render Frame Mode: SDFAA (Signed Distance Field Anti-Aliased High Quality).
Point Size Sampling Boundary: 36 Pt.
Glyph Padding Parameter Bounds: 9 Pixels (Prevents cross-texture sub-pixel bleed during high-scale interpolation transforms).
3.2 Dynamic Texture Atlas Calculation Model
The memory footprint of the dynamic atlas texture is tightly bounded by a fixed dimensional limit:
\text{VRAM}_{\text{bytes}} = \text{Width}_{\text{pixels}} \times \text{Height}_{\text{pixels}} \times \text{Bytes Per Pixel}
For an uncompressed 8-bit Alpha channel SDF atlas (1024 \times 1024 \times 1), the memory usage remains locked at exactly 1.048 MB, regardless of the total number of characters supported across the global localization sheets.
3.3 Glyph Eviction & Rebuild Fail-Safe Routine
When a player navigates to long chat segments containing diverse CJK character inputs, the dynamic 1024x1024 texture atlas can encounter pixel capacity exhaustion. Rather than dropping characters or causing text corruption, the asset engine intercepts texture allocation failures through an automated eviction fallback system:
+-------------------------------------------+| Atlas Texture Capacity Exception Triggered |+-------------------------------------------+                      |                      v+-------------------------------------------+| Flush Complete Active Glyph Matrix Clear  |+-------------------------------------------+                      |                      v+-------------------------------------------+| Scan and Collect Characters Visible       || on the Active Viewport Frame Layers       |+-------------------------------------------+                      |                      v+-------------------------------------------+| Re-render Validated Character Blocks Only || into the Regenerated Clean Atlas Surface  |+-------------------------------------------+
This recovery process ensures that the dynamic font texture never balloons into larger VRAM profiles, maintaining a highly optimized memory footprint on low-spec mobile target chipsets.

MODULE 38: MOBILE THERMAL MANAGEMENT, FRAME-RATE THROTTLING & HARDWARE BATTERY OPTIMIZATION FRAMEWORKS
1. Adaptive Refresh Rate Systems & Game State Throttling
Folk-Idle is an automated idle experience meant to remain active on a user’s mobile screen for hours at a time. Running at a constant 60 or 120 frames per second (FPS) during passive automation states causes rapid battery depletion, overheating, and CPU hardware degradation. The execution layer enforces a dynamic state-driven frame throttling framework.
1.1 State-Driven Frame Target Matrix
The engine shifts its execution constraints by analyzing client interaction vectors and hardware state flags.
F_{\text{target}}(S, T) = \begin{cases} 60 & \text{if } S = \text{ActiveUIInteraction} \land T < T_{\text{critical}} \\ 30 & \text{if } S = \text{PassiveGridSimulation} \land T < T_{\text{critical}} \\ 15 & \text{if } S = \text{BackgroundDeepIdle} \lor T \ge T_{\text{critical}} \\ 5 & \text{if } S = \text{ScreenDimmedAutomation} \lor T \ge T_{\text{fatal}} \end{cases}
Where:
S is the client interface operational state mode.
T is the physical device temperature tracking register.
1.2 State Transition Allocation Table
Runtime System State

2. Platform Thermal API Integration & Hardware Callback Handlers
The client application queries underlying operating system kernels via native bridge plugins (Android ThermalStatus Listener API and iOS NSProcessInfo ThermalState Notifications) to intercept thermal saturation vectors before hardware-level downclocking occurs.
2.1 Cross-Platform Thermal Protection Broker Blueprint
using UnityEngine;using System;public class MobileThermalOptimizationBroker : MonoBehaviour{    private int regularTargetFrameRate = 60;        void Awake()    {        // Bind platform-specific native operating system thermal warnings        #if UNITY_ANDROID && !UNITY_EDITOR        AndroidThermalCallbackRelay.OnThermalStatusChanged += HandleAndroidThermalMutation;        #elif UNITY_IOS && !UNITY_EDITOR        IOSThermalCallbackRelay.OnThermalStateChanged += HandleIOSThermalMutation;        #endif    }    private void HandleAndroidThermalMutation(int thermalStatusSeverityIndex)    {        // Android Thermal Status mapping index configurations:        // 0 = NONE, 1 = LIGHT, 2 = MODERATE, 3 = SEVERE, 4 = CRITICAL, 5 = EMERGENCY, 6 = SHUTDOWN        switch (thermalStatusSeverityIndex)        {            case 0:            case 1:                Application.targetFrameRate = regularTargetFrameRate;                QualitySettings.vSyncCount = 0;                break;            case 2:                Application.targetFrameRate = 30; // Initiate safety frame drop                break;            case 3:            case 4:                Application.targetFrameRate = 15; // Force severe rendering limits                DisableVolatileVisualParticleEmitters();                break;            default:                Application.targetFrameRate = 5; // Emergency power containment mode                ForceDeepPowerSaveScreenOverlay();                break;        }    }    private void DisableVolatileVisualParticleEmitters()    {        // Disables background rendering passes for atmospheric sprites and UI glow shaders        Shader.DisableKeyword("_HIGH_QUALITY_BLOOM_ON");        QualitySettings.shadows = ShadowQuality.Disable;    }    private void ForceDeepPowerSaveScreenOverlay()    {        // Enforces black canvas alpha overlay to dim pixel power consumption on OLED panels        PowerSaveOverlayController.Instance.ActivateEmergencyScreenDimmerCanvas();    }}
3. GPU Shader & Battery Draw Minimization Framework
When the client determines the application is operating inside a low-interaction background simulation window, it modifies global Unity rendering passes to lower system draw calls and protect hardware longevity.
3.1 Frame Discard and Canvas Deactivation Engine
When shifting down into the ScreenDimmedAutomation tier (5 FPS mode), the engine bypasses standard multi-pass geometry processing.
Canvas Disassembly: The main high-frequency rendering canvas elements are completely unlinked from the camera viewport matrix (canvasInstance.enabled = false).
Frame Render Skips: The application forces the primary camera component to execute a complete layout skip, processing exclusively the core mathematical ticks via C# worker coroutines while outputting an entirely flat, un-shaded static pixel surface to the hardware frame buffers.
3.2 Dynamic Resolution Scalar Modification
To limit mobile GPU power draw, the platform dynamically scales down the render target resolution when battery levels (B) drop below established safety corridors.
\text{Screen Scale Factor} = \begin{cases} 1.0 & \text{if } B \ge 0.50 \\ 0.75 & \text{if } 0.20 \le B < 0.50 \\ 0.50 & \text{if } B < 0.20 \end{cases}
// Modifies internal render texture allocation bounds based on battery telemetry parameterspublic void OptimizeGPUScalerViaBatteryStatus(float baselineBatteryPercentValue){    if (baselineBatteryPercentValue < 0.20f)    {        // Downscale rendering buffer resolution to 50% of native device constraints        ScalableBufferManager.ResizeBuffers(0.50f, 0.50f);    }    else if (baselineBatteryPercentValue < 0.50f)    {        ScalableBufferManager.ResizeBuffers(0.75f, 0.75f);    }    else    {        ScalableBufferManager.ResizeBuffers(1.00f, 1.00f);    }}
By dropping resolution metrics linearly, mobile devices bypass typical thermal runtime traps, securing continuous background farming uptime without system stability issues.
