MODULE 40: GUILD TRADE DEPOTS, PEER-TO-PEER ECONOMIES & FRAUD PREVENTION MATRIX
1. Guild Trade Depot Architecture & Order Book System
To support player interaction without enabling hyperinflation or real-money trading (RMT) channels, trade is channeled through localized Guild Trade Depots. These depots operate as a server-authoritative asynchronous marketplace restricted by guild membership duration and localized item verification rules.
1.1 Guild Trade Depot Listing Ledger Schema
The marketplace structure avoids direct player-to-player trade prompts. Instead, it processes transactions via an item order book to verify the custody of assets before altering database values.
CREATE TABLE guild_trade_listings (    listing_id BIGSERIAL PRIMARY KEY,    guild_id UUID NOT NULL,    seller_account_id UUID NOT NULL,    buyer_account_id UUID,    item_base_id VARCHAR(64) NOT NULL,    item_quantity INT NOT NULL CHECK (item_quantity > 0),    unit_price_gold INT NOT NULL CHECK (unit_price_gold > 0),    listing_status VARCHAR(16) DEFAULT 'ACTIVE' NOT NULL, -- 'ACTIVE', 'COMPLETED', 'CANCELLED'    created_at TIMESTAMP WITH TIME ZONE DEFAULT NOW() NOT NULL,    resolved_at TIMESTAMP WITH TIME ZONE,    CONSTRAINT chk_listing_lifecycle CHECK (        (listing_status = 'ACTIVE' AND buyer_account_id IS NULL AND resolved_at IS NULL) OR        (listing_status IN ('COMPLETED', 'CANCELLED') AND resolved_at IS NOT NULL)    ));CREATE INDEX idx_guild_trade_active_orders ON guild_trade_listings (guild_id, listing_status, item_base_id);
2. Dynamic Price Collar & Algorithmic Market Controls
To block exploit vectors where bot networks pass millions in gold to clean accounts via low-value dummy items, the system applies server-enforced price corridors. The edge pricing engine tracks a rolling 7-day average price vector (P_{\text{avg}}) for all stackable materials and item classifications.
2.1 Price Bound Constraint Equation
The server rejects trade creation transactions if the user's targeted unit price deviates outside the algorithmic price collar boundaries:
P_{\text{min}} = \max(1, P_{\text{avg}} \times (1 - \delta)) P_{\text{max}} = P_{\text{avg}} \times (1 + \delta)
Where:
P_{\text{avg}} represents the dynamically computed rolling global market average valuation metric.
\delta represents the system configuration volatility tolerance coefficient, hard-locked at exactly 0.20 (20\%).
2.2 Market Liquidity Flattening Tax Matrix
Trades are subject to an immediate silver-sink taxation bracket designed to wipe excess liquidity from old profiles. The tax percentage scales dynamically relative to the seller's total accumulated net wealth.

W_{\text{delta}} = \frac{\text{AccountWealth}_{\text{Highest}}}{\max(1, \text{AccountWealth}_{\text{Lowest}})}
If W_{\text{delta}} > 50.0 and the trade involves high-frequency resource stacks sold at maximum price collar limits (P_{\text{max}}), the logging layer triggers an economic flag event packet.

4. Atomic Multi-Shard Trade Settlement Engine
To prevent item duplication bugs during high-concurrency order attempts across separate regional backend database shards, matching transactions use an explicitly sequenced atomic routine.
// Authoritative trade execution routine enforcing multi-entity balance isolationpublic class GuildDepotSettlementEngine{    private readonly IDatabaseContext dbContext;    public async Task<bool> ExecuteOrderSettlementAsync(long activeListingId, Guid purchasingUserUuid)    {        // Enforce isolation level serialized to completely lock reading row states during validation        using (var dbTransaction = await dbContext.Database.BeginTransactionAsync(System.Data.IsolationLevel.Serializable))        {            try            {                var listing = await dbContext.GuildListings.LockRowForUpdate().FirstOrDefaultAsync(l => l.ListingId == activeListingId);                if (listing == null || listing.ListingStatus != "ACTIVE")                {                    await dbTransaction.RollbackAsync();                    return false; // Listing already claimed or invalid                }                var buyerProfile = await dbContext.AccountBalances.LockRowForUpdate().FirstOrDefaultAsync(b => b.AccountId == purchasingUserUuid);                int totalCostCalculated = listing.Unit減PriceGold * listing.ItemQuantity;                if (buyerProfile == null || buyerProfile.CurrentGold < totalCostCalculated)                {                    await dbTransaction.RollbackAsync();                    return false; // Insufficient buyer financial assets                }                // Compute tax deductions                double globalTaxScalar = buyerProfile.CurrentGold > 5000000 ? 0.15 : 0.05;                int goldBurned = (int)(totalCostCalculated * globalTaxScalar);                int netSellerPayout = totalCostCalculated - goldBurned;                // Execute monetary balances mutation                buyerProfile.CurrentGold -= totalCostCalculated;                                var sellerProfile = await dbContext.AccountBalances.LockRowForUpdate().FirstOrDefaultAsync(b => b.AccountId == listing.SellerAccountId);                if (sellerProfile != null)                {                    sellerProfile.CurrentGold += netSellerPayout;                }                // Update ledger row configuration state to close order pipeline                listing.BuyerAccountId = purchasingUserUuid;                listing.ListingStatus = "COMPLETED";                listing.ResolvedAt = DateTimeOffset.UtcNow;                await dbContext.SaveChangesAsync();                await dbTransaction.CommitAsync();                return true;            }            catch (Exception)            {                await dbTransaction.RollbackAsync();                throw;            }        }    }}

2. The Seasonal-to-Legacy Conversion Function
To ensure that high-velocity seasonal grinding feels rewarding, player achievements map directly into a persistent currency token: Legacy Shards (S_{\text{legacy}}). The volume of distributed shards is calculated at the moment of season termination using a multi-variable calculation routine.
The server calculates legacy shard rewards via the following formula:
S_{\text{legacy}} = \lfloor \alpha \cdot \log_{10}(G_{\text{total}} + 1) + \beta \cdot \sum_{i=1}^{C} (L_i)^2 + \gamma \cdot I_{\text{score}} \rfloor
Where:
G_{\text{total}} represents the absolute accumulated Gold volume held within the seasonal village coffer at the exact termination epoch timestamp.
L_i represents the end-of-season level achieved by character index i within the player's active 50-character population matrix (C).
I_{\text{score}} represents the holistic inventory quality coefficient derived from the combined item item tiers.
\alpha, \beta, \gamma represent structural tuning constants configured in the Remote Configuration profile to manage global legacy reward balancing (\alpha = 12.5, \beta = 0.05, \gamma = 1.50).
3. Server-Authoritative Database Era Transition Procedure
The seasonal transition executes via an automated database script. This operation isolates active account data rows, copies structural data sets to historical leaderboard tables, purges transient state trackers, and mints legacy rewards.
BEGIN;-- Step 1: Log an immutable historical snapshot of the top seasonal rankingsINSERT INTO historical_leaderboard_archives (season_era_id, account_id, combined_mastery_score, final_ranking_placement)SELECT 'era_03_2026', account_id, total_mastery_xp, RANK() OVER (ORDER BY total_mastery_xp DESC)FROM account_seasonal_progressWHERE active_season_id = 'era_03_2026';-- Step 2: Extract asset parameters and execute the Legacy Shard allocation functionUPDATE account_permanent_registry prSET legacy_shards_balance = pr.legacy_shards_balance + sub.calculated_shardsFROM (    SELECT         account_id,        FLOOR(12.5 * LOG(village_gold + 1) + 0.05 * character_level_sum_squared) AS calculated_shards    FROM account_seasonal_progress    WHERE active_season_id = 'era_03_2026') subWHERE pr.account_id = sub.account_id;-- Step 3: Clear the volatile item tables linked to the expired seasonDELETE FROM items WHERE account_id IN (SELECT account_id FROM account_seasonal_progress WHERE active_season_id = 'era_03_2026');-- Step 4: Reset character skill progression and attribute rows to baseline statesUPDATE character_skillsSET current_level = 1, accumulated_xp = 0WHERE character_id IN (SELECT character_id FROM characters WHERE active_season_id = 'era_03_2026');-- Step 5: Mutate the account state flag to prompt mandatory initialization upon subsequent user boot sequencesUPDATE account_security_registrySET account_status_flag = 'Seasonal_Initialization_Required'WHERE account_id IN (SELECT account_id FROM account_seasonal_progress WHERE active_season_id = 'era_03_2026');COMMIT;

--- Proceed with Module 44_ Dynamic Memory Asset Garba.._.docx ---
MODULE 44: DYNAMIC MEMORY ASSET GARBAGE COLLECTION PIPELINES & UNMANAGED HEAP LAYOUTS WITHIN UNITY
1. Unity Incremental Garbage Collection Configuration & Frame Budget Throttling
Unity utilizes a non-generational, incremental Boehm-Demers-Weiser garbage collector. In highly dense simulation environments like Folk-Idle—where continuous background math operations run across dozens of character rows—unmanaged spikes in managed heap allocations trigger immediate frame-rate stuttering when the garbage collector forces a stop-the-world phase.
1.1 Incremental GC Frame Time Slice Equation
To ensure a continuous 60 FPS execution floor (16.66\text{ ms} target frame time), the execution layer caps the garbage collection execution slice (T_{\text{slice}}) using an absolute margin budget allocation formula:
T_{\text{slice}} \le T_{\text{target}} - (T_{\text{render}} + T_{\text{simulation}} + T_{\text{input}})
Where:
T_{\text{target}} = 16.66\text{ ms}.
T_{\text{render}} represents the CPU overhead required to issue GPU draw calls and process mesh batches.
T_{\text{simulation}} represents the core multi-slot mechanical calculation tick overhead.
If the baseline rendering and simulation tasks occupy 12.0\text{ ms} of a given frame window, the maximum permissible time slice assigned to incremental garbage collection scanning must never exceed exactly 4.66\text{ ms}. If GC operations exceed this value, the collector suspends its traversal tree operation and resumes on the subsequent frame index, keeping frame delivery smooth.
1.2 Programmatic GC Control & Allocation Auditing
During high-intensity interface operations (e.g., initial scene loading sequences or processing bulk item conversions inside the Forge), the engine programmatically forces garbage collection behavior to clear the managed heap during idle windows.
using UnityEngine;using UnityEngine.Scripting;public class GarbageCollectionThrottler : MonoBehaviour{    void Awake()    {        // Enforce incremental garbage collection behaviors at the global application layer        GarbageCollector.GCMode = GarbageCollector.Mode.Enabled;    }    public static void TriggerSystemSanitizationFreeze()    {        // Force an immediate synchronous garbage collection pass strictly during controlled windows        long memoryBeforeBites = System.GC.GetTotalMemory(false);                System.GC.Collect(System.GC.MaxGeneration, System.GCCollectionMode.Forced, true, true);                long memoryAfterBytes = System.GC.GetTotalMemory(false);        Debug.Log($"System Sanitization Complete. Reclaimed: {(memoryBeforeBites - memoryAfterBytes) / 1024.0f} KB");    }}
2. Unmanaged Native Heap Layouts & Native Collection Matrices
To eliminate garbage collection scanning overhead during intensive 10 Hz character calculation passes, the simulation engine shifts data matrices out of the C# managed heap entirely. By processing data inside the native unmanaged C++ heap layer via the Unity Collections package, memory avoids the GC traversal footprint.
2.1 Unmanaged Native Simulation Buffer Script
The system wraps native memory blocks in structure layouts (struct) to process character attribute mutations without allocating reference tracking records.
using System;using Unity.Collections;using Unity.Collections.LowLevel.Unsafe;public struct CharacterStatDataBlock{    public int CharacterId;    public int CurrentLevel;    public int AttackPower;    public float ActionSpeedModifier;}public class UnmanagedSimulationEngine : IDisposable{    // Allocates memory directly onto the unmanaged native C++ heap    private NativeArray<CharacterStatDataBlock> populationProcessingBuffer;    private bool isDisposed;    public UnmanagedSimulationEngine(int populationCapacity)    {        // Allocator.Persistent ensures memory remains locked and stable across frames indefinitely        populationProcessingBuffer = new NativeArray<CharacterStatDataBlock>(            populationCapacity,             Allocator.Persistent,             NativeArrayOptions.ClearMemory        );        isDisposed = false;    }    public void ExecuteHighSpeedBatchProcessing(float timeDeltaConstant)    {        if (isDisposed) throw new ObjectDisposedException("Buffer has been safely unlinked from native memory.");        // Loop execution runs inside unmanaged memory boundaries with zero managed heap object creation        for (int i = 0; i < populationProcessingBuffer.Length; i++)        {            CharacterStatDataBlock currentCharacter = populationProcessingBuffer[i];                        // Execute mechanical calculations inside structural memory boundaries            float effectiveTickStep = timeDeltaConstant * currentCharacter.ActionSpeedModifier;                        // Re-write data value modifications back into the exact native memory register address            populationProcessingBuffer[i] = currentCharacter;        }    }    public void Dispose()    {        if (!isDisposed)        {            // Explicitly deallocate unmanaged native heap arrays to prevent memory leaks            if (populationProcessingBuffer.IsCreated)            {                populationProcessingBuffer.Dispose();            }            isDisposed = true;        }    }}

When long gaming sessions stream dynamic content (such as swapping multi-generation character art variations or unloading alternate UI layouts), memory leaks will manifest if Addressable handle reference counts fail to clear cleanly.

3.2 Asynchronous Handle Release and Unloading Pipeline
When a user closes a heavy UI window (e.g., exiting the Breeding Incubation Chamber and returning to the minimal core view), an explicit garbage collection asset sweep triggers to release memory locks.
using UnityEngine;using UnityEngine.AddressableAssets;using UnityEngine.ResourceManagement.AsyncOperations;using System.Collections.Generic;public class AssetLifecycleAutomationEngine : MonoBehaviour{    private List<AsyncOperationHandle> activeInstantiationHandlesPool = new List<AsyncOperationHandle>();    public void TrackLoadedAssetHandle(AsyncOperationHandle trackingHandle)    {        activeInstantiationHandlesPool.Add(trackingHandle);    }    public void ExecuteFullContextUnloadSequence()    {        // Step 1: Enforce reverse loop iteration to safely unlink handles from the active pool        for (int i = activeInstantiationHandlesPool.Count - 1; i >= 0; i--)        {            AsyncOperationHandle targetHandle = activeInstantiationHandlesPool[i];                        if (targetHandle.IsValid())            {                // Decrement the Addressables system internal reference counter registry                Addressables.Release(targetHandle);            }        }                activeInstantiationHandlesPool.Clear();        // Step 2: Flush unused asset bundle dependencies from native GPU memory regions instantly        AsyncOperationHandle<long> clearCacheOperation = Addressables.ClearDependencyCacheAsync(activeInstantiationHandlesPool, true);        clearCacheOperation.Completed += (op) =>        {            // Force an immediate asset resource collection sweep across all dead references            Resources.UnloadUnusedAssets();        };    }}
By maintaining a clear dividing line between managed and unmanaged data structures, Folk-Idle prevents memory fragmentation and stays well within the strict memory constraints required for continuous multi-hour mobile background farming operations.

--- Proceed with Module 45_ Secure Client-Server Hands.._.docx ---
MODULE 45: SECURE CLIENT-SERVER HANDSHAKE PROTOCOLS, CRYPTOGRAPHIC SESSION TOKEN RENEWAL & RECONNECTION STATE MACHINES
1. Secure Client-Server Handshake Protocol
To prevent man-in-the-middle (MITM) session hijacking, packet sniffing, and unauthorized api replay injection loops, the initial WebSocket connection executes a server-authoritative cryptographic handshake. This process leverages an Elliptic Curve Diffie-Hellman (ECDH) key exchange over the P-256 curve to establish an ephemeral symmetric shared secret key used for encrypting sub-protocol payloads via AES-256-GCM.
Client Device                                              Stateless API Gateway     |                                                               |     | --- [1. HTTP GET Upgrade Request + Client Ephemeral Public Key] -> |     |                                                               |     | <-- [2. HTTP 101 Switching Protocols + Server Public Key + Signature] - |     |                                                               |     | ===== [3. Ephemeral Shared Secret Derived via ECDH-P256] =====|     |                                                               |     | === [4. Secure Binary Frame Transmission via AES-256-GCM] === |
1.1 Handshake Signature Validation Ledger
The server validates the initial handshake parameters by evaluating a cryptographic binding signature derived from the user’s authenticated identity provider token (Module 29). The server signs its handshake response using a private Ed25519 signing key, which the client verifies using a hardcoded public pinning master key.
2. Cryptographic Session Token Renewal Core Architecture
Authentication uses a two-tier token topology: a short-lived JSON Web Token (JWT Access Token) and a long-lived, cryptographically isolated Refresh Token stored securely within device storage sandboxes (EncryptedPlayerPrefs / Keychain).
2.1 Access Token JWT Payload Configuration Structure
{  "protectedHeader": {    "alg": "RS256",    "typ": "JWT",    "kid": "prod_gate_key_2026_v1"  },  "tokenClaimsPayload": {    "iss": "auth.folkidle.game",    "sub": "9b1deb4d-3b7d-4bad-9bdd-2b0d7b3dcb6d",    "aud": "compute.folkidle.game",    "exp": 1783021800,    "iat": 1783020900,    "jti": "a82b3c4d-9e0f-4112-b3a1-112233445566",    "scopes": ["simulation_read", "action_write", "guild_chat"]  }}
Lifespan Window: Access tokens expire exactly 15 minutes (900 seconds) after generation.
Sliding Window Refresh Processing: The client automatically issues an asynchronous token renewal request when the access token's remaining validity drops below 3 minutes, executing an absolute atomic swap via the server's refresh validation controller.
2.2 Server-Authoritative Token Swapping Engine (C# API Controller)
using System;using System.Threading.Tasks;using Microsoft.AspNetCore.Mvc;[ApiController][Route("api/v1/auth")]public class TokenRenewalController : ControllerBase{    private readonly ITokenVerificationProvider tokenEngine;    private readonly ISecureDistributedCache sessionCache;    [HttpPost("refresh-token-swap")]    public async Task<IActionResult> ExecuteSecureTokenSwap([FromBody] TokenSwapRequest payload)    {        // Step 1: Decode and validate structural signature properties of the expired access token        var principalClaimGroup = tokenEngine.ExtractPrincipalClaimsWithoutExpiryCheck(payload.ExpiredAccessToken);        var accountIdClaim = principalClaimGroup.FindFirst("sub")?.Value;        if (string.IsNullOrEmpty(accountIdClaim)) return Forbid("Malformed authentication claim payload mapping.");        // Step 2: Fetch and evaluate the matching Refresh Token signature inside Redis cache layers        string cachedSessionKey = $"auth:refresh_token:{accountIdClaim}";        string activeValidTokenHash = await sessionCache.GetStringAsync(cachedSessionKey);        if (string.IsNullOrEmpty(activeValidTokenHash) || activeValidTokenHash != CryptographicHasher.ComputeSha256(payload.RawRefreshToken))        {            // Revoke current session flags to block cascade replay intrusion vectors            await sessionCache.RemoveAsync(cachedSessionKey);            return Unauthorized("Invalid or compromised refresh token signature submitted.");        }        // Step 3: Spin up a completely unique token identifier to guarantee absolute multi-access prevention        string structuralNewJti = Guid.NewGuid().ToString();        var concreteNewTokens = tokenEngine.GenerateTokenPair(accountIdClaim, structuralNewJti);        // Overwrite the cache layer with the new token hash parameter using a sliding window expiration        await sessionCache.SetStringAsync(cachedSessionKey, CryptographicHasher.ComputeSha256(concreteNewTokens.RefreshToken), TimeSpan.FromDays(7));        return Ok(new TokenSwapResponse        {            NewAccessToken = concreteNewTokens.AccessToken,            NewRefreshToken = concreteNewTokens.RefreshToken,            ExpiresInSeconds = 900        });    }}

Mobile network connections are highly volatile. To prevent data corruption or dropping character loop cycles when transitioning between Wi-Fi routers and cellular antennas, the client runs an isolated Reconnection Finite State Machine (FSM).

3.2 Cryptographic Reconnection and State Recovery Loop
When the connection breaks, the client uses an automated recovery routine to reconnect securely without forcing a full client reload.
Transition to Heartbeat Missing StateTrigger ModeThe client engine intercepts a WebSocket frame drop. The UI blocks interactions instantly, rendering a modal blocker to shield the system state.
Compute Exponential Backoff DelayMathematical BackoffThe network thread calculates the exact sleep duration for the retry attempt using a randomized exponential equation to prevent server thundering herd collisions:
Execute Target Access Token ValidationCryptographic SweepThe engine checks if the cached JWT access token is valid. If it has expired, the client routes a token swap request through the HTTP gateway to refresh the token before attempting to reconnect to the socket.

By binding connection lifecycles to this automated state engine, Folk-Idle handles intermittent connection drops transparently. It maintains state synchronization while protecting the server architecture from high-frequency retry attacks.

--- Proceed with Module 46_ Dedicated WebSocket Heartb.._.docx ---
MODULE 46: DEDICATED WEBSOCKET HEARTBEAT METRICS, PING/PONG FRAMES & NETWORK JITTER OPTIMIZATION FILTERS
1. Server-Authoritative Ping/Pong Heartbeat Protocol
To maintain long-running socket connections through aggressive carrier-grade NAT (CGNAT) gateways, mobile firewalls, and proxy networks—which frequently sever silent TCP pipelines after 30 to 60 seconds of inactivity—the infrastructure implements a low-overhead connection auditing engine.
The mechanism bypasses heavy application-layer JSON payloads, relying instead on raw WebSocket opcode control frames to minimize serialization costs and CPU wake-cycles on the client device.
Server Gateway Node                                            Client Device Terminal        |                                                                 |        | --- [ Control Frame: 0x09 (Ping) + 4-Byte Epoch Payload ] ----> |        |                                                                 |        | <--- [ Control Frame: 0x0A (Pong) + Echoed 4-Byte Payload ] --- |        |                                                                 |        | =================== [ Verify Evaluation Window ] ============== |
Transmission Interval: The server gateway pushes a native 0x09 (Ping) control frame every 15 seconds to all connected sockets.
Client Dead-Line Verification Window: The client runtime intercepts the opcode at the native driver boundary and immediately echoes back a matching 0x0A (Pong) frame carrying identical payload bytes. The client must return this frame within an absolute 5-second response window.
Eviction Guard: If the server fails to capture the corresponding 0x0A frame before the deadline expires, it flags the socket as dropped, immediately tears down the TCP allocation pool, and shifts the user session into the Heartbeat_Missing recovery state (Module 45).
2. Algorithmic Network Jitter & Latency Smoothing Engine
Raw Round-Trip Time (RTT) measurements on cellular data networks fluctuate violently during tower transitions, signal degradation, or packet bufferbloat. Feeding raw, un-filtered network metrics directly into client-side interpolation routines leads to severe visual rubber-banding and erratic system updates.
The client engine processes incoming timing deltas using an Exponential Moving Average (EMA) combined with a statistical variance filter to track true connection stability.
2.1 Smoothed Latency Tracking Formula
The filtered network latency metric (RTT_{\text{smoothed}}) updates upon every successful Pong frame confirmation loop:
RTT_{\text{smoothed}, t} = \alpha \cdot RTT_t + (1 - \alpha) \cdot RTT_{\text{smoothed}, t-1}
Where \alpha represents the historical weight dampening coefficient, hard-locked at exactly 0.125 (1/8) to prioritize long-term trends over isolated packet anomalies.
2.2 Network Jitter Statistical Variance Formula
Network Jitter (J) is defined as the statistical variance between consecutive latency samples. It is computed continuously using an independent tracking loop:
J_t = J_{t-1} + \left( |RTT_t - RTT_{t-1}| - J_{t-1} \right) \cdot \beta
Where \beta represents the jitter calculation scaling factor, configured at exactly 0.250 (1/4).
3. Dynamic Network Classification Matrix
The engine maps the calculated RTT_{\text{smoothed}} and J_t vectors into distinct operational network profile tiers. This classification dynamically tunes the game's network sync behaviors:
Connection Quality Profile Tier
RTT_{\text{smoothed}} Horizon Bounds
J_t Variance Thresholds
Client Input Buffer Adjustments

\le 50\text{ ms}
\le 5\text{ ms}

> 75\text{ ms}

4. Unmanaged Jitter Processing Pipeline
To maximize thread efficiency, the network filtering calculations run inside the client's unmanaged background network worker loop, bypassing the Unity main thread and avoiding managed heap overhead.
using System;using System.Runtime.InteropServices;[StructLayout(LayoutKind.Sequential)]public struct NetworkQualityMetricsBlock{    public double SmoothedRttSeconds;    public double CurrentJitterSeconds;    public double LastRawRttSeconds;    public uint TotalProcessedHeartbeats;}public static class NetworkJitterOptimizationFilter{    private const double AlphaScalingWeight = 0.125;    private const double BetaScalingWeight = 0.250;    // Executes calculation logic using raw pointers to eliminate marshaling and heap allocations    public static unsafe void IngestHeartbeatSample(NetworkQualityMetricsBlock* metricsBuffer, double sampledRttSeconds)    {        if (metricsBuffer == null) return;        if (metricsBuffer->TotalProcessedHeartbeats == 0)        {            // Establish baseline values on the initial connection handshake frame            metricsBuffer->SmoothedRttSeconds = sampledRttSeconds;            metricsBuffer->CurrentJitterSeconds = 0.0;        }        else        {            // Execute the historical Exponential Moving Average (EMA) smoothing evaluation loop            double doubleRttDelta = sampledRttSeconds - metricsBuffer->LastRawRttSeconds;            double absoluteDeltaValue = doubleRttDelta < 0 ? -doubleRttDelta : doubleRttDelta;            // Update statistical variance data parameters            metricsBuffer->CurrentJitterSeconds += (absoluteDeltaValue - metricsBuffer->CurrentJitterSeconds) * BetaScalingWeight;            metricsBuffer->SmoothedRttSeconds += (sampledRttSeconds - metricsBuffer->SmoothedRttSeconds) * AlphaScalingWeight;        }        metricsBuffer->LastRawRttSeconds = sampledRttSeconds;        metricsBuffer->TotalProcessedHeartbeats++;    }}
When connection quality slips down to Tier Gamma or Tier Omega, the simulation engine automatically delays immediate transaction dispatches to the API pods. Instead, it aggregates action packets into structured batches. This reduces network packet density, lowers the risk of dropped frames, and prevents state sync desynchronization during periods of poor network stability.

--- Proceed with Module 47_ Client-Side Predictive Vis.._.docx ---
MODULE 47: CLIENT-SIDE PREDICTIVE VISUAL SIMULATION MATCHING, STATE EXTRAPOLATION MODELS & VISUAL SNAP-CORRECTION SIEVES
1. Client-Side Visual Prediction Architecture
To ensure immediate visual feedback in high-latency mobile networks, the client interface cannot wait for a round-trip server confirmation before advancing progress metrics. The client UI layer operates an independent, predictive simulation engine that advances state parameters locally in synchronization with predicted server clocks.
1.1 Local Visual State Projection Formula
Let S_{\text{client}}(t) represent the predicted visual state vector (e.g., progress bar percentage, accumulated experience fill, or health pool remaining) rendering at time t. It is derived from the last authoritative server state checkpoint S_{\text{server}}(t_0) received at timestamp t_0:
S_{\text{client}}(t) = S_{\text{server}}(t_0) + \int_{t_0}^{t} R_{\text{sim}}(\tau) \cdot \Phi_{\text{net}}(\tau) \, d\tau
Where:
R_{\text{sim}}(\tau) represents the localized simulation tick rate coefficient (e.g., resource generation velocity per second).
\Phi_{\text{net}}(\tau) represents the dynamic network performance scaling scalar derived from the active jitter optimization filters (Module 46).
2. State Extrapolation and Dead Reckoning under Network Jitter
When network connection quality degrades to Tier Gamma or Tier Omega, authoritative state packets fail to arrive within the established 100 ms server-tick frame window. To prevent the user interface from locking up or freezing animation loops, the client switches into an Extrapolation State Engine (Dead Reckoning).
2.1 Linear Extrapolation Constraints
The client continues to project the simulation state forward using the last known velocity vector. However, to prevent wild visual desynchronization during an unmitigated network drop, the extrapolation system is governed by a strict maximum time threshold constraint:
T_{\text{extrap\_max}} = 3.0 \text{ seconds}
If the network connection fails to recover and verify states before t - t_0 > T_{\text{extrap\_max}}, the extrapolation engine halts immediately. The UI pauses progress indicators and renders the connection-blocking modal container to shield the local state from diverging completely from database realities.
3. The Visual Snap-Correction Sieve
When a delayed authoritative server packet finally reaches the client device, the local predictive state vector S_{\text{client}}(t) must be reconciled with the true server state vector S_{\text{server}}(t). Directly snapping the visual metrics to match the server values introduces highly jarring visual artifacts (such as health bars teleporting backward or item counters flickering). The system filters adjustments through a dual-tier reconciliation sieve.
3.1 Reconciliation Divergence Threshold Categories
Soft Error Margin (|S_{\text{client}} - S_{\text{server}}| \le \text{Threshold}_{\text{soft}}): Divergence is negligible, caused by minor local frame-rate time-delta drift. The client hides the delta entirely by smoothly interpolating (LERPing) visual values over a short smoothing window (200\text{ ms}).
Hard Error Margin (|S_{\text{client}} - S_{\text{server}}| > \text{Threshold}_{\text{hard}}): Signal desynchronization is severe, indicating an illegal input rejection or an unexpected server state rollback. The system bypasses interpolation, forcing an immediate layout snap-redraw to restore mathematical truth instantly.
3.2 Non-Allocating Visual Interpolation Sieve Script
using UnityEngine;using System;public class VisualReconciliationSieve : MonoBehaviour{    private const float SoftThresholdBounds = 0.05f; // 5% maximum variance allocation    private const float HardThresholdBounds = 0.25f; // 25% structural divergence limit    private const float InterpolationSpeedCoefficient = 5.0f;    private float targetedAuthoritativeValue;    private float currentVisualRenderedValue;    private bool isInterpolatingActive;    public void IngestAuthoritativeServerState(float serverValidatedValue, float activeClientPredictedValue)    {        float absoluteDivergenceDelta = Mathf.Abs(activeClientPredictedValue - serverValidatedValue);        if (absoluteDivergenceDelta > HardThresholdBounds)        {            // Hard Error Margin: Force immediate structural snap to protect data truth            currentVisualRenderedValue = serverValidatedValue;            targetedAuthoritativeValue = serverValidatedValue;            isInterpolatingActive = false;            ExecuteViewportHardRedraw(serverValidatedValue);        }        else if (absoluteDivergenceDelta > SoftThresholdBounds)        {            // Soft Error Margin: Initialize smooth historical interpolation loop            targetedAuthoritativeValue = serverValidatedValue;            isInterpolatingActive = true;        }        else        {            // Variation falls below processing corridor limits; ignore divergence entirely            targetedAuthoritativeValue = serverValidatedValue;        }    }    void Update()    {        if (!isInterpolatingActive) return;        // Non-allocating frame-rate independent linear interpolation equation        currentVisualRenderedValue = Mathf.Lerp(            currentVisualRenderedValue,             targetedAuthoritativeValue,             Time.deltaTime * InterpolationSpeedCoefficient        );        ExecuteViewportSmoothUpdate(currentVisualRenderedValue);        // Check completion boundaries to close active processing loop        if (Mathf.Abs(currentVisualRenderedValue - targetedAuthoritativeValue) < 0.001f)        {            currentVisualRenderedValue = targetedAuthoritativeValue;            isInterpolatingActive = false;        }    }    private void ExecuteViewportHardRedraw(float absoluteValue)    {        // Directly overwrites vertex configurations inside TMPro components or image buffers    }    private void ExecuteViewportSmoothUpdate(float intermediateValue)    {        // Mutates slider filling ratios or local element anchor offsets smoothly    }}
4. Extrapolation Verification Assertion Sheet
To validate compliance with data-truth boundaries during continuous automation phases under simulated high-latency network drops, the verification pipeline executes runtime unit checks.
{  "assertionSuiteID": "EXTRAP_VISUAL_RECON_V1",  "simulationProfile": {    "networkProfileTier": "Tier_Gamma_Unstable",    "injectedPacketLossRate": 0.15,    "targetLoopCycleSeconds": 10.0  },  "validationConstraints": {    "maxAllowedVisualSnapEventsPerMinute": 1,    "interpolationMaxDurationSeconds": 0.25  },  "automatedAssertions": [    "Assert.IsFalse(VisualEngine.IsExtrapolatingPastLimit(3.0s), 'Extrapolation loop failed to halt when exceeding the maximum 3-second boundary lock.')",    "Assert.LessOrEqual(VisualEngine.GetLastReconciliationDelta(), 0.25f, 'Visual snap correction exceeded the hard threshold limits without triggering an immediate redraw sequence.')"  ]}

MODULE 48: CLOUD INFRASTRUCTURE SHARDING, GLOBAL MULTI-REGION DATABASE REPLICATION & LOAD BALANCING TOPOLOGIES
1. Cross-Region Anycast DNS & Layer 7 Proxy Topologies
To deliver sub-50ms connection latency across primary deployment territories (Europe, North America, East Asia), Folk-Idle utilizes an Anycast-routed border network network topology. Incoming TCP connection streams hit regional edge locations before forwarding traffic down private cloud fiber paths to the primary state compute clusters.
                  +-----------------------------------------+                  |       Global Anycast Edge Gateway       |                  +-----------------------------------------+                                       |             +-------------------------+-------------------------+             | Geo-IP Routing Loop                               |             v                                                   v+---------------------------------------+   +---------------------------------------+|  EU Central Region (Frankfurt Shard)  |   |   US East Region (N. Virginia Shard)  ||  - Layer 7 Envoy Proxy Router         |   |  - Layer 7 Envoy Proxy Router         ||  - Stateless API Node Pod Cluster     |   |  - Stateless API Node Pod Cluster     |+---------------------------------------+   +---------------------------------------+
Edge Ingestion: Traffic hits localized routing points running Anycast IP configurations. Network layers handle TLS termination at the edge, protecting the main compute layers from direct exposure.
Layer 7 Request Distribution: Envoy Proxy configurations inspect authorization headers (Bearer JWT) to identify the incoming packet's explicit regional destination shard, passing the network connection payload straight to matching node pools via persistent HTTP/2 keep-alive pathways.
2. Horizontal Database Sharding & Account Mapping Registry
While stateless compute instances run concurrently in every geographical zone, write-heavy persistent player data states are isolated into decoupled regional database shards to bypass global deadlock traps. Shard assignments are tracked inside a central lookup directory.
2.1 Global Account Location Registry Schema
This central routing table is globally replicated across all active relational databases using high-speed multi-master replication rings.
CREATE TABLE global_account_shard_registry (    account_id UUID PRIMARY KEY,    assigned_region_shard VARCHAR(32) NOT NULL, -- e.g., 'eu-central-1', 'us-east-1', 'ap-northeast-1'    routing_gateway_url VARCHAR(256) NOT NULL,    registered_at TIMESTAMP WITH TIME ZONE DEFAULT NOW() NOT NULL);CREATE INDEX idx_global_shard_routing ON global_account_shard_registry (account_id);
2.2 Sharded Execution Boundary Safeguards
When a player initiates a connection from an alternate geographical destination (e.g., during intercontinental vacation travel), the regional Layer 7 proxy catches the region mismatch by querying the localized multi-master registry. Instead of processing actions locally, the proxy passes a temporary HTTP 307 redirect token or forwards the internal socket frame down the private network backbone to the proper home database cluster.
3. Read-Replica Synchronization Lag Mitigation & Write-Forwarding
To handle massive reporting read requests (such as processing historical analytics, loading global leaderboard brackets, or generating guild catalog configurations), regional shard setups utilize a decoupled architecture featuring one primary write master database and multiple read replicas.
3.1 Replication Lag Consistency Model
Data modifications commit directly to the primary master shard before streaming asynchronously to the secondary read nodes. This introduces a measurable replication lag window (\tau_{\text{lag}}):
\tau_{\text{lag}} = t_{\text{replica\_visible}} - t_{\text{master\_commit}}
To protect the client interface from visual regressions caused by reading stale data right after a modification (such as an item disappearing from an inventory bag because a subsequent read request hit a replica before the update synced), the API layer enforces a localized Session-Pinning Lockout.
3.2 Dynamic Master Read-Pinning Formula
Following any mutating HTTP POST/PUT write transaction, the player's active session state forces all subsequent data reads to query the primary master database node directly for an explicit time-window ceiling (t_{\text{pin}}):
t_{\text{pin}} = \max \left( 1.5\text{ seconds}, \; \overline{\tau}_{\text{lag}} \times \sigma^2 \right)
Where \overline{\tau}_{\text{lag}} represents the moving average replication lag duration tracked by internal telemetry metrics, and \sigma^2 tracks the variance multiplier.
3.3 Programmatic Write-Forwarding Filter Blueprint
using System;using System.Threading.Tasks;using Microsoft.AspNetCore.Http;public class DatabaseSessionRoutingMiddleware{    private readonly RequestDelegate nextPipelineStep;    private readonly IDistributedSessionCache replicationSessionStore;    public DatabaseSessionRoutingMiddleware(RequestDelegate next, IDistributedSessionCache cache)    {        nextPipelineStep = next;        replicationSessionStore = cache;    }    public async Task InvokeAsync(HttpContext httpContext)    {        string requestMethod = httpContext.Request.Method;        string userAccountId = httpContext.User.FindFirst("sub")?.Value;        if (!string.IsNullOrEmpty(userAccountId))        {            string sessionLockCacheKey = $"db_route:master_pin:{userAccountId}";            if (requestMethod == "POST" || requestMethod == "PUT" || requestMethod == "DELETE")            {                // Write Event: Force session to pin to primary master database for 2.0 seconds                await replicationSessionStore.SetStringAsync(sessionLockCacheKey, "TRUE", TimeSpan.FromSeconds(2.0));                httpContext.Items["TargetDatabaseNodeScope"] = "PRIMARY_WRITE_MASTER";            }            else            {                // Read Event: Check if the specific user profile has an active master pinning lock                string isPinnedToMaster = await replicationSessionStore.GetStringAsync(sessionLockCacheKey);                                if (!string.IsNullOrEmpty(isPinnedToMaster))                {                    httpContext.Items["TargetDatabaseNodeScope"] = "PRIMARY_WRITE_MASTER";                }                else                {                    httpContext.Items["TargetDatabaseNodeScope"] = "ASYNC_READ_REPLICA";                }            }        }        await nextPipelineStep(httpContext);    }}
By separating reads and writes while managing consistency delays programmatically, Folk-Idle handles sudden traffic spikes transparently. It scales data handling cleanly across regional shards without introducing race conditions or database deadlocks during multi-character automated farming intervals.

--- Proceed with Module 49_ Security Hardening, Binary.._.docx ---
MODULE 49: SECURITY HARDENING, BINARY OBFUSCATION, RUNTIME MEMORY SCRAPING PROTECTIONS & ANTI-TAMPER ASSEMBLIES
1. Runtime Memory Value Projection & Bitwise XOR Obfuscation
To block automated memory scanners (such as Cheat Engine, GameGuardian, or customized memory dumpers) that scan RAM addresses for raw data patterns (e.g., looking for sequential changes in a 4-byte signed integer to locate gold or premium currency balances), the runtime engine never holds raw parameters in open memory spaces. All volatile numeric allocations are encapsulated within memory projection structures backed by randomized bitwise XOR masks.
Let V_{\text{actual}} be the true functional balance value, and M_{\text{mask}} be a cryptographically generated runtime unsigned integer mask initialized at the boot frame. The stored projected value V_{\text{projected}} occupies memory as:
V_{\text{projected}} = V_{\text{actual}} \oplus M_{\text{mask}}
When a value is read or updated, the system decodes the true value momentarily on the processor register before calculating a new random mask string. This continuously shifts the memory signature of the data variable across different heap addresses during runtime operations.
2. Native IL2CPP Metadata Shielding & Dumper Defenses
While the Unity IL2CPP backend transforms intermediate C# bytecode into compiled native C++ machine code, it generates an unencrypted layout file named global-metadata.dat. This binary blob explicitly maps out string literals, class definitions, and function pointers. Attackers exploit this by using utilities like Il2CppDumper to completely reconstruct the game's structural symbol tables and locate critical code targets.
To prevent structural reverse engineering, Folk-Idle integrates automated build-pipeline tooling to strip and corrupt the signature profiles of the metadata layer.
String Encryption Sieve: All string literals (API paths, secret keys, local server configurations) undergo compile-time transformation into encrypted character byte arrays inside the native binary (libil2cpp.so), removing them from the open metadata indexing table.
Metadata Header Corruption: The post-compilation processing layer applies an offset transformation to the headers of global-metadata.dat, altering the magic signature key (0xAFB01BBF) and scrambling internal table pointers. The custom native loader restores these parameters directly inside unmanaged memory at the initial boot loop execution step.
3. Native Guard Watchdog & Anti-Debugging / Root Gateways
The client security layer deploys a persistent native C++ daemon thread running outside the primary Unity main execution loop. This watchdog hooks into underlying operating system kernel properties to intercept active debugger attachments and unauthorized kernel modifications (Root/Jailbreak configurations).
Anti-Debugging via ptrace Enforcement: On Android deployment environments, the watchdog blocks attachment attempts by executing a self-trace loop: ptrace(PTRACE_TRACEME, 0, 0, 0). Because an active process can only accept a single ptrace controller at any given moment, subsequent debugger hook attempts from GDB or LLDB fail instantly.
Integrity Validation via /proc/self/maps: The watchdog monitors memory map allocation profiles (/proc/self/maps) to catch external library injections (such as Frida.so injection scripts or customized runtime cheat libraries). If string matches verify illegal hooks, an immediate exit execution fires.
4. Non-Allocating Memory Protected Variable Wrapper
using System;using System.Runtime.InteropServices;[StructLayout(LayoutKind.Sequential)]public struct ObfuscatedInt32{    private int projectedValue;    private int currentMask;    public ObfuscatedInt32(int baseValue)    {        currentMask = GenerateRuntimeCryptographicSeed();        projectedValue = baseValue ^ currentMask;    }    public int GetDecryptedValue()    {        return projectedValue ^ currentMask;    }    public void UpdateValue(int newValue)    {        int newMask = GenerateRuntimeCryptographicSeed();        projectedValue = newValue ^ newMask;        currentMask = newMask;    }    private static int GenerateRuntimeCryptographicSeed()    {        byte[] buffer = new byte[4];        using (var rng = System.Security.Cryptography.RandomNumberGenerator.Create())        {            rng.GetBytes(buffer);        }        int seed = BitConverter.ToInt32(buffer, 0);        return seed == 0 ? 0x5F3759DF : seed;    }}

Criticky vzato: Ano. Přechod na uzavřenou ekonomiku typu Albion Online (Modul 51) odhalil kritickou strukturální chybu, kterou předchozí moduly nepokrývají.
V idle hře, kde postavy těží a vyrábějí předměty 24/7, samotná dobrovolná tavící smyčka (Salvage Loop) k udržení zdravé ekonomiky nestačí. Pokud si hráč jednou koupí „Masterpiece“ meč, nemá důvod kupovat další. Poptávka se zastaví, ale nabídka od tisíců automatizovaných craftovacích účtů poroste dál. Trh během několika týdnů zkolabuje kvůli absolutnímu přetlaku nabídky.
Ekonomika tohoto typu nutně vyžaduje mechanismus opotřebení, oprav jako odtoku zlata (Gold Sink) a permanentní destrukce předmětů. Bez Modulu 52 je hra dlouhodobě nefunkční.
MODULE 52: ITEM DURABILITY DEGRADATION, REPAIR SINKS & PERMANENT EQUIPMENT LOSS MATRIX
1. Algoritmická degradace odolnosti (Durability Decay)
Aby se zajistil neustálý oběh zboží, každá akce v bojovém nebo těžebním uzlu má šanci na snížení aktuální odolnosti (current_durability) předmětu. Výpočet probíhá v rámci simulačního ticku (Modul 44).
Pravděpodobnost degradace odolnosti \mathbb{P}(D_{\text{loss}}) při úspěšné simulaci akce je definována jako:
\mathbb{P}(D_{\text{loss}}) = \max \left( 0.01, \; \rho_{\text{base}} \times (1 - \text{Skill}_{\text{maintenance}} \times 0.005) \right)
Kde:
\rho_{\text{base}} je základní koeficient opotřebení daného typu předmětu (např. těžké brnění = 0.08, krumpáč = 0.12).
\text{Skill}_{\text{maintenance}} je úroveň pasivní dovednosti postavy v údržbě výstroje.
Při úspěšném zásahu filtru se current_durability sníží o hodnotu vygenerovanou uniformním rozdělením \mathcal{U}(1, 3).
2. Finanční odtok zlata skrze opravy (Gold-Sink Repair)
Pokud odolnost klesne pod 100\%, předmět začne ztrácet efektivitu svých statistik (lineární škálování až na 50\% základní hodnoty při 1\% odolnosti). Při dosažení 0\% se předmět stává nefunkčním. Hráč ho musí opravit v cechovním depotu zaplacením poplatku v Goldech.
Cena opravy (C_{\text{repair}}) reflektuje kvalitu předmětu a cenu surovin na trhu:
C_{\text{repair}} = \lfloor (D_{\text{max}} - D_{\text{current}}) \times T_{\text{quality}} \times \kappa \rfloor
Kde:
T_{\text{quality}} je multiplikátor tieru kvality předmětu (Normal = 1.0, Masterpiece = 4.5).
\kappa je globální ekonomická konstanta spravovaná přes Remote Config pro kalibraci odtoku měny z oběhu (\kappa = 1.25).
3. Permanentní destrukce předmětů (The Trash Sieve)
Klíčový prvek uzavřené ekonomiky: předměty musí z herního světa trvale mizet. Každý proces opravy opotřebovaného předmětu nese inherentní riziko permanentního poškození struktury nebo úplného zničení předmětu.
Při spuštění opravy generuje server kontrolní parametr R \in \langle0.0, 1.0\rangle.
\text{RepairResult} = \begin{cases} \text{Destruction (Trash)} & \text{if } R < 0.015 \\ \text{MaxDurabilityReduction } (-5\%) & \text{if } 0.015 \le R < 0.10 \\ \text{PerfectRepair} & \text{if } R \ge 0.10 \end{cases}
Destruction (1.5\% šance): Předmět je nenávratně smazán z databáze. Hráč obdrží pouze 10\% základních surovin jako „odpad“ (Trash Sieve). To generuje permanentní poptávku po nových zbraních na trhu.
MaxDurabilityReduction (8.5\% šance): Maximální možná odolnost předmětu (maximum_durability) klesne o 5\%. Tím se zkracuje životní cyklus předmětu, dokud jeho maximální odolnost neklesne na kritické minimum, což donutí hráče koupit nový kus.
4. Serverový transakční skript pro exekuci oprav a destrukce
public class EquipmentMaintenanceEngine{    private readonly IDatabaseContext dbContext;    public async Task<RepairResultPayload> ExecuteEquipmentRepairAsync(Guid accountId, long instanceId, Guid guildId)    {        using (var transaction = await dbContext.Database.BeginTransactionAsync(System.Data.IsolationLevel.Serializable))        {            try            {                // 1. Uzamčení řádku předmětu a kontrola vlastnictví                var item = await dbContext.EquipmentInstances.LockRowForUpdate()                    .FirstOrDefaultAsync(e => e.InstanceId == instanceId && e.OwnerAccountId == accountId);                if (item == null || item.CurrentDurability == item.MaximumDurability || item.IsLockedInEscrow)                {                    await transaction.RollbackAsync();                    return new RepairResultPayload { Success = false, StatusMessage = "INVALID_TARGET_STATE" };                }                // 2. Výpočet ceny opravy                int missingDurability = item.MaximumDurability - item.CurrentDurability;                double qualityMultiplier = item.ItemQualityTier == 4 ? 4.5 : 1.0;                int repairCost = (int)Math.Floor(missingDurability * qualityMultiplier * 1.25);                // 3. Kontrola a uzamčení financí hráče a cechu                var player = await dbContext.AccountBalances.LockRowForUpdate().FirstOrDefaultAsync(b => b.AccountId == accountId);                var guild = await dbContext.GuildVaults.LockRowForUpdate().FirstOrDefaultAsync(g => g.GuildId == guildId);                if (player == null || player.CurrentGold < repairCost)                {                    await transaction.RollbackAsync();                    return new RepairResultPayload { Success = false, StatusMessage = "INSUFFICIENT_FUNDS" };                }                // 4. Stržení zlata (Cech si bere 10 % z ceny opravy realizované na jeho území)                int guildCut = (int)(repairCost * 0.10);                player.CurrentGold -= repairCost;                if (guild != null) guild.VaultGoldBalance += guildCut;                // 5. Výpočet Trash Sieve (Destrukční matice)                double roll = System.Security.Cryptography.RandomNumberGenerator.GetDouble();                string outcomeStatus;                if (roll < 0.015)                {                    // Totální destrukce předmětu                    dbContext.EquipmentInstances.Remove(item);                    outcomeStatus = "ITEM_DESTROYED_ON_ANVIL";                }                else if (roll < 0.10)                {                    // Snížení maximální trvanlivosti o 5 %                    item.MaximumDurability = (int)Math.Floor(item.MaximumDurability * 0.95);                    item.CurrentDurability = item.MaximumDurability;                    outcomeStatus = "REPAIRED_WITH_STRUCTURAL_DECAY";                }                else                {                    // Perfektní oprava                    item.CurrentDurability = item.MaximumDurability;                    outcomeStatus = "PERFECT_REPAIR_SUCCESS";                }                await dbContext.SaveChangesAsync();                await transaction.CommitAsync();                return new RepairResultPayload { Success = true, StatusMessage = outcomeStatus, GoldExpended = repairCost };            }            catch (Exception)            {                await transaction.RollbackAsync();                throw;            }        }    }}
Tímto modulem je Albion model definitivně uzavřen a zabezpečen. Zlato permanentně odtéká ze systému skrze opravy, cechy získávají pasivní příjem z údržby vybavení na svém území a trvalá destrukce předmětů garantuje, že craftovací profese budou mít odbyt po celých 90 dní sezóny.
Nyní jsou všechny logické, ekonomické a infrastrukturní vazby kompletní. Můžeme přejít k implementaci?

MODULE 51: CLOSED-LOOP PLAYER ECONOMY, CRAFTER METADATA SIGNATURES & ATOMIC MATCHING ENGINE
1. Item Instance Metadata & Deflationary Salvage Math
To build an Albion-style closed-loop economy within Folk-Idle, every item must carry an individual identity trace containing its structural origin data, crafter attribution signatures, and dynamic durability states. To prevent the inevitable market saturation caused by continuous 24/7 background automation, the economy enforces a strict deflationary barrier through resource destruction mechanics (Salvaging).
1.1 The Structural Salvage Recovery Function
When a player dismantles a piece of equipment to inject raw materials back into the market or free up stash space, the system runs an authoritative destruction formula to determine resource recovery rates:
M_{\text{recovered}} = \min \left( \lfloor M_{\text{required}} \times \mu_{\text{base}} \times (1 + \gamma \cdot \text{Skill}_{\text{salvage}}) \rfloor, \; \lfloor M_{\text{required}} \times \mu_{\text{max}} \rfloor \right)
Where:
M_{\text{required}} represents the exact volume of raw components originally required to craft the item.
\mu_{\text{base}} represents the baseline recovery efficiency variable, hard-locked at exactly 0.50 (50\% permanent item destruction).
\gamma represents the structural mastery progression coefficient, set to 0.002.
\text{Skill}_{\text{salvage}} tracks the character’s current unmanaged processing skill level.
\mu_{\text{max}} establishes an absolute recovery ceiling, capped at 0.75 (75\%).
2. Distributed Database Schema for Open Ledger Audits
The database schema splits inventory management into a highly optimized, stohable resource framework for base materials and a robust metadata JSONB architecture for individual gear tracking. This configuration allows player-to-player trade matching engines to run query checks without triggering table locks.
-- Tracks raw, stackable commodities with high concurrency stabilityCREATE TABLE market_commodity_registry (    commodity_id BIGSERIAL PRIMARY KEY,    account_id UUID NOT NULL,    material_sku VARCHAR(64) NOT NULL,    current_quantity INT NOT NULL CHECK (current_quantity >= 0),    updated_at TIMESTAMP WITH TIME ZONE DEFAULT NOW() NOT NULL);-- Tracks unique item assets, preserving history and item signaturesCREATE TABLE market_equipment_instances (    instance_id BIGSERIAL PRIMARY KEY,    owner_account_id UUID NOT NULL,    item_base_id VARCHAR(64) NOT NULL,    crafter_account_id UUID NOT NULL,    crafter_character_name VARCHAR(64) NOT NULL,    item_quality_tier INT NOT NULL CHECK (item_quality_tier BETWEEN 1 AND 4),    current_durability INT NOT NULL,    maximum_durability INT NOT NULL,    affix_data_payload JSONB,    is_locked_in_escrow BOOLEAN DEFAULT FALSE NOT NULL);-- Houses active order book matrices for both Buy and Sell actionsCREATE TABLE market_order_ledger (    order_id BIGSERIAL PRIMARY KEY,    issuer_account_id UUID NOT NULL,    guild_id UUID NOT NULL,    order_direction VARCHAR(4) NOT NULL CHECK (order_direction IN ('BUY', 'SELL')),    target_asset_sku VARCHAR(64) NOT NULL,    equipment_instance_id BIGINT REFERENCES market_equipment_instances(instance_id),    total_volume INT NOT NULL CHECK (total_volume > 0),    remaining_volume INT NOT NULL CHECK (remaining_volume >= 0),    unit_price_gold INT NOT NULL CHECK (unit_price_gold > 0),    guild_tax_rate_applied NUMERIC(4,2) NOT NULL,    is_order_active BOOLEAN DEFAULT TRUE NOT NULL,    created_at TIMESTAMP WITH TIME ZONE DEFAULT NOW() NOT NULL);CREATE INDEX idx_market_order_matching_speed ON market_order_ledger (target_asset_sku, order_direction, unit_price_gold) WHERE is_order_active = TRUE;
3. High-Performance Non-Duplicating Market Matching Engine
To prevent item duplication exploits caused by concurrent transaction spikes (e.g., two buyers attempting to claim the same unique weapon simultaneously via separate network threads), order matching executes within a strict pessimistic transaction boundary. The engine verifies account balances, processes dynamic fee deductions, distributes guild cuts, and updates inventory records inside a single serializable operation block.
using System;using System.Threading.Tasks;using Microsoft.EntityFrameworkCore;public class AtomicMarketMatchingEngine{    private readonly IDatabaseContext dbContext;    public async Task<MarketTransactionResult> ProcessSellOrderFulfillmentAsync(long activeOrderId, Guid buyerAccountId)    {        // Enforce strict serialized isolation to eliminate multi-instance race conditions        using (var dbTransaction = await dbContext.Database.BeginTransactionAsync(System.Data.IsolationLevel.Serializable))        {            try            {                // 1. Lock the order row for update processing                var order = await dbContext.MarketOrders.LockRowForUpdate()                    .FirstOrDefaultAsync(o => o.OrderId == activeOrderId && o.IsOrderActive);                if (order == null || order.RemainingVolume <= 0)                {                    await dbTransaction.RollbackAsync();                    return MarketTransactionResult.FailedOrderUnavailable;                }                // 2. Lock and verify the buyer profile balances                var buyerBalance = await dbContext.AccountBalances.LockRowForUpdate()                    .FirstOrDefaultAsync(b => b.AccountId == buyerAccountId);                int grossTransactionCost = order.UnitPriceGold * 1; // Processing order fulfillment unit step                if (buyerBalance == null || buyerBalance.CurrentGold < grossTransactionCost)                {                    await dbTransaction.RollbackAsync();                    return MarketTransactionResult.FailedInsufficientFunds;                }                // 3. Lock the seller profile and guild vault parameters                var sellerBalance = await dbContext.AccountBalances.LockRowForUpdate()                    .FirstOrDefaultAsync(b => b.AccountId == order.IssuerAccountId);                var guildVault = await dbContext.GuildVaults.LockRowForUpdate()                    .FirstOrDefaultAsync(g => g.GuildId == order.GuildId);                // 4. Calculate financial distribution brackets                int guildCut = (int)(grossTransactionCost * (order.GuildTaxRateApplied / 100.0));                int marketSinkBurn = (int)(grossTransactionCost * 0.03); // Fixed 3% inflation protection drop                int netSellerPayout = grossTransactionCost - (guildCut + marketSinkBurn);                // 5. Execute monetary transformations                buyerBalance.CurrentGold -= grossTransactionCost;                if (sellerBalance != null) sellerBalance.CurrentGold += netSellerPayout;                if (guildVault != null) guildVault.VaultGoldBalance += guildCut;                // 6. Transfer asset custody                if (order.EquipmentInstanceId.HasValue)                {                    // Unique item route                    var itemInstance = await dbContext.EquipmentInstances                        .FirstOrDefaultAsync(e => e.InstanceId == order.EquipmentInstanceId.Value);                    if (itemInstance != null)                    {                        itemInstance.OwnerAccountId = buyerAccountId;                        itemInstance.IsLockedInEscrow = false;                    }                }                else                {                    // Stackable resource route                    await AddCommodityToInventoryAsync(buyerAccountId, order.TargetAssetSku, 1);                }                // 7. Mutate order book configuration metrics                order.RemainingVolume -= 1;                if (order.RemainingVolume == 0)                {                    order.IsOrderActive = false;                }                await dbContext.SaveChangesAsync();                await dbTransaction.CommitAsync();                return MarketTransactionResult.Success;            }            catch (Exception)            {                await dbTransaction.RollbackAsync();                throw;            }        }    }    private async Task AddCommodityToInventoryAsync(Guid accountId, string sku, int quantity)    {        var commodity = await dbContext.Commodities            .FirstOrDefaultAsync(c => c.AccountId == accountId && c.MaterialSku == sku);        if (commodity != null)        {            commodity.CurrentQuantity += quantity;        }        else        {            dbContext.Commodities.Add(new CommodityRecord            {                AccountId = accountId,                MaterialSku = sku,                CurrentQuantity = quantity            });        }    }}public enum MarketTransactionResult{    Success,    FailedOrderUnavailable,    FailedInsufficientFunds}
4. The Deflationary Salvage Execution Pipeline
To maintain equilibrium within the resource loop, players dismantle unwanted craft or drop inventory directly within the unmanaged simulation thread. The transaction strips attribute arrays, calculates efficiency via the character skill matrix, breaks the unique item asset row, and drops commodity tokens back into the player's material inventory bags.
public class ItemSalvageController{    private readonly IDatabaseContext dbContext;    public async Task<bool> ExecuteItemSalvageAsync(Guid playerAccountId, long targetInstanceId, int characterSalvageSkill)    {        using (var dbTransaction = await dbContext.Database.BeginTransactionAsync(System.Data.IsolationLevel.Serializable))        {            try            {                // Secure unique asset data rows and check owner authenticity constraints                var item = await dbContext.EquipmentInstances.LockRowForUpdate()                    .FirstOrDefaultAsync(e => e.InstanceId == targetInstanceId && e.OwnerAccountId == playerAccountId);                if (item == null || item.IsLockedInEscrow)                {                    await dbTransaction.RollbackAsync();                    return false;                }                // Look up original building block requirements from static system configuration tables                var recipe = GameRecipeRegistry.GetRecipeBySku(item.ItemBaseId);                if (recipe == null)                {                    await dbTransaction.RollbackAsync();                    return false;                }                // Execute the structural salvage efficiency calculation                double baseEfficiency = 0.50;                double skillBonus = 0.002 * characterSalvageSkill;                double finalEfficiencyScalar = Math.Min(0.75, baseEfficiency * (1.0 + skillBonus));                // Process resource recovery arrays                foreach (var materialRequirement in recipe.RequiredMaterials)                {                    int recoveredVolume = (int)Math.Floor(materialRequirement.Quantity * finalEfficiencyScalar);                    if (recoveredVolume > 0)                    {                        await InjectResourceTokensAsync(playerAccountId, materialRequirement.MaterialSku, recoveredVolume);                    }                }                // Completely remove the unique item instance from the global database tables                dbContext.EquipmentInstances.Remove(item);                await dbContext.SaveChangesAsync();                await dbTransaction.CommitAsync();                return true;            }            catch (Exception)            {                await dbTransaction.RollbackAsync();                throw;            }        }    }    private async Task InjectResourceTokensAsync(Guid accountId, string sku, int amount)    {        var resource = await dbContext.Commodities            .FirstOrDefaultAsync(c => c.AccountId == accountId && c.MaterialSku == sku);        if (resource != null)        {            resource.CurrentQuantity += amount;            resource.UpdatedAt = DateTimeOffset.UtcNow;        }        else        {            dbContext.Commodities.Add(new CommodityRecord            {                AccountId = accountId,                MaterialSku = sku,                CurrentQuantity = amount,                UpdatedAt = DateTimeOffset.UtcNow;            });        }    }}
This structural architecture ensures that a complete, Albion-style closed economic model can operate safely on an idle backend framework. Volume and pricing remain entirely under player jurisdiction, while automated system burns and resource recycling filters neutralize long-term hyperinflationary traps at the database boundary.

MODULE 02: FOLKLORE RACES & GENETIC BREEDING ALGORITHMS
1. Base Race Attribute Profiles
Every character possesses 5 primary attributes: Strength (STR), Dexterity (DEX), Intelligence (INT), Constitution (CON), and Luck (LCK). When a character levels up, they receive flat baseline attribute points. These points are multiplied by the specific race growth coefficients.
1.1 Race Growth Coefficients Matrix
Human: STR 1.00 | DEX 1.00 | INT 1.00 | CON 1.00 | LCK 1.00
Vila: STR 0.60 | DEX 1.50 | INT 1.10 | CON 0.60 | LCK 1.20
Fomóiri: STR 1.60 | DEX 0.50 | INT 0.70 | CON 1.50 | LCK 0.70
Draugr: STR 1.30 | DEX 0.90 | INT 0.80 | CON 1.20 | LCK 0.80
Kobold: STR 0.90 | DEX 1.10 | INT 0.90 | CON 0.80 | LCK 1.30
Moosleute: STR 0.70 | DEX 1.20 | INT 1.30 | CON 0.70 | LCK 1.10
Vodník: STR 1.10 | DEX 0.80 | INT 1.20 | CON 1.00 | LCK 0.90
1.2 Unique Passive Traits & Penalties
Human
Passive: Adaptability. Increases all Experience Point (XP) gains across all Combat and Professional skills by 10%.
Penalty: None.
Vila
Passive: Sylvan Precision. Increases Ranged Damage by 20% and Critical Strike Chance by 5%.
Penalty: Fragile Frame. Total Physical Armor gained from equipped gear is reduced by 30%.
Fomóiri
Passive: Abyssal Density. Grants a flat Damage Reduction of 15 points against every incoming physical attack.
Penalty: Sluggish Momentum. Base Attack Speed is reduced by 25%, and the spawn delay between enemies in the active combat zone is increased by 1.5 seconds.
Draugr
Passive: Relentless Hunger. Converts 8% of all inflicted Melee Damage into immediate health recovery (Lifesteal).
Penalty: Calcified Flesh. Out-of-combat Health Regeneration and the healing efficacy of consumed food items are reduced by 50%.
Kobold
Passive: Subterranean Hoarder. Grants a 15% chance to duplicate any ore extracted via Mining, and a 10% chance to salvage raw metal ingots during Smithing operations.
Penalty: Restricted Pack. Inventory capacity for non-ore and non-bar items is reduced by 50% during AFK calculations, filling the inventory twice as fast.
Moosleute
Passive: Forest Synergy. Increases Woodcutting speed by 15%, grants a 12% chance for a double yield during Herbalism harvesting, and increases cooked Alchemy potion potency by 10%.
Penalty: Crude Handling. Tool Durability degradation is increased by 25% across all equipped axes and sickles.
Vodník
Passive: Aquatic Dominance. Reduces active Fishing wait times by 20%, increases Mythic/Rare fish catch rate by 10%, and adds a 15% chance to craft an Excellent tier item during Cooking.
Penalty: Bound to the Depths. The maximum allowed Offline AFK calculation time is strictly restricted from the global 12-hour maximum to an 8-hour maximum.
2. Genetic Breeding & Inheritance Mechanics
When two Adult characters of the exact same race reach Level 50, they can be placed into the Village Breeding Grounds to generate a Generation (G+1) offspring. Breeding does not consume the parents, but places them on a 48-hour cooldown timer.
2.1 Inheritance Formula
Each primary attribute modifier inherits its baseline values directly from the parents using an average calculation altered by a random variance factor.
Base\_Offspring\_Mod = \frac{Parent1\_Mod + Parent2\_Mod}{2} Final\_Offspring\_Mod = Base\_Offspring\_Mod + \text{Random}(-0.02, +0.02)
2.2 Mutation Matrix
During every breeding execution, there is a fixed 3% baseline probability for a genetic mutation. If a mutation triggers, one of the 5 attribute growth modifiers is selected at random and receives a permanent upgrade.
Common Mutation (75% chance within mutation event): +0.05 to the selected modifier.
Rare Mutation (20% chance within mutation event): +0.10 to the selected modifier.
Epic Mutation (4.9% chance within mutation event): +0.15 to the selected modifier.
Legendary Mutation (0.1% chance within mutation event): +0.25 to the selected modifier.
Maximum Cap: No individual genetic modifier can exceed a maximum inherited value of 2.00.
3. Aging & Lifespan Progression
Characters progress through 4 distinct life stages based on real-world elapsed time accumulated since their generation/birth timestamp.
3.1 Age Tiers and Attribute Penalties
Child (Age 0 to 2 game years / 14 real days)
Character cannot be assigned to active Combat slots.
Character cannot be assigned to active Gathering/Crafting slots.
Character cannot breed.
Adult (Age 2 to 12 game years / 84 real days)
Character operates at 100% of statistical efficiency.
Eligible for all tasks and breeding functions.
Senior (Age 12 to 16 game years / 28 real days)
All combat attributes (STR, DEX, INT) are degraded by a flat 10% penalty.
Gathering and Crafting speeds are reduced by 5%.
Character can still breed, but mutation chances are reduced to 0%.
Old (Age 16+ game years / 28 real days+)
All combat and professional attributes suffer a permanent 25% penalty.
Character is entirely locked out of the breeding system.
Passive Utility: Characters in the Old bracket provide a passive +5% XP training mentor buff to any Child or lower-level Adult character sharing the same race pool in the village.

MODULE 28: ECONOMY TELEMETRY, KPI INSTRUMENTATION & ANALYTICS PIPELINES
1. Sinks and Sources Parity Tracking Matrix
To maintain macroeconomic stability and prevent runaway inflation across the shared village economy, the server executes a continuous auditing loop tracking the Sink-to-Source ratio (R_{\text{eco}}). This monitor evaluates the relationship between minted resources (sources) and permanently destroyed resources (sinks).
The system targets an equilibrium corridor:
0.85 \le R_{\text{eco}} \le 1.15
Where R_{\text{eco}} is calculated dynamically over a rolling 7-day window:
R_{\text{eco}} = \frac{\sum \text{Gold}_{\text{Minted}} + \sum (\text{Diamonds}_{\text{Minted}} \times 500)}{\sum \text{Gold}_{\text{Consumed}} + \sum (\text{Diamonds}_{\text{Consumed}} \times 500)}
1.1 Realtime Economic Audit Table Schema
Every economic transaction processed by the server-authoritative API dumps a telemetry tracking vector into the non-volatile ledger store.
CREATE TABLE economy_telemetry_ledger (    ledger_id BIGSERIAL PRIMARY KEY,    account_id UUID NOT NULL,    transaction_type VARCHAR(32) NOT NULL,    currency_type VARCHAR(16) NOT NULL,    raw_amount INT NOT NULL,    system_context VARCHAR(64) NOT NULL,    recorded_at TIMESTAMP WITH TIME ZONE DEFAULT NOW() NOT NULL);CREATE INDEX idx_eco_telemetry_metrics ON economy_telemetry_ledger (recorded_at, transaction_type, currency_type);
2. KPI Telemetry Instrumentation Hooks
Player behavioral events are serialized into lightweight JSON packets and emitted asynchronously to eliminate runtime processing overhead on compute threads.
2.1 Event Schema: Character Task Allocation Mutation
Trigger Condition: Pushed instantly whenever a user alters a citizen's role state from the Bottom Navigation Dock.
{  "eventID": "c20a969e-128d-4e94-b778-9964177feefb",  "eventType": "KPI_CHARACTER_ALLOCATION_CHANGED",  "accountID": "9b1deb4d-3b7d-4bad-9bdd-2b0d7b3dcb6d",  "timestamp": "2026-07-01T22:30:15Z",  "payload": {    "characterID": "4f9d8a3e-7b2c-4e12-8f11-3c4a5b6c7d8e",    "characterLevel": 54,    "lineageRace": "Vila",    "previousState": "Gathering_Active",    "newState": "Combat_Active",    "targetNodeID": "region_06_node_03"  }}
2.2 Event Schema: Macro Churn Vector Indicator
Trigger Condition: Fired when an active combat slot character runs out of automated Auto-Eat food supplies, forcing an unmanaged termination of active grinding loops.
{  "eventID": "e843bb01-447a-4281-9b62-09255bbcd14f",  "eventType": "KPI_AUTO_EAT_DEPLETED_HALT",  "accountID": "9b1deb4d-3b7d-4bad-9bdd-2b0d7b3dcb6d",  "timestamp": "2026-07-01T22:31:02Z",  "payload": {    "slotIndex": 2,    "lastEncounteredEnemyID": "mob_r06_e04",    "discardedOfflineSeconds": 14200,    "accumulatedGoldBeforeHalt": 42050  }}
3. Distributed Data Streaming Architecture Topology
To route high-velocity event frameworks without locking relational datastores, processing uses an asynchronous messaging pipeline streaming directly into specialized analytical warehouses.
Ingestion Isolation: Stateless ASP.NET Core compute instances append events directly to a local, non-blocking Apache Kafka logging ring buffer.
Analytical Processing: Downstream vector consumers ingest data partitions continuously from Kafka, grouping raw logs into structured column arrays before executing bulk batch insertions into cold storage analytical layers (ClickHouse or Snowflake) for visual dashboard representation.
